{{long|date=October 2020}}

{{Use dmy dates|date=February 2019}}
{{Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen infobox}}
{{Campaignbox Yemeni Crisis}}
{{Yemeni Crisis (2011–present)}}
The '''Saudi-led intervention in Yemen''' is an intervention launched by [[Saudi Arabia]] on 26 March 2015, leading a coalition of nine countries from [[Western Asia|West Asia]] and [[North Africa]], in response to calls from the pro-Saudi<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.theamericanconservative.com/buchanan/with-friends-like-the-saudis/|title=With Friends Like the Saudis|first=Patrick J.|last=Buchanan|website=The American Conservative}}</ref> president of Yemen [[Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi]] for military support after [[Houthi takeover in Yemen|he was ousted]] by the [[Houthi movement]] due to economic and political grievances, and fled to Saudi Arabia.<ref name="https">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/03/26/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0ML0YC20150326|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Yemeni leader Hadi leaves country as Saudi Arabia keeps up air strikes|date=26 March 2015}}</ref>

Code-named '''Operation Decisive Storm''' ({{lang-ar|عملية عاصفة الحزم}} ''Amaliyyat 'Āṣifat al-Ḥazm''), the intervention initially consisted of a bombing campaign on Houthi rebels and later a naval [[blockade of Yemen|blockade]] and the deployment of ground forces into [[Yemen]].<ref>Gatten, Emma. [https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/saudi-blockade-starves-yemen-of-vital-supplies-as-bombing-raids-continue-10509460.html Saudi blockade starves Yemen of vital supplies, as bombing raids continue]. ''[[The Independent]]''. 19 September 2016. Retrieved 23 October 2016.</ref> The Saudi-led coalition has attacked the positions of the [[Houthi]] militia, and loyalists of the former [[President of Yemen]], [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]], allegedly supported by [[Iran]] (see [[Iran–Saudi Arabia proxy conflict]]).<ref name="CBC News">{{cite news|url= http://www.cbc.ca/news/world/yemeni-s-abed-rabbo-mansour-hadi-arrives-in-saudi-capital-1.3010698|title=Yemeni's Abed Rabbo Mansour Hadi arrives in Saudi capital|date=26 March 2015|access-date=26 March 2015|publisher=[[CBC News]]}}</ref><ref name="https"/>

[[Fighter jet]]s and ground forces from [[Egypt]], [[Morocco]], [[Jordan]], [[Sudan]], the [[United Arab Emirates]], [[Kuwait]], [[Qatar]], [[Bahrain]], and [[Academi]] (formerly called Blackwater) took part in the operation. [[Djibouti]], [[Eritrea]], and [[Somalia]] made their airspace, territorial waters, and military bases available to the coalition.<ref name="Ssfpstsciy">{{cite news |title=SOMALIA: Somalia finally pledges support to Saudi-led coalition in Yemen – Raxanreeb Online |url=http://www.wargeyska.so/somalia-somalia-finally-pledges-support-to-suadi-led-coalition-in-yemen-raxanreeb-online/ |archive-url=https://archive.today/20150407194428/http://www.wargeyska.so/somalia-somalia-finally-pledges-support-to-suadi-led-coalition-in-yemen-raxanreeb-online/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=7 April 2015 |agency=RBC Radio |date=7 April 2015 |access-date=7 April 2015 }}</ref> The [[United States]] provided intelligence and logistical support, including [[aerial refueling]] and search-and-rescue for downed coalition pilots.<ref name="rescue"/><ref name=hp-20160810>{{cite news |url=https://huffingtonpost.com/entry/barack-obama-could-end-the-killing-in-yemen-in-hours_us_57f7d5dee4b0b6a43031ba4e |title=Obama Could End The Slaughter in Yemen Within Hours |author=Akbar Shahid Ahmed |work=[[HuffPost]] |date=10 August 2016 |accessdate=8 October 2016}}</ref> It also accelerated the sale of weapons to coalition states<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.mcclatchydc.com/2015/04/07/262381/us-stepping-up-weapons-shipments.html|publisher=[[The McClatchy Company|McClatchy DC]] |first=James|last=Rosen |authorlink=James Rosen (journalist) |title=U.S. stepping up weapons shipments to aid Saudi air campaign over Yemen|date=7 April 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref> and continued [[List of drone strikes in Yemen|strikes against AQAP.]] The US and Britain have deployed their military personnel in the command and control centre responsible for Saudi-led air strikes on Yemen, having access to lists of targets.<ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-15_BZM">{{cite news |first=Emma |last=Graham-Harrison |title=British and US military 'in command room' for Saudi strikes on Yemen |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=15 January 2016 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/15/british-us-military-in-command-room-saudi-strikes-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eaDLp4Dq?url=http://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/15/british-us-military-in-command-room-saudi-strikes-yemen |archivedate=16 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-19_BHS">{{cite news |first=Vickie |last=Hawkins |title=Bombing hospitals and schools cannot become the new normal |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=19 January 2016 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2016/jan/19/yemen-msf-bombing-hospitals-schools-cannot-become-the-new-normal |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ehgjdWF7?url=http://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2016/jan/19/yemen-msf-bombing-hospitals-schools-cannot-become-the-new-normal |archivedate=21 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="publications-parliament-uk_2016-01-12_HoC">{{cite web |title=House of Commons debate, Tuesday 12 January 2016 | publisher=publications.parliament.uk (Daily Hansard – Debate, Column 681) |date=12 January 2016 |url=https://publications.parliament.uk/pa/cm201516/cmhansrd/cm160112/debtext/160112-0001.htm |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ehizuhFw?url=http://www.publications.parliament.uk/pa/cm201516/cmhansrd/cm160112/debtext/160112-0001.htm |archivedate=21 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

The war received [[International reactions to the Saudi-led intervention in Yemen (2015–present)|widespread criticism]] and had a dramatic worsening effect on Yemen's humanitarian situation, that reached the level of a "humanitarian disaster"<ref name="auto">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jun/05/saudi-led-naval-blockade-worsens-yemen-humanitarian-disaster |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |title=Saudi-led naval blockade leaves 20&nbsp;m Yemenis facing humanitarian disaster |date=5 June 2015|first=Julian |last=Borger |authorlink=Julian Borger |access-date=31 October 2015}}</ref> or "humanitarian catastrophe",<ref name="un-org_2015-07-28_DCN">{{cite news|url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51516|title=Durable ceasefire needed as 'humanitarian catastrophe' leaves millions suffering in Yemen – UN relief chief)|date=28 July 2015|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6aOLG7U6O?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51516|archivedate=29 July 2015|url-status=live|publisher=UN News Centre}}</ref><ref name="ECHAO_2015-12-14_ECS">{{cite web |title=European Commission steps up humanitarian aid for Yemen crisis |via=[[ReliefWeb]] |publisher=European Commission's Directorate-General for European Civil Protection and Humanitarian Aid Operations |date=14 December 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/european-commission-steps-humanitarian-aid-yemen-crisis |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dqN1KtTh?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/european-commission-steps-humanitarian-aid-yemen-crisis |archivedate=17 December 2015 |url-status=live }}; Original source: {{cite web |title=European Commission steps up humanitarian aid for Yemen crisis |url=http://ec.europa.eu/echo/news/european-commission-steps-humanitarian-aid-yemen-crisis_en |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dqNESGuF?url=http://ec.europa.eu/echo/news/european-commission-steps-humanitarian-aid-yemen-crisis_en |archivedate=17 December 2015 |url-status=live |date=14 December 2015 }}</ref><ref name="BBCNews_2015-08-19_YCH">{{cite news |title=Yemen crisis: How bad is the humanitarian situation? |work=BBC News |date=24 August 2015 |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34011187 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6bskayjqI?url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34011187 |archivedate=28 September 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> and many have labelled it as a [[genocide]].<ref name="independent.co.uk"/><ref>{{cite web |url=https://theconversation.com/us-complicity-in-the-saudi-led-genocide-in-yemen-spans-obama-trump-administrations-106896|title=US complicity in the Saudi-led genocide in Yemen spans Obama, Trump administrations|last=Bachman|first=Jeff |date=November 26, 2018 |website=[[The Conversation (website)|The Conversation]] |publisher= |access-date=January 13, 2020 |quote=As a scholar of genocide and human rights, I believe the destruction brought about by these attacks combined with the blockade amounts to genocide.}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|last=Taves|first=Harold|date=2019-02-23|title=Genocide in Yemen-Is the West Complicit?|url=https://www.researchgate.net/publication/331306103|quote=Is there a genocide in Yemen? Based on the definition of genocide: The deliberate killing of a large group of people, especially those of a particular ethnic group or nation. The answer is an unequivocal YES.}}</ref> The question of whether or not the intervention is in compliance with [[Use of force by states|Article 2(4)]] of the [[Charter of the United Nations|UN Charter]] has been the matter of academic dispute.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Nußberger |first1=Benjamin |title=Military strikes in Yemen in 2015: intervention by invitation and self-defence in the course of Yemen's 'model transitional process' |journal=Journal on the Use of Force and International Law |date=5 January 2017 |volume= 4, 2017 |pages=110–160 |doi=10.1080/20531702.2017.1256565 |s2cid=157698592 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.irinnews.org/analysis/2015/04/03/saudi-war-yemen-legal|title=Is the Saudi war on Yemen legal?|date=3 April 2015|website=IRIN}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|first1=Luca|title=Weathering the Storm: Legality and Legal Implications of the Saudi-Led Military Intervention in Yemen|last1=Ferro|first2=Tom|last2=Ruys|journal=International & Comparative Law Quarterly|volume=65|issue=1|pages=61–98|doi=10.1017/S0020589315000536|year=2016}}</ref> 

In 2019, the conflict's status was described a "military stalemate for years".<ref>{{cite news |title=Yemeni Separatists Relinquish Control of Buildings in Aden |url= https://www.nytimes.com/2019/08/17/world/middleeast/yemen-houthi-saudi-oilfield.html |accessdate=4 September 2019 |work=The New York Times |agency=Reuters |date=17 August 2019}}</ref> The global [[COVID-19 pandemic]] is said to have given Saudi Arabia an opportunity to review its interests in Yemen.<ref name="covid">{{cite news|url=https://www.theglobalist.com/yemen-war-saudi-arabia-iran-houthis-coronavirus-pandemic-covid19-war-crimes-islam/ |title=The Saudis' War in Yemen Is a Crime Against Humanity |author=Ben-Meir, Alon|date=18 April 2020|work=[[The Globalist]]|accessdate=25 April 2020}}</ref> It is said that Saudi Arabia is searching for an exit strategy, believing that the pandemic can make it look like a humanitarian gesture instead of a surrender.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Arabia and the War in Yemen - Riyadh's Retreat |url= https://magazine.zenith.me/en/politics/saudi-arabia-and-war-yemen |accessdate=22 April 2020 |work=Zenith Magazine |date=21 April 2020}}</ref>

{{toclimit|3}}

== Background ==
{{See also|Houthi insurgency in Yemen|Aftermath of the Houthi takeover in Yemen}}

Saudi-backed [[Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi]], running unopposed as the only candidate for president, won the [[2012 Yemeni presidential election|2012 Yemeni elections]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-22096125|title=Yemen President Hadi 'removes Republican Guard commander'|work=BBC News |date=10 April 2013|access-date=12 April 2015}}</ref> Since August 2014, the [[Houthis]] (or Ansar Allah), a [[Zaidiyyah|Zaidi]] [[Shia Islam|Shia]] movement and militant group thought to be backed by [[Iran]], dissatisfied with Hadi government's decisions and the new constitution, arranged mass protests which culminated into [[2014–15 Yemeni coup d'état|their takeover of the Yemeni government]] in 2015, declaring victory of the revolution and drafting a new constitution when Hadi's provisional government had already expired its term. Saudi Arabia and other countries denounced this as an unconstitutional coup d'état.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/01/21/uk-yemen-security-gcc-idUKKBN0KU1YX20150121|title=Gulf Arab ministers condemn Houthi 'coup' in Yemen|work=[[Reuters]]|date=21 January 2015|access-date=5 May 2015}}</ref>

In military operations on the ground, the Houthis were supported by sections of the Yemeni armed forces loyal to former president [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]], who was removed from power as part of the 2011 Arab Spring uprisings.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/rebels-push-offensive-in-aden-killing-dozens-with-artillery-fire/2015/03/31/79f53d9e-d729-11e4-bf0b-f648b95a6488_story.html|title=Yemen's Houthi Rebels get boost from country's ousted dictator|date=31 March 2015|work=[[The Washington Post]]|first=Ali|last=al-Mujahed}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/yemen-leak-collusion-between-houthis-and-ex-president-saleh-1125273454|title=Yemen leak: Collusion between Houthis and ex-president Saleh|publisher=[[Middle East Eye]]|date=22 January 2015}}</ref> Houthi leaders claimed<ref name="Al Monitor">{{cite news |url=http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2015/03/yemen-saudi-saleh-airstrikes.html#|title=Yemen's Saleh proves to be a survivor|publisher=[[Al-Monitor]] |date=29 March 2015}}</ref> that Saudi Arabia was trying to break the alliance between the Houthis and Saleh's supporters, reports<ref name="Al Monitor"/> claimed that Saleh's son Ahmed Ali Saleh had traveled to the Saudi capital to attempt to broker a deal to end the airstrikes. Saudi media claim that Saleh or his son had approached Riyadh seeking such a deal.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://english.alarabiya.net/en/News/middle-east/2015/03/28/Saleh-offered-Saudi-Arabia-anti-Houthi-coup-for-immunity.html|title=Saleh offered Saudi Arabia anti-Houthi coup for immunity |publisher=[[Al Arabiya English]]|date=28 March 2015}}</ref>

By September 2014, Houthi fighters captured [[Sana'a|Sanaʽa]], toppling Hadi's government. Soon after, a peace deal (known as the 'Peace and Partnership Agreement') was sealed between the Hadi government and the Houthis, but was not honored by either party. The deal was drafted with the intent of defining a power-sharing government. A conflict over a draft constitution resulted in the Houthis consolidating control over the Yemeni capital in January 2015. After resigning from his post alongside his prime minister and remaining under virtual house arrest for one month, Hadi fled to [[Aden]] in [[South Yemen|southern Yemen]] in February.<ref>{{cite web |url= http://www.crisisgroup.org/en/regions/middle-east-north-africa/iraq-iran-gulf/yemen/b045-yemen-at-war.aspx |title= Yemen at War | publisher=[[International Crisis Group]] |date= 27 March 2015| access-date= 6 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Heinze|first=Marie-Christine|url= http://en.qantara.de/content/the-crisis-in-yemen-the-primacy-of-stability-over-real-change |title= The crisis in Yemen – The primacy of stability over real change | publisher= [[Qantara.de]] |date=30 January 2015|access-date=12 April 2015}}</ref> Upon arriving in Aden, Hadi withdrew his resignation, saying that the actions of the Houthis from September 2014 had amounted to a "coup" against him.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/yemens-hadi-withdraws-resignation-un-pushes-dialogue-1907885482|title=Yemen's Hadi withdraws resignation, as UN pushes for dialogue|date=24 February 2015|publisher=[[Middle East Eye]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/02/yemen-abd-rabbu-masnour-hadi-150224001628332.html|title=Yemen's ousted president withdraws resignation|date=24 February 2015|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]] }}</ref> By 25 March, forces answering to Sanaʽa were [[Battle of Aden (2015)|rapidly closing in on Aden]], which Hadi had declared to be Yemen's temporary capital.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.yementimes.com/en/1871/news/4999/Al-Subaihi-captured-and-Lahj-falls-as-Houthis-move-on-Aden.htm|newspaper=[[Yemen Times]] |title=Al Subaihi captured and Lahj falls as Houthis move on Aden|date=25 March 2015|access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref>

During the [[Yemeni Civil War (2015–present)#Southern offensive|Houthis' southern offensive]], Saudi Arabia began a military buildup on its [[Saudi Arabia–Yemen border|border]] with Yemen.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/03/24/us-yemen-security-usa-saudi-idUSKBN0MK2S120150324|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Exclusive: Saudi Arabia building up military near Yemen border – U.S. officials|date=24 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref> In response, a Houthi commander boasted that his troops would counterattack against any Saudi aggression and would not stop until they had taken [[Riyadh]], the Saudi capital.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/yemen-protests-against-militants-leave-one-dead-17-injured-1427193838|work=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|title=Yemen's Houthi Militants Extend Push Southward|last=Almasmari|first=Hakim |authorlink=Hakim Almasmari |date=24 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref>

On 25 March, Hadi called on the UN Security Council to authorise "willing countries that wish to help Yemen to provide immediate support for the legitimate authority by all means and measures to protect Yemen and deter the Houthi aggression".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32045984 |title=Yemen's President Hadi asks UN to back intervention |date=25 March 2015 |work=BBC News }}</ref>

Yemen's foreign minister, [[Riad Yassin]], requested military assistance from the [[Arab League]] on 25 March, amid reports that Hadi had fled his provisional capital.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.vice.com/article/with-a-bounty-on-his-head-yemens-president-flees-as-rebels-advance|publisher=[[Vice News]] |title=Saudi Arabia Launches Airstrikes in Yemen as President Flees Amid Rebel Advance|date=25 March 2015|first=John|last=Beck|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref><ref>{{in lang|vi}} [http://www.nguoi-viet.com/absolutenm2/templates/viewarticlesNVO.aspx?articleid=204942&zoneid=5 "Phiến quân Shiite tấn công, tổng thống Yemen bỏ chạy"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150402123101/http://www.nguoi-viet.com/absolutenm2/templates/viewarticlesNVO.aspx?articleid=204942&zoneid=5 |date=2 April 2015 }}. 25 March 2015. Retrieved 26 March 2015</ref> On 26 March, Saudi state TV station [[Al-Ekhbariya TV]] reported that Hadi arrived at a Riyadh airbase and was met by [[Saudi Arabia|Saudi]] Defense Minister [[Mohammad bin Salman Al Saud]]. His route from Aden to Riyadh was not immediately known.<ref name="CBC News"/>

At a summit of the Arab League held in Sharm El-Sheikh, Egypt, on 28–29 March, President Hadi again repeated his calls for international intervention in the fighting. A number of League members pledged their support to Hadi's government during that meeting.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.dw.de/arab-league-summit-wraps-up-with-plan-for-pan-arab-force/a-18348096|date=29 March 2015|title=Arab League summit wraps up with plan for pan-Arab force|publisher=[[Deutsche Welle]] }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.dw.de/yemen-crisis-tops-agenda-as-arab-league-summit-opens/a-18346872|date=28 March 2015|title=Yemen crisis tops agenda as Arab League summit opens|publisher=[[Deutsche Welle]]}}</ref>

Many ancient [[cultural heritage]] sites in Yemen have been destroyed and damaged by Saudi-led coalition airstrikes including some as old as 3,000 years.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2015/06/05/the-world-may-be-ignoring-the-destruction-of-cultural-treasures-in-yemen/|title=The world may be ignoring the destruction of cultural treasures in Yemen|first=Adam|last=Taylor|date=5 June 2015 |newspaper=The Washington Post |accessdate=9 February 2018}}</ref>

== Operation Decisive Storm ==
According to the Saudi news outlet [[Al Arabiya]], Saudi Arabia contributed 100 warplanes and 150,000 soldiers to the military operation. Reuters indicated that planes from [[Egypt]], [[Morocco]], [[Jordan]], [[Sudan]], [[Kuwait]], the [[United Arab Emirates]], [[Qatar]] and [[Bahrain]] were taking part.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-coalition-factbox-idUSKBN0N11F220150410|title=Factbox: Saudi-led coalition against Yemen's Houthis|date=10 April 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/03/25/middleeast/yemen-unrest/ |title=Saudi Arabia launches airstrikes in Yemen|author=Steve Almasy |author2=Jason Hanna |publisher=CNN |date=25 March 2015}}</ref> Egypt had previously sent four warships supporting the Saudi naval blockade.<ref name="sites.tufts.edu">{{Cite web|url=https://sites.tufts.edu/reinventingpeace/2018/02/28/who-is-arming-the-yemen-war-and-is-anyone-planning-to-stop/|title=Who is arming the Yemen war? (And is anyone planning to stop?) {{!}} Reinventing Peace|date=28 February 2018|access-date=2019-02-16}}</ref>

The UAE contributed 30 fighter jets, Kuwait sent 15 (understood to be three squadrons of [[McDonnell Douglas F/A-18 Hornet|F/A-18 Hornet]] aircraft),<ref name="strength">{{cite news |url= http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2015/03/saudi-ambassador-announces-military-operation-yemen-150325234138956.html|title= Saudi and Arab allies bomb Houthi positions in Yemen|date= 26 March 2015 |access-date=26 March 2014}}</ref> Bahrain sent 15, Qatar 10, Jordan and Morocco six each and Sudan four.<ref name="repel">{{cite news|url=http://english.alarabiya.net/en/News/middle-east/2015/03/26/GCC-states-to-repel-Houthi-aggression-in-Yemen-statement-.html|title=Saudi warplanes bomb Houthi positions in Yemen|date=25 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015|publisher=[[Al Arabiya English]]}}</ref><ref name="sudan">{{cite news |url=http://www.worldbulletin.net/todays-news/157087/sudan-denies-plane-shot-down-by-yemens-houthis|publisher=World Bulletin|title=Sudan denies plane shot down by Yemen's Houthis|date=28 March 2015|access-date=28 March 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/mar/26/gulf-states-yemen-ground-offensive-to-halt-houthi-rebel-advance|title=Gulf states consider Yemen ground offensive to halt Houthi rebel advance|date= 26 March 2015 |work=[[The Guardian]] |access-date=26 March 2014}}</ref>

The operation was declared over on 21 April 2015.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32402688?post_id=100001523553823_889997584394352#_=_|title= Yemen conflict: Saudi Arabia ends air campaign | work= BBC News |date=21 April 2015 | access-date= 21 April 2015}}</ref>

=== Air campaign ===

==== March 2015 ====
In March 2015, in a joint statement, the member-states of the [[Gulf Cooperation Council]] (with the exception of [[Oman]]) said they had decided to intervene against the Houthis at the request of Hadi's government.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2015/03/saudi-ambassador-announces-military-operation-yemen-150325234138956.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Saudi and Arab allies bomb Houthi positions in Yemen|date=26 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref>

The coalition declared Yemeni airspace to be a restricted area, with [[Salman of Saudi Arabia|King Salman]] declaring the [[Royal Saudi Air Force|RSAF]] to be [[No-fly zone|in full control of the zone]].<ref name="repel"/> Saudi Arabia began airstrikes, reportedly relying on US intelligence reports and surveillance images to select and hit targets, including weapons, aircraft<ref name="cnn">{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/03/25/middleeast/yemen-unrest/|publisher=CNN|title=Saudi Arabia launches airstrikes in Yemen|date=26 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref> on the ground and air defences.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/officials-saudi-led-action-in-yemen-relied-heavily-on-us-intelligence/2015/03/26/6d15302c-d3da-11e4-8fce-3941fc548f1c_story.html|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]]|title=Officials: Saudi-led action relied on U.S. intelligence|last=DeYoung|first=Karen |authorlink=Karen DeYoung |date=26 March 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref> [[Al Jazeera]] reported that [[Mohammed Ali al-Houthi]], a Houthi commander appointed in February as president of the [[Revolutionary Committee (Yemen)|Revolutionary Committee]], was injured and three other Houthi commanders were killed by airstrikes in Sanaʽa.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://america.aljazeera.com/articles/2015/3/25/houthi-aden.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Saudis launch air campaign to defend Yemen government|date=25 March 2015|access-date=1 April 2015}}</ref>

Strikes on 26 March also hit [[Al Anad Air Base]], a former [[United States special operations forces|US special operations forces]] facility in [[Lahij Governorate]] seized by Houthis earlier in the week.<ref name="leads">{{cite news |url=http://america.aljazeera.com/articles/2015/3/26/Saudi-airstrikes-yemen.html|title=Saudi Arabia leads airstrikes against Yemen's Houthi rebels|date=26 March 2015|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]] America|access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref> The targets reportedly included the Houthi-controlled missile base in Sanaʽa and its fuel depot.<ref name="offensive">{{cite news |url=https://www.theglobeandmail.com/news/world/saudi-arabia-has-150000-troops-for-yemen-operation-report/article23628188/ |newspaper=[[The Globe and Mail]] |title=Egypt, Jordan and Sudan ready for ground offensive in Yemen.: report |date=26 March 2015 |location=Toronto |access-date=26 March 2015 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150326221558/http://www.theglobeandmail.com/news/world/saudi-arabia-has-150000-troops-for-yemen-operation-report/article23628188/ |archivedate=26 March 2015 }}</ref> Strikes overnight also targeted Houthis in [[Taiz]] and [[Sa'dah]]. Thousands demonstrated in Sanaʽa against the intervention, which ex-president [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]] also condemned. In Taiz thousands came out supporting Hadi and Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/03/coalition-jets-continue-hit-houthi-targets-yemen-150327022702372.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Coalition jets continue to hit Houthi targets in Yemen|date=27 March 2015|access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref>

The scope of strikes expanded further on 27 March, with a radar installation in the [[Ma'rib Governorate]] and an airbase in the [[Abyan Governorate]] coming under air attack. The commander of the operation dismissed reports of civilian casualties, saying airstrikes were being carried out with precision.<ref name="voa">{{cite news |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/saudi-led-airstrikes-continue-for-second-day-in-yemen/2696496.html|publisher=[[Voice of America]] |title=Egyptian, Saudi Vessels Approach Yemen Coast|first=Edward|last=Yeranian|date=27 March 2015|access-date=27 March 2015}}</ref> Additional strikes early on the next day hit targets in [[Al Hudaydah]], Sa'dah and the Sanaʽa area, as well as [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]]'s main base. Rumours indicated Saleh fled to [[Sanhan, Yemen|Sanhan]], on the outskirts of the Houthi-controlled capital.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/03/yemen-aden-saudi-arabia-150327174924579.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Saudi-led air strikes hit Yemen for third night|date=28 March 2015|access-date=27 March 2015}}</ref> An Aden government official said Saudi strikes destroyed a long-range missile facility controlled by the Houthis.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.worldbulletin.net/todays-news/157098/saudi-operation-hit-yemen-base-holding-long-range-missiles |date=28 March 2015|publisher=World Bulletin|title=Saudi operation hit Yemen base holding long-range missiles|access-date=28 March 2015}}</ref>

The Houthis claimed to have shot down a [[Sudanese Air Force]] plane over northern Sanaʽa and captured its pilot on 28 March. The Sudanese government denied that any of its four warplanes had come under fire or been shot down.<ref name="sudan"/> On the previous day, the Houthis claimed to have shot down a "hostile" Saudi drone in Sanaʽa.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.aa.com.tr/en/world/yemens-houthis-shoot-down-drone-in-sanaa-tv/63148|title=Yemen's Houthis shoot down drone in Sanaa: TV|website=www.aa.com.tr}}</ref>

Airstrikes hit an arms depot, military airbase and special forces headquarters in Sanaʽa early on 29 March. A weapons depot outside Sanaʽa was destroyed, causing damage to an airport and planes on the ground. Sa'dah and Al Hudaydah were targeted as well. Brigadier General [[Ahmad Asiri (military)|Ahmed Asiri]], the coalition's spokesman, said Saudi artillery and [[Boeing AH-64 Apache|Apache]] attack helicopters were mobilised to "deter" Houthi fighters massing on the border with Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/03/fresh-saudi-led-strikes-hit-houthi-targets-yemen-150328224634577.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|date=29 March 2015 |title=Fresh Saudi-led strikes hit Houthi targets in Yemen |access-date=28 March 2015}}</ref>

On 30 March, at least 40 people including children were killed and 200 were injured<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/saudi-arabia-accused-of-killing-40-including-children-in-air-strike-on-yemen-refugee-camp-10145294.html|title=Saudi Arabia accused of killing 40 including children in air strike on Yemen refugee camp|work=[[The Independent]] | location=London|first=Lizzie|last=Dearden|date=31 March 2015}}</ref> by an airstrike that hit Al-Mazraq refugee camp near a military installation in northern district of [[Haradh]], international organizations said. Airstrikes also hit areas near the presidential palace in Sanaʽa,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/airstrikes-shake-yemens-capital-shiite-rebels-push-south-30000813|publisher=[[ABC News]] |title=Yemeni Rebels Shell Aden as Saudi Launches More Airstrikes|first=Ahmed|last=Al-Haj|date=30 March 2015|access-date=30 March 2015}}</ref> as well as [[Aden International Airport]].<ref name="dozens">{{cite news |url=https://www.smh.com.au/world/dozens-killed-as-yemens-houthis-shell-aden-saudi-jets-bomb-airport-20150331-1mccn3.html|newspaper=[[The Sydney Morning Herald]]|title=Dozens killed as Yemen's Houthis shell Aden, Saudi jets bomb airport|date=31 March 2015|access-date=31 March 2015}}</ref>

Food storage of Yemen Economic Corporation in Hodeidah was destroyed by three coalition strikes on 31 March.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.thenational.ae/world/middle-east/yemeni-civilians-struggle-to-get-by-amid-conflict|title=Yemeni civilians struggle to get by amid conflict|date=6 April 2015|access-date=8 April 2015}}</ref> Airstrikes were not limited to the Yemeni mainland. Missiles struck homes on the island of [[Perim]], according to residents who fled by boat to [[Djibouti]].<ref>{{cite news |publisher=CNN|url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/04/09/middleeast/yemen-refugees-djibouti/index.html|date=9 April 2015 |title='A window into hell:' Desperate Yemenis flee Saudi airstrikes by boat|first=Nima|last=Elbagir |authorlink=Nima Elbagir |access-date=9 April 2015}}</ref>

==== April 2015 ====
{{multiple image|caption_align=center
 | align       = right
 | direction   = horizontal
 | header      = Destruction in Sana'a after air strike on 20 April 2015
 | width1      = 220
 | width2      = 220
 | image1      = Sana'a after airstrike 20-4-2015 - Widespread destruction- 15.jpg
 | caption1    = Destruction in the residential neighborhoods near mountain Attan
 | image2      = Sana'a after airstrike 20-4-2015 - destruction (34734594).jpeg
 | caption2    = Destroyed Shopping center
}}
Dozens of casualties came from an explosion in a dairy and oil factory in [[Al Hudaydah]], which was variously blamed on an airstrike or a rocket from a nearby military base on 1 April. Medical sources reported 25 deaths, while the Yemen Army said 37 were killed and 80 wounded.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/01/us-yemen-security-factory-idUSKBN0MS3H020150401|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Explosion at Yemen factory kills at least 25: residents, medics|date=1 April 2015|access-date=1 April 2015}}</ref> Airstrikes also hit targets in Sa'dah on 1 April.<ref name="rages">{{cite news |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-03-31/yemen-rebels-seize-base-near-shipping-lane-as-saudis-target-aden|publisher=[[Bloomberg News]] |title=Saudi Coalition Hits Houthi Stronghold as Aden Battle Rages|date=31 March 2015|first=Mohammed|last=Hatem|access-date=1 April 2015}}</ref>

Despite persistent airstrikes, Houthi and allied units continued to advance on central Aden, backed by tanks and heavy artillery.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/death-toll-in-yemen-rises-as-saudi-led-military-attacks-continue/2015/04/01/12feec94-d7f0-11e4-b3f2-607bd612aeac_story.html|title=Rebel forces push farther into key Yemeni port city of Aden|work=[[The Washington Post]] | first=Ali|last=al-Mujahed|date=1 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/01/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0MS4Y120150401|title=Yemen Houthi fighters backed by tanks reach central Aden|work=[[Reuters]] | date=1 April 2015}}</ref> Houthis seized the presidential palace on 2 April, but reportedly withdrew after overnight air raids early the next day.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://zeenews.india.com/news/world/yemen-rebels-quit-aden-palace-after-air-raids-senior-official_1572403.html|publisher=[[Zee News]]|title=Yemen rebels quit Aden palace after air raids: Senior official|date=3 April 2015|access-date=2 April 2015}}</ref> Coalition planes also airdropped weapons and medical aid to pro-Hadi fighters in Aden.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.hindustantimes.com/world-news/saudis-airdrop-arms-to-aden-defenders-houthis-pull-back/article1-1333664.aspx|newspaper=[[Hindustan Times]] |title=Saudis airdrop arms to Aden defenders, Houthis pull back|date=3 April 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref>

The [[International Committee of the Red Cross]] announced on 5 April that it had received permission from the coalition to fly medical supplies and aid workers into Sanaʽa and was awaiting permission to send a surgical team by boat to [[Aden]]. The coalition said it had set up a special body to coordinate aid deliveries to Yemen.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/04/red-cross-permission-deliver-aid-yemen-150406011849828.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Red Cross given permission to deliver aid to Yemen|date=6 April 2015|access-date=5 April 2015}}</ref>

On 6 April, airstrikes began before sunset and struck targets in western Sanaʽa, Sa'dah and the [[Ad Dali' Governorate]], a supply route for Houthis in the [[Battle of Aden (2015)|Battle of Aden]].<ref name="fiercefighting">{{cite news |url=http://www.chron.com/news/world/article/Pakistan-says-Saudi-led-coalition-in-Yemen-wants-6180919.php|newspaper=[[Houston Chronicle]] |title=Fierce fighting as rebels move on holdouts in Yemen's Aden|date=6 April 2015|access-date=6 April 2015}}</ref>

Airstrikes on 7 April hit a [[Republican Guard (Yemen)|Republican Guard]] base in the [[Ibb Governorate]], injuring 25 troops. Yemeni sources claimed three children at a nearby school were killed by the attack,<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.bostonherald.com/news_opinion/international/middle_east/2015/04/saudi_led_airstrikes_hit_yemens_south_amid_ground|newspaper=[[Boston Herald]] |title=Saudi-led airstrikes hit Yemen's south amid ground fighting|date=7 April 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref> while six were injured.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/04/07/middleeast/yemen-crisis-houthis-saudi-arabia/|publisher=CNN|title=Yemen says Saudi airstrikes hit school, injuring students|date=7 April 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref>

The [[Parliament of Pakistan]] voted against military action on 10 April, despite a request from Saudi Arabia that it join the coalition.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/10/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0N10LO20150410|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Pakistan declines Saudi call for armed support in Yemen fight|date=10 April 2015|first=Mohammed|last=Mukhashaf|access-date=10 April 2015}}</ref>

Airstrikes launched on 12 April, against the base of the 22nd Brigade of the [[Republican Guard (Yemen)|Yemeni Republican Guard]] in the [[Taiz Governorate]] struck both the brigade and a nearby village inhabited by members of the [[Al-Akhdam]] minority community, killing eight civilians and injuring more than ten others.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.yementimes.com/en/1875/news/5048/Civilians-killed-by-a-coalition-strike-on-a-Republican-Guards-Brigade-in-Taiz.htm|newspaper=[[Yemen Times]] |title=Civilians Killed by a Coalition Strike on a Republican Guards Brigade in Taiz |date=12 April 2015|access-date=12 April 2015}}</ref> On 17 April, both the GCC coalition's spokesman called by Saudi broadcaster Al-Ehkbariya TV and a commander of the pro-Hadi rebels on the ground said airstrikes had intensified, focusing on both Sanaʽa and Taiz.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/calls-274-million-yemen-aid-humanitarian-30387289|title=Al-Qaida in Yemen Takes Massive Weapons Depot From Army|date=17 April 2015|publisher=[[ABC News]] |agency=Associated Press}}</ref> One strike on the Republican Palace in [[Taiz]] killed 19 pro-Houthi gunmen.<ref>{{cite news |author1=Ahmed Al-Haj|title=Yemen militia aligned with President Hadi attacks Houthi-held base|url=https://www.thestar.com/news/world/2015/04/18/yemen-militia-aligned-with-president-hadi-attacks-houthi-held-base.html |newspaper=[[Toronto Star]] |date=18 April 2015 |access-date=19 April 2015}}</ref>

[[File:Yemen ethno 2002.jpg|thumb|upright=1.45|Ethnoreligious groups in 2002. [[Zaidiyyah|Zaydi]] [[Shi'a]] followers make up between 35% and 42.1% of Muslims in Yemen.<ref>{{cite book|last=Day|first=Stephen W.|title=Regionalism and Rebellion in Yemen: A Troubled National Union|date=2012|page=31|publisher=Cambridge University Press|isbn=978-1-107-02215-7}}</ref>]]

=== Naval role ===
[[Egypt]] and Saudi Arabia committed warships to support coalition operations.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.militarytimes.com/story/military/2015/03/27/saudi-arabia-egypt-yemen-airstrikes/70545168/|work=[[Military Times Media Group|Military Times]] |first=Ahmed|last=al-Haj|title=Saudi, Egyptian warships move into strait as Yemen airstrikes widen|date=27 March 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref> Somalia offered its airspace and territorial waters.<ref name="Ssfpstsciy"/> Four [[Egyptian Navy]] vessels steamed toward the [[Gulf of Aden]] after operations began.<ref name="leads"/> Riyadh requested access to Somali airspace and waters to carry out operations.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.somalicurrent.com/2015/03/26/saudi-led-coalition-request-somalia-to-use-its-airspace-to-attack-houthi-rebels/|work=Somali Current|title=Saudi led coalition request Somalia to use its airspace to attack Houthi rebels|date=26 March 2015|access-date=6 October 2019|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150709131008/http://www.somalicurrent.com/2015/03/26/saudi-led-coalition-request-somalia-to-use-its-airspace-to-attack-houthi-rebels/ |archivedate=9 July 2015}}</ref> On 27 March, the [[military of Egypt|Egyptian military]] said a squadron of Egyptian and Saudi warships took up positions at the [[Bab al-Mandab]] strait.<ref name="voa"/> The Saudi military threatened to destroy any ship attempting to make port.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/03/26/middleeast/yemen-saudi-arabia-airstrikes/|publisher=CNN|title=Saudi-led coalition strikes rebels in Yemen, inflaming tensions in region|date=26 March 2015|access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref>

The [[Royal Saudi Navy]] evacuated diplomats and United Nations staff from Aden to [[Jeddah]] on 28 March.<ref name="flee">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/03/28/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0ML0YC20150328|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Diplomats and U.N. staff flee Yemen as Houthis target Aden|date=28 March 2015|access-date=28 March 2015}}</ref>

Witnesses told [[Reuters]] that Egyptian warships bombarded Houthi positions as they attempted to advance on Aden on 30 March.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.trust.org/item/20150330141004-371fq/?source=search|publisher=Thomson Reuters Foundation|title=Warships shell Houthis outside Yemeni city of Aden -witnesses|date=30 March 2015|access-date=30 March 2015}}</ref> Warships again fired on Houthi positions at Aden International Airport on or about 1 April.<ref name="rages"/>

Djibouti foreign minister [[Mahmoud Ali Youssouf]] said the Houthis placed heavy weapons and fast attack boats on [[Perim]] and a smaller island in the Bab al-Mandab strait. He warned that "the prospect of a war in the strait of Bab al-Mandab is a real one" and said the weapons posed "a big danger" to his country, commercial shipping traffic, and military vessels. He called on the coalition to clear the islands, which he said included missiles and long-range cannons.<ref name="youssouf">{{cite news |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-04-02/yemeni-rebels-strengthen-positions-in-key-strait-djibouti-says |publisher=[[Bloomberg News]] |first=Paul |last=Richardson |date=2 April 2015|title=Yemeni Rebels Strengthen Positions at Entrance to Red Sea|access-date=2 April 2015}}</ref>

On 4 April, Egyptian President [[Abdel Fattah el-Sisi]] called protecting [[Red Sea]] shipping and securing the Bab al-Mandab "a top priority for Egypt's national security".<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.timesofoman.com/News/49836/Article-Securing-key-Yemen-strait-a-priority-for-Egypt-says-Sisi|newspaper=[[Times of Oman]] |title=Securing key Yemen strait a priority for Egypt, says Sisi|date=4 April 2015|access-date=7 April 2015}}</ref>

On 15 April, coalition spokesman Saudi Brigadier General Ahmed Al-Asiri, said that its warships were focusing on protecting shipping routes and screening ships heading to port for shipments intended for the Houthis.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.operationdecisivestorm.com/day-22-april-15-2015-saudi-ministry-of-defense-briefing/#sthash.oPYRw15c.dpbs|title=Day 21 April 15, 2015: Saudi Ministry of Defense Briefing|date=15 April 2015|publisher=Saudi Ministry of Defense}}</ref>

The [[United States Navy|US Navy]] provided support to the naval blockade, halting and searching vessels suspected of carrying Iranian arms to the Houthis.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-widens-role-in-saudi-led-campaign-against-yemen-rebels-1428882967|newspaper=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|title=U.S. Widens Role in Saudi-led Campaign Against Houthi Rebels in Yemen|date=12 April 2015|first1=Maria|last1=Abi-Habib|first2=Adam|last2=Entous|access-date=13 April 2015}}</ref> On 21 April, the United States announced it was deploying warships to Yemeni waters to monitor Iranian ships.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/04/20/politics/iran-united-states-warships-monitoring/|title=U.S.: Warships near Yemen create 'options' for dealing with Iranian vessels|publisher=CNN|date=21 April 2015}}</ref> The US in particular noted a convoy of Iranian vessels, which US authorities said could potentially be carrying weapons to Houthi fighters in contravention of UN sanctions.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://2009-2017.state.gov/r/pa/prs/dpb/2015/04/240950.htm#YEMEN|title=Daily Press Briefing for 21 April 2015|publisher=U.S. Department of State|date=21 April 2015}}</ref> The US reported that the Iranian convoy reversed course on 23 April.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/iranian-ships-turn-back-after-a-warning-about-arming-rebels-in-yemen-1429818885|title=Iranian Ships Turn Back After a Warning About Arming Rebels in Yemen|work=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|date=23 April 2015|first=Dion|last=Nissenbaum}}</ref>

=== Ground clashes ===
Sudan said it was stationing ground troops in Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.ynetnews.com/articles/0,7340,L-4641287,00.html|work=[[Ynetnews]]|title=Sudan says will take part in Yemen campaign with ground, air forces|date=26 March 2015|access-date=31 March 2015}}</ref> The Special Forces of the [[Bahrain Defence Force]], Taskforce 11, were also deployed to Yemen.<ref>{{cite news |publisher=[[Bahrain News Agency]] |title=HRH Crown Prince visits Royal Guard, honours servicemen who participated in Taskforce 11 |date=21 June 2017 |url=http://www.bna.bh/portal/en/news/791025 |access-date=13 July 2017 |quote=The Crown Prince presented the military medals awarded by His Majesty the King to the officers, non-commissioned officers, and personnel of the BDF's Special Operations Force (Taskforce 11) in recognition of their dedicated service in Yemen.}}</ref>

Between 31 March and April, Saudi and Houthi forces reportedly traded artillery and rocket fire across the border between SA and Yemen.<ref name="dozens"/><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/03/31/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0MR0HE20150331|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Heavy clashes on Saudi-Yemeni border; Hadi government pleads for troops|date=31 March 2015|access-date=31 March 2015}}</ref> A Saudi border guard was killed on 2 April, the campaign's first confirmed coalition casualty.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32157994|work=BBC News|title=Yemen crisis: Rebels storm presidential palace in Aden|date=2 April 2015|access-date=2 April 2015}}</ref> Followed by another two soldiers killed the next day.<ref name="provinces">{{cite news |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/yemeni-troops-retake-other-provinces-al-qaeda-rules-mukalla-port-city-2129445977|publisher=[[Middle East Eye]]|title=Yemeni troops retake provinces as al-Qaeda captures port city of Mukalla|date=4 April 2015|access-date=4 April 2015}}</ref> An Egyptian truck driver was killed by Houthi shelling.<ref>{{cite news |title=Egyptian truck driver killed by shelling at Yemeni-Saudi border|url=http://english.ahram.org.eg/NewsContent/1/64/126826/Egypt/Politics-/Egyptian-truck-driver-killed-by-shelling-at-Yemeni.aspx|work=[[Al-Ahram]]|date=3 April 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref>

SA reportedly began removing sections of the [[Saudi–Yemen barrier]] fence along its border with the Sa'dah and [[Hajjah Governorate|Hajjah]] [[governorates of Yemen|governorates]] on 3 April. The purpose of the removal was not immediately clear.<ref name="remove">{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/04/yemen-leader-loyalists-drive-houthis-aden-150403132431234.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Saudi-led airstrikes drive Houthis from Aden|date=3 April 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref>

On 12 April, members of the Takhya tribe launched an attack on a Saudi base after several of its members died in an airstrike. Weapons and ammunition were taken.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.yemenakhbar.com/yemen-news/166853.html?source=true|title=القبائل اليمنية تواصل إحكام سيطرتها على مواقع عسكرية سعودية وأسر 17 جندي سعودي – اخبار اليمن الان|access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.khabaragency.net/news24336.html|title=مصادر "خبر": القبائل اليمنية أسرت 17 ضابطاً وجندياً سعودياً|work=وكالة خبر للأنباء|access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.mtgdnews.com/arab/27743.html|title=أخبار الصراع اليمني السعودي: قبائل "طخية" تأسر 17 ضابط وجندي سعودي وتقتل 20 آخرين |work=أخبار متجددة|publisher=mtgdnews.com |access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref>

On 19 April, as Houthi leader Abdul-Malek El-Houthi accused SA of planning to invade Yemen,<ref name="Reuters">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/19/us-yemen-security-saudi-idUSKBN0NA0JB20150419|title=Yemen's Houthi leader accuses Saudi Arabia of seeking to invade|date=19 April 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref> Asiri claimed that coalition forces had information regarding a planned Houthi incursion into SA.<ref>{{cite web |url= http://www.spa.gov.sa/english/details.php?id=1351622|title=Daily Briefing of GCC Coalition spokesman Brig. Gen Ahmed Asiri|publisher=SPA|date=19 April 2015}}</ref>
A Saudi border guard died on 19 April and two others were injured from gunfire and mortar shelling across the border.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.chicagotribune.com/news/nationworld/chi-yemen-navy-warship-iran-20150420-story.html#page=2|newspaper=[[Chicago Tribune]] |title=U.S. warship heads to Yemeni waters to intercept Iranian weapons|date=20 April 2015|access-date=21 April 2015}}</ref>

== Operation Restoring Hope ==
[[File:Secretary Kerry Sits With Saudi King Salman, Foreign Minister al-Jubeir Before Bilateral Meeting in Washington (21148062001).jpg|thumb|King [[Salman of Saudi Arabia]] and Saudi Foreign Minister Adel al-Jubeir meet with [[John Kerry|U.S. Secretary of State John Kerry]] in September 2015]]
On 21 April, the [[Ministry of Defence (Saudi Arabia)|Saudi Defence Ministry]] declared it was ending the campaign of airstrikes because it had "successfully eliminated the threat" to its security posed by Houthi ballistic and heavy weaponry.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-04-21/saudi-arabia-says-airstrikes-in-yemen-succeeded-in-ending-threat|title=Saudi Arabia Says Airstrikes Succeeded in Ending Threat|first=Nadeem|last=Hamid|date=21 April 2015 |publisher=[[Bloomberg News]] |access-date=21 April 2015}}</ref> It announced the start of a new phase codenamed Operation Restoring Hope.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.operationrenewalofhope.com/operation-decisive-storm-ends-operation-renewal-of-hope-begins/ |title=With military objectives achieved, focus shifts to the political process|date=22 April 2015|publisher=Operation Renewal of Hope}}</ref> In a televised address, Hadi said the end of airstrikes had come at his request and thanked the Arab coalition for their support.<ref name="bbc.com: Iran urges aid effort">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32408312 |title=Yemen conflict: Iran urges aid effort as Saudi air strikes end |date=22 April 2015 |work=BBC News}}</ref>

Earlier that day King Salman ordered the Saudi National Guard to join the military operation.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cbsnews.com/news/saudi-arabia-king-salman-national-guard-yemen-iran-houthi-rebels/|title=Saudi king orders troops to join Yemen|publisher=[[CBS News]] |date=21 April 2015|access-date=21 April 2015}}</ref> Air and naval strikes continued despite the announcement that ''Decisive Storm'' had ended.

Both the Omani<ref name="omanpeace">{{cite news |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/04/22/uk-yemen-security-idUKKBN0ND0G620150422|title=Yemen rivals battle on despite declared end to Saudi raids|work=[[Reuters]]|date=22 April 2015|access-date=22 April 2015}}</ref> and Iranian<ref name="bbc.com: Iran urges aid effort"/><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/21/saudi-arabia-airstrikes-yemen-military-campaign-end|title=Saudi Arabia declares end to Yemen air strikes after four weeks of bombing|date=22 April 2015|work=[[The Guardian]]}}</ref> governments said they welcomed the end of airstrikes. On 22 April, Oman presented a seven-point peace deal to both parties. The proposed peace treaty entailed the reinstatement of Hadi's government and the evacuation of Houthi fighters from major cities.<ref name="omanpeace"/>

On 8 May, Saudi Arabia announced a five-day ceasefire set to start on 12 May,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/05/09/world/middleeast/saudi-arabia-announces-cease-fire-in-yemen.html |title=Saudi Arabia Announces Cease-Fire in Yemen |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=8 May 2015 |first1=Alissa J. |last1=Rubin |authorlink=Alissa J. Rubin |first2=Kareem |last2=Fahim}}</ref> following heavy pressure from the US.<ref>{{cite news |title=The war in Yemen: From Aden to Camp David|url=https://www.economist.com/news/middle-east-and-africa/21651273-could-temporary-truce-yemen-help-end-fighting-aden-camp-david |work=[[The Economist]]|date=14 May 2015|access-date=18 May 2015}}</ref> Later in the day, Saudi airplanes dropped leaflets in the [[Saada Governorate]] warning of airstrikes throughout the area.<ref>{{cite news |title=Arab coalition warns Yemenis to leave Saada province|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/05/yemenis-ordered-leave-saada-province-150508145754277.html |work=[[Al Jazeera]]|date=9 May 2015|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref> Houthi spokesman Mohamed al-Bukhaiti later told the [[BBC]] that the ceasefire had not been formally proposed and the Houthis would not respond until a plan was properly laid out.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32677260|title=Yemen conflict: UN criticises Saudi civilian bombings|work=BBC News|access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref> A spokesman for the Houthi-aligned military announced agreement to the ceasefire plan on 10 May, although he warned that a breach of the truce would prompt a military response.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/yemens-houthi-rebels-accept-five-day-truce-proposal-1431250255|newspaper=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|title=Yemen's Houthi Rebels Accept Five-Day Truce Proposal|date=10 May 2015|first1=Asa|last1=Fitch|first2=Mohammed|last2=al-Kibsi |access-date=10 May 2015}}</ref>

On 13 May, humanitarian agencies said they were trying to get aid into Yemen after a five-day ceasefire took effect on Tuesday night. Ships carrying humanitarian supplies docked at the Houthi-controlled [[Red Sea]] port of [[Al Hudaydah|Hudaydah]] as planes were standing by to help evacuate the injured.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32719194 |title=Yemen conflict: Aid effort begins as truce takes hold |date=13 May 2015 |work=BBC News}}</ref> Meanwhile, King Salman doubled his country's Yemen aid pledge to $540&nbsp;million, funds the UN said would "meet the life-saving and protection needs of 7.5&nbsp;million people affected".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/saudi-king-doubles-yemen-aid-pledge-540-mn-104046759.html |title=Saudi king doubles Yemen aid pledge to $540 mn|date=13 May 2015 |work=[[Yahoo! News]] |agency=Agence France-Presse}}</ref>

=== Airstrikes ===
At the operation's announcement, coalition leadership stressed that their campaign would attempt a political solution and that they would continue the air and naval blockade.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.dailystar.com.lb/News/Middle-East/2015/Apr-21/295278-saudi-led-coalition-ends-military-operation-in-yemen.ashx|title=Saudi-led coalition ends military operation in Yemen &#124; News , Middle East &#124; THE DAILY STAR|website=www.dailystar.com.lb}}</ref> Airstrikes resumed almost immediately following the coalition's announcement of the end of Operation Decisive Storm.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32430003 |title= Yemen conflict: Saudis launch new air strikes on rebels |work=BBC News |date=23 April 2015}}</ref>

On 22 April airstrikes continued in [[Taiz]], where an army base was hit shortly after Houthi fighters took it over,<ref name="npr-shifts">{{cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/blogs/thetwo-way/2015/04/22/401453167/saudi-arabia-shifts-military-campaign-in-yemen-airstrikes-continue|publisher=[[NPR]] |title=Saudi Arabia Shifts Military Campaign in Yemen; Airstrikes Continue|date=22 April 2015 |first=Bill|last=Chappell |access-date=22 April 2015}}</ref> and Aden, where an airstrike targeted Houthi tanks moving into a contested district,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/22/yemen-crisis-air-strike-hits-aden-after-saudi-arabia-ends-bombing-campaign|newspaper=[[The Guardian]]|title=Yemen crisis: air strike hits Aden after Saudi Arabia ends bombing campaign|first=Ian|last=Black |authorlink=Ian Black (journalist) |date=22 April 2015|access-date=22 April 2015}}</ref> among other locations, such as Al Hudaydah and [[Ibb]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/23/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0NC2LD20150423|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Saudi-led coalition launches air strikes throughout Yemen: residents|date=23 April 2015|access-date=23 April 2015}}</ref> The Houthis continued to fight for territory,<ref name="npr-shifts"/> with a Houthi spokesman saying the group would be prepared for peace talks on the condition of "a complete halt of attacks". The previous round of UN-sponsored talks collapsed after Houthi rebels attacked Hadi's residence in Sanaʽa.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/04/22/middleeast/yemen-crisis/|title=Houthis call for peace talks as Saudi planes strike Yemen|date=22 April 2015 |publisher=CNN |access-date=22 April 2015}}</ref>

By 26 April, coalition forces were striking what they described as Houthi military targets in Sanaʽa and Aden and in other locations, notably in Sa'ada province near the Saudi border, nearly every night.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2015/04/air-raids-ground-clashes-rage-yemen-150426123231533.html|title=Air raids and ground clashes rage in Yemen|date=26 April 2015|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/26/us-yemen-security-strikes-idUSKBN0NH04C20150426|title=Fighting escalates across Yemen, air strikes on capital Sanaa|date=26 April 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref> On 26 April, after midnight, airstrikes struck Houthi and pro-Saleh positions and targets in and around Sanaʽa, Aden, and the [[Ma'rib Governorate|Ma'rib]] and [[Ad Dali' Governorate|Ad Dali']] governorates, backing up anti-Houthi fighters in the latter three locations, with more than 90 rebels reportedly killed.<ref>{{cite news|title=Saudi air raids strike Yemeni capital|url=http://www.3news.co.nz/world/saudi-air-raids-strike-yemeni-capital-2015042708|agency=Agence France-Presse|publisher=[[MediaWorks New Zealand]]|date=27 April 2015|access-date=27 April 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150518082725/http://www.3news.co.nz/world/saudi-air-raids-strike-yemeni-capital-2015042708|archive-date=18 May 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> Coalition warships shelled fighters near Aden's commercial port. Saudi warplanes also targeted Houthis in the Sa'dah Governorate, while Saudi artillery fired on targets in the Hajjah Governorate along the border.<ref>{{cite news |title=Air raids and ground clashes rage in Yemen|date=26 April 2015 |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2015/04/air-raids-ground-clashes-rage-yemen-150426123231533.html |publisher=[[Al Jazeera]] |access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref> The Saudi National Guard was deployed on the border.<ref>{{cite news |title=First Saudi National Guards reach Yemen border zone|url=http://english.ahram.org.eg/NewsContent/2/8/128747/World/Region/First-Saudi-National-Guards-reach-Yemen-border-zon.aspx |agency=Agence France-Presse|newspaper=[[Al-Ahram]] |date=27 April 2015|access-date=27 April 2015}}</ref>

On 28 April, [[Sana'a International Airport|Sanaʽa International Airport]] was bombed<ref>{{cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/yemen-rebels-allies-advance-southern-city-aden-30671835|publisher=[[ABC News]] |title=Yemen Rebels and Allies Advance in Southern City of Aden|first=Ahmed|last=Al-Haj|date=29 April 2015|access-date=29 April 2015}}</ref> by Saudi F-15 fighters to prevent an Iranian plane<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/news/picture/yemen-airport-bombed?articleId=USRTX1ATMJ|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Yemen airport bombed|date=29 April 2015|access-date=29 April 2015}}</ref> belonging to [[Iranian Red Crescent Society]] (IRCS) from landing, while it was approaching to land. The fighters had warned the plane to turn back, in an unsuccessful attempt to thwart its landing, but the Iranian pilot ignored the "illegal warnings", saying that, on the basis of international law, his plane did not need further permission to land.<ref>{{cite news |title=Aid flights to Yemen blocked after Saudi Arabian jets bomb airport runway|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/28/aid-flights-to-yemen-blocked-after-saudi-arabia-bombs-airport-runway|access-date=30 April 2015|newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |agency=[[Reuters]]|date=29 April 2015}}</ref>

On the night of 6 May 2015, the Saudi-led coalition carried out 130 airstrikes in Yemen in a 24-hour period. At first, coalition spokesperson Ahmed Asiri admitted that schools and hospitals were targeted but claimed that these were used as weapon storage sites. Asiri later claimed that his words had been mistranslated. The United Nations humanitarian coordinator for Yemen Johannes Van Der Klaauw said that these bombings constituted a [[war crime]]. "The indiscriminate bombing of populated areas, with or without prior warning, is a contravention international humanitarian law," he said. He continued to say that he was particularly concerned about airstrikes on Saada "where scores of civilians were reportedly killed and thousands were forced to flee their homes after the coalition declared the entire governate a military target".<ref name="edition.cnn.com">{{cite news |title=U.N. rep accuses Saudi-led coalition of violating international law |author=Mariano Castillo |date=12 May 2015 |publisher=CNN |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/05/09/asia/saudi-airstrikes-yemen/|author-link=Mariano Castillo }}</ref>

[[File:Secretary Kerry Listens As Saudi Foreign Minister al-Jubeir Announces During Paris News Conference That Yemen Cease Fire Will Begin Tuesday (17427072602).jpg|thumb|Saudi foreign minister [[Adel al-Jubeir]] announced a five-day ceasefire in Yemen, 8 May 2015]]

[[Iranian Foreign Ministry|The Iranian Foreign Ministry]] summoned the Saudi [[chargé d'affaires]], and the [[Iranian Parliament]] and the Iranian Red Crescent Society blasted Saudi Arabia for blocking Iranian humanitarian aid.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://en.ghatreh.com/view/5043/Iranian-Parliament-Condemns-Saudi-Arabia-for-Blocking-Humanitarian-Aid-to-Yemen|title=Iranian Parliament Condemns Saudi Arabia for Blocking Humanitarian Aid to Yemen |publisher=ghatreh|access-date=18 May 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://kayhan.ir/en/news/13138/iran-summons-saudi-envoy-over-blocking-humanitarian-aid-to-yemen|title=Iran Summons Saudi Envoy Over Blocking Humanitarian Aid to Yemen|newspaper=[[Kayhan]] |access-date=18 May 2015}}</ref>

The UN [[Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]] (OCHA) "strongly urged" the coalition to stop targeting airports and seaports so that aid could reach all Yemenis.<ref name="reuters-airport"/><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.yementimes.com/en/1875/news/5077/Humanitarian-flights-unable-to-land-after-bombing-Sana'a-International-Airport.htm|title=Humanitarian flights unable to land, after bombing Sana'a International Airport|work=[[Yemen Times]] }}</ref>

ICRC and [[Médecins Sans Frontières]] (MSF), also known as Doctors Without Borders, said that they were extremely concerned about damage to the airports at Sanaa and to the port city of [[Hodeidah]].<ref name="reuters-airport">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-humanitarian/un-urges-saudi-led-coalition-to-stop-targeting-yemen-airport-idUSKBN0NP1VJ20150504 |title=UN urges Saudi-led coalition to stop targeting Yemen airport |work=[[Reuters]] |date=4 May 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

Overnight on 29 and 30 April, SA was reported to have airdropped arms to anti-Houthi fighters in Taiz.<ref name="ReferenceB">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/29/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0NK0N020150429|title=Heavy fighting in Yemen, Saudi Arabia trains tribal fighters|date=30 April 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>

On 30 April airstrikes hit five provinces.<ref name="ReferenceB"/> New airstrikes hit SIA, completely halting aid deliveries.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/30/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0NL0Q720150430|title=Houthis clash with Saudi forces on Yemen border, dozens killed|work=[[Reuters]] | date=30 April 2015}}</ref>

[[File:Air strike in Sana'a 11 May 2015 01.jpg|thumb|upright|An airstrike in Sanaʽa,<br/>11 May 2015]]
On 6 May coalition airstrikes targeted the Police Training Center in the [[Dhamar Governorate]], damaging nearby houses<ref name="Saba Net – Yemen news agency">{{cite news |date=6 May 2015 |url=http://www.sabanews.net/en/news395227.htm|title=Saudi airstrikes kill 11 people in Dhamar |publisher=[[Saba News Agency]] |access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref> meanwhile the civil aviation authority announced it would re-open the airport to receive aid.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.saharasamay.com/world-news/676572666/yemen-saudi-led-warplanes-bomb-sanaa-airport.html|title=Yemen:Saudi-led warplanes bomb Sanaa airport|access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref>

Coalition airstrikes targeted the houses of Saleh in Sanaʽa in the early hours of 10 May, eyewitnesses said. Khabar, a Yemeni news agency allied with Saleh said that the former president and his family were unharmed.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/may/10/saudi-air-strikes-in-yemen-target-house-of-ex-president-saleh|title=Saudi air strikes in Yemen target house of ex-president Saleh|date=10 May 2015|work=[[The Guardian]]}}</ref>

The Moroccan government said on 10 May that one of its [[General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon]] aircraft taking part in the air campaign went missing in action over Yemen, along with its pilot.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/moroccan-fighter-jet-missing-yemen-30946660|publisher=[[ABC News]] |title=Moroccan Fighter Jet Goes Missing in Yemen|date=11 May 2015|access-date=10 May 2015}}</ref> The Houthis claimed responsibility, with Yemeni state TV broadcasting a report on the jet being downed by tribal militias over the Sa'dah Governorate and showing images of the wreckage.<ref name="airloss">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32688816|work=BBC News|title=Yemen conflict: Houthi rebels 'down Moroccan warplane'|date=11 May 2015|access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref>

On 18 May Saudi-led airstrikes reportedly resumed on Houthi positions after a humanitarian ceasefire expired late on Sunday. Three coalition airstrikes hit Sa'ada on Monday. Yemen's exiled Foreign Minister Riyadh Yassin blamed the rebel group for the renewal of hostilities. Al-Arabiya said Saudi forces shelled Houthi outposts along Yemen's northern border after the fighters fired mortars at a Saudi army post in Najran province.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/18/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0O30II20150518|title=Saudi-led air strikes hit Yemen after truce expires|date=18 May 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>

On 23 May [[OCHA]] reported that airstrikes continued in the northern governorates of Sa'ada (Baqim, Haydan, Saqayn and As Safra) and Hajjah (Abs, Hayran, Haradh, Huth, Kuhlan Affar and Sahar districts). The road connecting Haradh and Huth districts was reportedly hit. Airstrikes were also reported in Al Jawf Governorate (Bart Al Anan district).<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Flash%20Update%20on%20the%20Escalating%20Conflict%20-%20No.%2036%20-%2023%20May%202015.pdf |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Flash Update 36 |date= 23 May 2015 |publisher=[[ReliefWeb]] |accessdate=25 February 2016}}</ref>

On 27 May airstrikes hit a police station in the capital, [[Sana'a|Sanaʽa]], killing 45 officers.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.thehansindia.com/posts/index/2015-05-28/Saudi-led-airstrikes-on-Yemen-police-headquarters-kills-45-153829|title=Saudi-led airstrikes on Yemen police headquarters kills 45|date=28 May 2015|publisher=thehansindia.com}}</ref> The Houthi-controlled Ministry of Health announced that in total, 96 people were killed.

On 3 June the residence of a Houthi leader in Ibb province was hit by an airstrike, according to eyewitnesses.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/03/us-yemen-security-strikes-idUSKBN0OJ0J520150603|title=Air strikes kill 20 Houthi fighters in Yemen's Aden: militia|date=3 June 2015|work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>
{{multiple image|caption_align=center
 | align       = right
 | direction   = horizontal
 | header      = Destruction in the south of Sana'a (12 June 2015)
 | width1      = 260
 | width2      = 180
 | image1      = Destroyed house in the south of Sanaa 12-6-2015-1.jpg
 | caption1    = Destroyed house
 | image2      = Destroyed car in the south of Sanaa 12-6-2015-2.jpg
 | caption2    = Destroyed car
}}
On 12 June Saudi jets bombed the [[UNESCO World Heritage Site]] of Sanaʽa Old City, killing at least six people and destroying some of the ancient buildings. [[UNESCO]] Director General [[Irina Bokova]] said in a statement that she is "profoundly distressed by the loss of human lives as well as by damage inflicted on one of the world's oldest jewels of Islamic urban landscape". Locals also condemned the action.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.euronews.com/2015/06/12/unesco-condemns-bombing-of-sanaa-s-old-city/|title=UNESCO condemns bombing of Sanaa's Old City|publisher=euronews|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

On 23 September 2015, the Saudi-led coalition destroyed a ceramics factory in the town of Matnah. One civilian was killed and others were wounded. According to the BBC, the bomb is believed to have been produced in the United Kingdom by GEC-Marconi Dynamics.<ref>{{cite AV media |title=UK-made bomb 'hit Yemen factory' |author=[[Orla Guerin]] |date= 25 March 2016 |publisher=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/av/world-middle-east-35898999/uk-made-bomb-hit-yemen-factory |access-date=7 May 2017}}</ref> The factory's owner Ghalib al-Sawary told the BBC: "We built it over 20 years but to destroy it took only twenty minutes."<ref>{{cite news |title=A year of war that has set Yemen back decades |author=Orla Guerin |work=BBC News |date=26 March 2016 |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-35901321 |author-link=Orla Guerin }}</ref> Campaigners say this attack was a violation of the laws of war.

On 26 October 2015 Médecins Sans Frontières reported that a coalition airstrike had completely destroyed a hospital they ran in Saada province's Haydan governorate, including the operating room. When the first strike hit an unused part of the hospital the facility was completely evacuated, so there were no direct casualties. A spokesman for the coalition forces, Brig-Gen [[Ahmed Asiri|Ahmed al-Asiri]], denied responsibility for the attack.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34645469|title=Yemen conflict: MSF hospital destroyed by air strikes|work=BBC News|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref> "With the hospital destroyed, at least 200,000 people now have no access to lifesaving medical care," MSF said. "This attack is another illustration of a complete disregard for civilians in Yemen, where bombings have become a daily routine," said Hassan Boucenine, MSF head of mission in Yemen. The GPS coordinates of the only hospital in the Haydan district were regularly shared with the Saudi-led coalition, and the roof of the facility was clearly identified with the MSF logo, he said.<ref>[http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2015-10/28/c_134756413.htm "MSF hospital in Yemen bombed by airstrike"], Xinhua (28 October 2015)</ref> UNICEF said the hospital in Saada was the 39th health center hit in Yemen since March, when the violence escalated. "More children in Yemen may well die from a lack of medicines and healthcare than from bullets and bombs," its executive director Anthony Lake said in a statement. He added that critical shortages of fuel, medication, electricity and water could mean many more will close. Amnesty International said the strike may amount to a war crime and called for an independent investigation.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/10/27/us-yemen-security-idUSKCN0SL0VK20151027|title=Yemeni MSF hospital bombed, Saudi-led coalition denies responsibility|work=[[Reuters]]|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/10/28/doctors-without-borders-says-saudi-led-airstrikes-bomb-yemen-hospital/|title=Doctors Without Borders says Saudi-led airstrikes bomb Yemen hospital|publisher=Fox News Channel|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref>

In February 2016, the Saudis bombed the ancient citadel of Kawkaban, killing seven civilians.<ref name="auto2">{{cite news |title=A year of war that has set Yemen back decades |author=Orla Guerin |work=BBC News |date=26 March 2016 |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-35901321|author-link=Orla Guerin }}</ref>

On 8 October 2016, Saudi-led airstrikes [[2016 Sana'a funeral air raid|targeted]] a hall in Sanaʽa where a funeral was taking place. At least 140 people were killed and about 600 were wounded. According to ''The Independent'', one rescuer said: "The place has been turned into a lake of blood."<ref name="independent.co.uk">{{cite news |title=Saudi-led coalition in Yemen accused of 'genocide' after airstrike on funeral hall kills 140; US says it will 'review' its support after latest attack |author=Ben Kentish |date=9 October 2016 |newspaper=[[The Independent]] |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/yemen-air-strike-bomb-kills-140-saudi-arabia-usa-white-house-a7352386.html}}</ref> After initially denying it was behind the attack, the Coalition's Joint Incidents Assessment Team admitted that it had bombed the hall but claimed that this attack had been a mistake caused by bad information.<ref>{{cite news |date=15 October 2016 |title=Saudi-led coalition admits to bombing Yemen funeral |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/oct/15/saudi-led-coalition-admits-to-bombing-yemen-funeral}}</ref> After this attack, US national security spokesperson said that the US government was "deeply disturbed" by the bombing and added that US support for the Saudi-led coalition was "not a blank cheque". He added "we have initiated an immediate review of our already significantly reduced support to the Saudi-led Coalition."<ref name="independent.co.uk"/> The United Nations humanitarian co-ordinator in Yemen Jamie McGoldrick said he was "shocked and outraged" by the "horrific" bombing. "This violence against civilians in Yemen must stop," he said.<ref name="independent.co.uk"/>

On the night of 15 February 2017, the Saudi-led coalition bombed a funeral reception near Sanaa. Initial reports suggest the bombing killed nine women and one child with ten more women reported wounded. "People heard the sound of planes and started running from the house but then the bombs hit the house directly. The roof collapsed and there was blood was everywhere," a resident of the village told a Reuters news agency cameraman.<ref>{{cite news |date=16 February 2017 |title=Air raid on Yemen funeral 'kills at least nine women'; Houthi rebels blame Arab coalition for attack on Shiraa village 40km north of capital Sanaa |publisher=[[Al Jazeera]] |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/02/air-raid-yemen-funeral-kills-women-170216093707979.html}}</ref>

An explosion in a warehouse on Sunday 7 April 2019, in Sanaa, have killed at least 11 civilians, including school children and left more than 39 people wounded. The Associated Press news agency said 13 killed, including 7 children and more than 100 were wounded. According to Al Jazeera and Houthi officials, the civilians were killed in a Saudi-led coalition airstrike.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi-led air raids 'kill at least 11 civilians' in Yemen's Sanaa |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/04/saudi-led-air-raids-kill-11-civilians-yemen-sanaa-190407201257046.html |accessdate=8 April 2019 |agency=Aljazeera |publisher=aljazeera.com |date=7 April 2019}}</ref> The Saudi-led coalition denied any airstrikes took place that day on Sanaa. The state-run news agency in Aden, aligned with the internationally recognized government, said the rebels had stored weapons at the warehouse. According to ''The Washington Post'', "some families and residents of the district of Sawan said the explosion occurred after a fire erupted inside the warehouse. They said a fire sent columns of white smoke rising into the air, followed by the explosion." Their accounts were confirmed by several videos filmed by bystanders.<ref>{{cite news |title=Explosion in Yemen Warehouse Kills at Least 13, Including 7 Children |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/07/world/middleeast/yemen-explosion-warehouse.html |accessdate=8 April 2019 |agency=Nytimes |newspaper=nytimes.com |date=7 April 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/un-decries-killing-of-7-children-in-yemen-explosion/2019/04/08/100e26f8-5a00-11e9-98d4-844088d135f2_story.html|title=Yemenis recount horror of mysterious blast in capital|author=The Washington Post|date=8 April 2019}}</ref>
