=== Cross-border fighting ===
{{main|Saudi Arabian–Yemeni border conflict (2015–present)}}

=== Ground combat ===
{{See also|Battle of Aden (2015)|Conflict in Najran, Jizan and Asir|Battle of Taiz (2015–present)}}
On 3 April, [[CNN]] cited an unnamed Saudi source who claimed that Saudi special forces were on the ground in and around [[Aden]], "coordinating and guiding" the resistance.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/04/03/middleeast/yemen-saudi-forces/index.html|publisher=CNN|title=Saudi special forces help oppose Houthi rebels in Yemen, source says|date=3 April 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref> The Saudi government officially declined to comment on whether it had [[special forces]], with Saudi Ambassador to the United States [[Adel al-Jubeir]] saying on 2 April that Saudi Arabia had no "formal" troops in Aden.<ref name="remove"/>

The Battle of Aden came to an end with pro-Hadi forces again seized control of Aden port and moving into the city's commercial center.<ref name="Mohammed Mukhashaf">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/07/15/us-yemen-security-aden-idUSKCN0PP16I20150715|work=Reuters|title=Saudi-backed Yemen forces take Aden port from Houthis: residents|author= Mohammed Mukhashaf|date=16 July 2015|accessdate=16 July 2015}}</ref><ref name="Glen Carey">{{cite news|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-07-16/saudi-backed-forces-in-yemen-battle-to-take-districts-in-aden|publisher=Bloomberg|title=Saudi-Backed Forces in Yemen Claim Victories in Aden Battle|author= Glen Carey|date=17 July 2015|accessdate=17 July 2015}}</ref> On 22 July, pro-Hadi forces had retaken full control of Aden, and the Aden Airport was reopened. In late July, an offensive launched by pro-Hadi forces drove Houthi forces out of the towns neighboring Aden.<ref name="offensive"/>

On 4 September a Houthi [[OTR-21 Tochka]] missile [[September 2015 Ma'rib Toshka missile attack|hit an ammunition dump at a military base in Safer]] in Ma'rib Governorate killing 52 UAE, 10 Saudi and 5 Bahraini soldiers. The Safer base was being built up by coalition forces for a push against Sanaa.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34163982|title=Yemen crisis: UAE launches fresh Yemen attacks|work=BBC News|date=5 September 2015|access-date=6 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.thenational.ae/world/middle-east/marib-province-is-crucial-to-coalition-victory-in-yemen|title=Marib province is crucial to coalition victory in Yemen|work=The National|date=7 September 2015|access-date=7 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.thenational.ae/uae/emirati-serviceman-dies-during-yemen-ground-offensive|title=Emirati serviceman dies during Yemen ground offensive|work=The National|date=14 September 2015|access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref> "It was the deadliest single attack on coalition soldiers since the start of its operation against Houthi rebels in March" Asseri said.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/09/05/middleeast/yemen-weapons-depot-attack/|title=Saudi-led coalition strikes back at Houthis|last=Gray|first=Melissa|date=5 September 2015|publisher=CNN}}</ref> The attacked was the highest casualty loss in the history of the UAE military.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/09/05/us-yemen-security-idUSKCN0R507Y20150905|title=Coalition attacks Yemen capital after UAE, Saudi soldiers killed|work=[[Reuters]]|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref> Qatar deployed 1000 troops to Yemen after the incident.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/09/qatar-deploys-1000-ground-troops-fight-yemen-150907043020594.html|title=Qatar deploys 1,000 ground troops to fight in Yemen|author=[[Al Jazeera]] and agencies|date=7 September 2015|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]}}</ref>

By 8 September it was reported that the Saudi-led forces deployed in Yemen exceeded 10,000 troops and included 30 [[Boeing AH-64 Apache|AH-64 Apache]] attack helicopters.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.arabianbusiness.com/number-of-saudi-led-coalition-troops-in-yemen-rises-10-000--605525.html|title=Number of Saudi-led coalition troops in Yemen 'rises to 10,000' |agency=[[Reuters]] |newspaper=[[Arabian Business]] |date=8 September 2015|access-date=9 September 2015}}</ref>

On 14 December media reported a Houthi & Saleh Forces [[December 2015 Taiz missile attack|missile attack at a Saudi military camp south-west of the besieged city of Taiz]],<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.alaraby.co.uk/english/news/2015/12/14/dozens-of-gulf-troops-dead-in-yemen-rocket-attack|title=Gulf troops dead in Yemen rocket attack, sources |publisher=alaraby.co.uk|date=14 December 2015|access-date=8 February 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0TX0FW20151214|title=Two top Gulf commanders killed in Yemen rocket strike: sources |work=[[Reuters]]|date=14 December 2015|access-date=8 February 2016}}</ref> while sources confirmed the killings of over 150 coalition soldiers including 23 Saudi troops, 9 UAE officers and soldiers, 7 Moroccan soldiers and 42 Blackwater troops.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.ibtimes.com/saudi-coalition-houthi-rebels-intensify-attacks-yemen-ahead-proposed-ceasefire-2223830|title=Saudi Coalition, Houthi Rebels Intensify Attacks in Yemen Ahead of Proposed Ceasefire |publisher=Financial News|date=14 December 2015|access-date=8 February 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.moroccoworldnews.com/2015/12/175077/seven-moroccan-soldiers-reportedly-killed-in-yemen/|title=even Moroccan Soldiers Reportedly Killed in Yemen |publisher=Morocco World News|date=14 December 2015|access-date=8 February 2016}}</ref>

On 19 December 2015, reported clashes leaves over 40 Houthi rebels and 35 government loyalists dead, with dozens wounded on both sides.<ref>[http://time.com/4156068/fierce-fighting-in-yemen-kills-at-least-75/? "Fierce Fighting in Yemen kills at Least 75]. ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]''.</ref>

In June 2018, anti-Houthi forces led by Saudi Arabia and the [[United Arab Emirates]] assaulted the port of [[Al Hudaydah|Hudaydah]],<ref>"[https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/13/world/middleeast/yemen-al-hudaydah-assault-saudi-coalition.html Arab Coalition Attacks Yemeni City in Bid to Oust Rebels]". ''The New York Times''. 13 June 2018.</ref> in an effort to dislodge Houthi forces.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-deepens-role-in-yemen-fight-offers-gulf-allies-airstrike-target-assistance-1528830371 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20180613000241/https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-deepens-role-in-yemen-fight-offers-gulf-allies-airstrike-target-assistance-1528830371 |archive-date=13 June 2018 |newspaper=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |first=Dion |last=Nissenbam |title=U.S. Deepens Role in Yemen Fight, Offers Gulf Allies Airstrike-Target Assistance}}</ref>

Saudi Arabia faced growing criticism for the Saudi-led naval and air blockade, which effectively isolated the country.<ref name="NYT_2015-05-12_CFY">{{cite news |last1=Kalfood |first1=Mohammed Ali |last2=Fahim |first2=Kareem |title=A Cease-Fire in Yemen, but Fighting Is Persistent |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=12 May 2015 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/05/13/world/middleeast/iranian-cargo-ship-heads-toward-yemen-and-saudi-blockade.html|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e8Q7sdIs?url=http://www.nytimes.com/2015/05/13/world/middleeast/iranian-cargo-ship-heads-toward-yemen-and-saudi-blockade.html?_r=1 |archivedate=29 December 2015 |url-status=live }} ((Printed version: ''The New York Times'', 13 May 2015, page A10 of the New York edition)).</ref>

A "military source and pro-Hadi militiamen" told the AFP on 26 April that coalition warships were participating in the shelling of Aden.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/least-27-killed-south-yemen-fighting-102831816.html |title=Clashes rage in Yemen as calls for peace talks grow |date=26 April 2015 |work=[[Yahoo! News]] |agency=Agence France-Presse}}</ref>

On 30 April, the Iranian navy announced it had deployed two destroyers to the Gulf of Aden to "ensure the safety of commercial ships of our country against the threat of pirates", according to a rear admiral.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/iran-says-warships-entrance-key-yemen-strait-130223125.html|title=Iran says warships at entrance to key Yemen strait |date=30 April 2015 |work=[[Yahoo! News]] |agency=Agence France-Presse}}</ref> According to the same source, the deployment was scheduled to last until mid-June. Iran's deputy foreign minister, Hossein Amir-Abdollahian, told state-run [[Tasnim News Agency]] that "others will not be allowed to put our shared security at risk with military adventures".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/02/yemen-security-iran-idUSL5N0XT08L20150502|work=[[Reuters]]|title=Iran pledges to protect shared security interests with Yemen -Tasnim|date=2 May 2015|access-date=2 May 2015}}</ref>

=== Scale and participation of Saudi-led coalition members ===
[[Pakistan]] was called on by Saudi Arabia to join the coalition, but its parliament voted to maintain neutrality.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.geo.tv/article-180993-Parliament-passes-resolution-for-neutrality-in-Yemen-conflict|title=Parliament passes resolution for neutrality in Yemen conflict – PAKISTAN – geo.tv|date=10 April 2015|access-date=15 April 2015}}</ref> In February 2016 [[Academi]], the security firm withdraw from front-line duties in the Yemen campaign.<ref name="arwa1">{{cite web|url=http://arwarights.org/foreign-mercenaries-file |title=Use of Mercenaries by the Saudi-led Coalition to Violate Human Rights in Yemen and Impede the Exercise of the Yemeni People's Right to Self-determination|work=Arabian Right Watch Association|access-date=15 June 2020}}</ref> Qatar was suspended from the coalition due to the [[2017 Qatar diplomatic crisis]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.business-standard.com/article/international/gulf-rift-deepens-saudi-suspends-qatar-troops-involvement-in-yemen-war-117060500280_1.html|title=Gulf rift deepens: Saudi suspends Qatar troops' involvement in Yemen war|last=ANI|date=5 June 2017 |newspaper=Business Standard |accessdate=30 October 2017}}</ref> [[Morocco]] ended their participation in 2019 due to deterioration of [[Morocco–Saudi Arabia relations]]<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.news24.com/Africa/News/morocco-suspends-participation-in-saudi-led-war-in-yemen-20190208|title=Morocco suspends participation in Saudi-led war in Yemen|last=Aljazeera|date=8 February 2019 |newspaper=news24 |accessdate=1 August 2019}}</ref> followed by [[United Arab Emirates]] in July 2019 amid possible tensions with Iran on the Persian Gulf and differences with Saudi Arabia.<ref name="auto1"/> Sudan announced its decision to reduce troops commitment from 15,000 to 5,000 in early December 2019.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-sudan-politics-idUKKBN1YC0HX|title=Sudan says it has reduced troops in Yemen to 5,000|newspaper=Reuters|date=8 December 2019|via=uk.reuters.com}}</ref>

The Saudi-led campaign has received [[International reactions to the Saudi-led intervention in Yemen (2015–present)|widespread criticism]] and had a dramatic worsening effect on the humanitarian situation in Yemen, that reached the level of a "humanitarian disaster"<ref name="auto"/> or "humanitarian catastrophe".<ref name="un-org_2015-07-28_DCN"/><ref name="ECHAO_2015-12-14_ECS"/><ref name="BBCNews_2015-08-19_YCH"/> After the Saudi-led coalition declared the entire [[Saada Governorate]] a military target, the UN's Humanitarian Coordinator for Yemen and Human Rights Watch expressed concern that the bombing there was unnecessarily harming civilians.<ref name="ReutersUS_2015-05-09_SLS">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/09/us-yemen-security-saudi-un-idUSKBN0NU0PN20150509|title=Saudi-led strikes in Yemen break international law: U.N. coordinator|last=Miles|first=Tom|date=9 May 2015|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YQ90PbP8?url=http://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/09/us-yemen-security-saudi-un-idUSKBN0NU0PN20150509|archivedate=10 May 2015|url-status=live|publisher=Reuters U.S.}}</ref><ref name="OCHAYemen_2015-05-09_SBH">{{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/HC%20Statement%20on%20Yemen%209%20May%202015.pdf|title=Statement by the Humanitarian Coordinator for Yemen, Johannes Van Der Klaauw (9 May 2015)|date=9 May 2015|publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affair, UN Humanitarian Coordinator in Yemen|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YQIG6Yhe?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/HC%20Statement%20on%20Yemen%209%20May%202015.pdf|archivedate=10 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> On 1 July UN declared for Yemen a "level-three" emergency—the highest UN emergency level—for a period of six months.<ref name="UNOCHA_2015-11-22_2HNO">{{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/2016-humanitarian-needs-overview-enar|title=2016 Humanitarian Needs Overview|date=22 November 2015|publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs|via=[[ReliefWeb]]|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dHFRb9fu?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/2016-humanitarian-needs-overview|archivedate=24 November 2015|url-status=live}}; PDF: {{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/2016_HNO_English_%20FINAL.pdf|title=2016 Humanitarian Needs Overview|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dHFXhhD3?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/2016_HNO_English_%20FINAL.pdf|archivedate=24 November 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="unocha-org_2015-07-01_HER">{{cite web|url=http://www.unocha.org/top-stories/all-stories/yemen-highest-emergency-response-level-declared-six-months|title=Yemen: highest emergency response level declared for six months|date=1 July 2015|publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]]|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150702080509/http://www.unocha.org/top-stories/all-stories/yemen-highest-emergency-response-level-declared-six-months|archivedate=2 July 2015|url-status=dead|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> Human rights groups repeatedly blamed the Saudi-led military coalition for killing civilians and destroying health centres and other infrastructure with airstrikes.<ref name="NYT_2015-12-22_MAY"/> The de facto [[blockade]] left 78% (20&nbsp;million) of the Yemeni population in urgent need of food, water and medical aid. Aid ships are allowed, but the bulk of commercial shipping, on which the country relies, is blocked.<ref name="Borger">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jun/05/saudi-led-naval-blockade-worsens-yemen-humanitarian-disaster|title=Saudi-led naval blockade leaves 20&nbsp;m Yemenis facing humanitarian disaster|last=Borger|first=Julian |authorlink=Julian Borger |work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> In one incident, coalition jets prevented an [[Iranian Red Crescent]] plane from landing by bombing [[Sana'a International Airport|Sanaʽa International Airport]]'s runway, which blocked aid delivery by air.<ref name="The Guardian">{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/28/aid-flights-to-yemen-blocked-after-saudi-arabia-bombs-airport-runway|title=Aid flights to Yemen blocked after Saudi Arabian jets bomb airport runway|work=[[The Guardian]]}}</ref> As of 10 December, more than 2,500,000 people had been [[Internally displaced person|internally displaced]] by the fighting.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-12-10_TFP6R"/> Many countries evacuated more than 23,000 foreign citizens from Yemen.<ref name="Kumar">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/06/world/asia/india-tries-evacuating-citizens-in-yemen.html|title=India Tries Evacuating Citizens in Yemen|last1=Kumar|first1=Hari|date=5 April 2015|work=[[The New York Times]]|last2=Barry|first2=Ellen}}</ref><ref name="BBC News">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32173811|title=Yemen crisis: China evacuates citizens and foreigners from Aden|date=3 April 2015|work=BBC News}}</ref><ref name="IOM_UNHCR_2015-12-15_RFM">{{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/regional-refugee-and-migrant-response-impact-yemen-crisis-15-december-2015-enar|title=Regional refugee and Migrant Response: Impact of the Yemen Crisis, 15 December 2015 [EN/AR]|date=15 December 2015|publisher=International Organization for Migration, UN High Commissioner for Refugees|via=[[ReliefWeb]]|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e99RlIYv?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/regional-refugee-and-migrant-response-impact-yemen-crisis-15-december-2015-enar|archivedate=29 December 2015|url-status=live}}; PDF: {{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/YemenSituationfactsheet20151215.pdf|title=Regional refugee and Migrant Response: Impact of the Yemen Crisis, 15 December 2015 [EN/AR]|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e99xIFcm?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/YemenSituationfactsheet20151215.pdf|archivedate=29 December 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> More than 1,000,000 people fled Yemen for [[Saudi Arabia]],<ref name="arabnews.com">{{cite news|url=http://www.arabnews.com/saudi-arabia/news/843191|title=KSA shelters 1 million Yemeni refugees|date=30 November 2015|newspaper=[[Arab News]]}}</ref> [[Djibouti]], [[Somalia]], [[Ethiopia]], [[Sudan]] and [[Oman]].<ref name="IOM_UNHCR_2015-12-15_RFM"/> The war has caused a humanitarian crisis, including a [[Famine in Yemen|famine]] which has threatened over 17 million people, as well as an [[2016–17 Yemen cholera outbreak|outbreak of cholera]] which has infected hundreds of thousands.

On 13 April 2015, HRW wrote that some airstrikes were in apparent violation of the [[Law of war|laws of war]], such as 30 March attack on a displaced-persons camp in Mazraq that struck a medical facility and a market.<ref name="HRW_2015-04-13_CCH">{{cite web |title=Saudi Coalition/US: Curb Civilian Harm in Yemen |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/13/saudi-coalitionus-curb-civilian-harm-yemen |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=13 April 2015 |access-date=7 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YM3xkrhp?url=http://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/13/saudi-coalitionus-curb-civilian-harm-yemen |archivedate=7 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> Other incidents noted by HRW that had been deemed as indiscriminate or disproportionate or "in violation of the laws of war" were: a strike on a dairy factory outside the Red Sea port of Hodaida (31 civilian deaths);<ref name="HRW_2015-04-16_FAK">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Factory Airstrike Killed 31 Civilians – Saudi-Led, US-Backed Attack Raises Laws-of-War Concerns |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/15/yemen-factory-airstrike-killed-31-civilians |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=16 April 2015 |access-date=11 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YReY2gXI?url=http://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/15/yemen-factory-airstrike-killed-31-civilians |archivedate=11 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> a strike that destroyed a humanitarian aid warehouse of the international aid organization Oxfam in Saada;<ref name="HRW_2015-04-23_WST">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Warehouse Strike Threatens Aid Delivery – Inquiry Still Needed If Saudi-Led Bombing Campaign Ends |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/22/yemen-warehouse-strike-threatens-aid-delivery |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=23 April 2015 |access-date=9 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YOg2D59t?url=http://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/22/yemen-warehouse-strike-threatens-aid-delivery |archivedate=9 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> and the coalition's blockade that kept out fuel.<ref name="HRW_2015-05-11_CBD">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Coalition Blocking Desperately Needed Fuel – Tankers Wait Offshore as Civilians Go Without Water, Electricity |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/05/10/yemen-coalition-blocking-desperately-needed-fuel |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=11 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YRaXE0wz?url=http://www.hrw.org/news/2015/05/10/yemen-coalition-blocking-desperately-needed-fuel |archivedate=11 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> On 30 June 2015, HRW reported that several airstrikes were in clear violation of international law. The report confirmed 59 (including 14 women and 35 children) civilian deaths in Saada between 6 April and 11 May. The report also highlighted attacks on 6 civilian homes as well as five markets that were deliberate attacks.<ref name="mcclatchydc.com">{{cite news |url=http://www.mcclatchydc.com/news/nation-world/world/article25835662.html|title=Saudi airstrikes in Yemen violate laws of war, rights group says|publisher=[[The McClatchy Company|McClatchy DC]] |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

In February 2016, [[Amnesty International]] (AI) reported that it had investigated the circumstances and impact of more than 30 air strikes of the Saudi Arabia-led coalition forces in Sanaʽa, Hodeidah, Hajjah and Sa'da. They believed that the coalition was intentionally striking civilian targets.<ref name="AI_2016-02-18_UHR">{{cite web |title=Yemen: The UN Human Rights Council must address violations and abuses against civilians in Yemen conflict |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/documents/mde31/3390/2016/en/ |publisher=Amnesty International |date=18 February 2016 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fRatO6gC?url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/documents/mde31/3390/2016/en/ |archivedate=20 February 2016 |url-status=live}} Index number: MDE 31/3390/2016 ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=https://www.amnesty.org/download/Documents/MDE3133902016ENGLISH.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fRb2WgBl?url=https://www.amnesty.org/download/Documents/MDE3133902016ENGLISH.pdf |archivedate=20 February 2016 |url-status=live}})</ref> On 24 April 2015, Amnesty International said that airstrikes hit five densely populated areas (Sa'dah, Sanaʽa, Hodeidah, Hajjah and Ibb), and "raise concerns about compliance with the rules of international humanitarian law."<ref name="AI_2015-04-24_RAT">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Relentless airstrikes that have left hundreds of civilians dead must be investigated |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/articles/news/2015/04/yemen-investigate-relentless-airstrikes-that-have-left-hundreds-of-civilians-dead/ |publisher=Amnesty International |date=24 April 2015 |access-date=12 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YT8xuO0U?url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/articles/news/2015/04/yemen-investigate-relentless-airstrikes-that-have-left-hundreds-of-civilians-dead/ |archivedate=12 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="AI_2015-05-08_MEH">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Mounting evidence of high civilian toll of Saudi-led airstrikes |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/articles/news/2015/05/yemen-mounting-evidence-of-high-civilian-toll-of-saudi-led-airstrikes/ |publisher=Amnesty International |date=8 May 2015 |access-date=12 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YSxJL2Z7?url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/articles/news/2015/05/yemen-mounting-evidence-of-high-civilian-toll-of-saudi-led-airstrikes/ |archivedate=12 May 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> Their research indicates that there were at least 97 civilian deaths, including 33 children, and 157 civilians were wounded.<ref name="AI_2015-04-24_RAT"/>

According to [[Farea Al-Muslim]], direct war crimes were committed during the conflict; for example, an [[Internally displaced person|IDP(Internally displaced person)]] camp was hit by a Saudi airstrike, while Houthis sometimes prevented aid workers from giving aid.<ref>{{cite news |last=Kasinof|first=Laura|title=How Yemen's Civil Conflict Turned into a Regional Proxy War |url=http://www.thenation.com/article/206161/how-yemens-civil-conflict-turned-regional-proxy-war|work=[[The Nation]]}}</ref> The UN and human rights groups discussed the possibility that war crimes may have been committed by Saudi Arabia during the air campaign.<ref>{{cite news |title=Human Rights Watch: Saudi-Led Coalition Bombing Yemen with Banned U.S.-Made Cluster Munitions|url=http://www.democracynow.org/2015/5/5/human_rights_watch_saudi_led_coalition|date=5 May 2015}}</ref>

US Representative [[Ted Lieu]] has criticized the Saudi-led attacks on Yemen: "Some of these strikes look like war crimes to me, and I want to get answers as to why the US appears to be assisting in the execution of war crimes in Yemen."<ref name="lieu">{{cite news |last=Norton |first=Ben |date=17 March 2016 |title='Look like war crimes to me': Congressman raises concerns over U.S. support for Saudi war in Yemen |url= http://www.salon.com/2016/03/17/look_like_war_crimes_to_me_congressman_raises_concerns_over_u_s_support_for_saudi_war_in_yemen/ |work=[[Salon (website)|Salon]] |accessdate= 12 October 2016 }}</ref>

In March 2017, [[Human Rights Watch]] (HRW) reported that "Since the start of the current conflict, at least 4,773 civilians had been killed and 8,272 wounded, the majority by coalition airstrikes.... Human Rights Watch has documented 62 apparently unlawful coalition airstrikes, some of which may amount to war crimes, that have killed nearly 900 civilians, and documented seven indiscriminate attacks by Houthi-Saleh forces in Aden and Taizz that killed 139 people, including at least eight children."<ref>[https://www.hrw.org/news/2017/03/26/yemen-attack-refugee-boat-likely-war-crime "Yemen: Attack on Refugee Boat Likely War Crime"]. [[Human Rights Watch]]. 26 March 2017.</ref>

In an April 2020 report, the [[Human Rights Watch]] pointed out that the war crimes committed by [[Saudi Arabia]] and [[United Arab Emirates]] in [[Yemen]] go unmentioned. The countries have been held responsible for most number of child casualties and illegal attacks on schools.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/04/10/uns-timid-responses-war-crimes-against-children|title=The UN's Timid Responses to War Crimes Against Children|accessdate=10 April 2020|website=Human Rights Watch}}</ref>

=== Declaring the entire governorate of Sa'ada a military target ===
On 8 May 2015, a spokesperson for the Saudi-led coalition declared the entire city of [[Sa'dah]], with a population of around 50,000 people, a military target. According to [[Human Rights Watch]]: "This not only violated the laws-of-war prohibition against placing civilians at particular risk by treating a number of separate and distinct military objectives as a single military target, but possibly also the prohibition against making threats of violence whose purpose is to instill terror in the civilian population."<ref name="HRW Targeting Saada">{{cite web |date=30 June 2015 |title=Targeting Saada: Unlawful Coalition Airstrikes on Saada City in Yemen |publisher=[[Human Rights Watch]] |url=https://www.hrw.org/report/2015/06/30/targeting-saada/unlawful-coalition-airstrikes-saada-city-yemen}}</ref>

[[Human Rights Watch]] compiled the names and ages of some of the people killed in Saada City between 6 April and 11 May. Of the 59 people they found information on, 35 were children and 14 were women.<ref name="HRW Targeting Saada"/> The organisation's analysis of air-strike locations in Sa'dah showed that bombs fell across the city including near markets, schools and hospitals.<ref name="HRW Targeting Saada"/>

U.N. [[Humanitarian Coordinator]] for Yemen, Johannes van der Klaauw, agreed that the Saud-led coalition's actions breached international humanitarian law.<ref name="ReutersUS_2015-05-09_SLS"/><ref name="OCHAYemen_2015-05-09_SBH"/> "The indiscriminate bombing of populated areas, with or without prior warning, is in contravention of international humanitarian law," he said.<ref name="edition.cnn.com"/> He added that he was concerned that "scores of civilians were reportedly killed and thousands were forced to flee their homes after the coalition declared the entire governate a military target."

[[Save the Children]]'s Country Director in Yemen, Edward Santiago, said that the "indiscriminate attacks after the dropping of leaflets urging civilians to leave Sa'ada raises concerns about the possible pattern being established in breach of International Humanitarian Law. Warning civilians does not exonerate the coalition from their obligation to protect civilians and civilian infrastructure, and we have seen in the last days that the warnings have not been enough to spare civilian lives. At the same time, people are largely unable to flee for safety because of the de facto [[Blockade of Yemen|blockade]] imposed by the coalition leading to severe fuel shortages."<ref name="STC_2015-05-10_AAC">{{cite web |title=Aid Agencies Call For an Immediate and Permanent Cease Fire as an Additional 70,000 People Flee Coalition Airstrikes in Northern Yemen |url=http://www.savethechildren.org/site/apps/nlnet/content2.aspx?c=8rKLIXMGIpI4E&b=9241315&ct=14661497 |publisher=Save the Children |date=10 May 2015 |access-date=12 May 2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YSJSbBZj?url=http://www.savethechildren.org/site/apps/nlnet/content2.aspx?c=8rKLIXMGIpI4E&b=9241315&ct=14661497 |archivedate=11 May 2015 |url-status=dead }}</ref>

=== Attacks on facilities run by aid organizations ===
Since the Saudi-led coalition began military operations against Ansar Allah on 26 March 2015, Saudi-led coalition airstrikes unlawfully struck hospitals and other facilities run by aid organizations, according to Human Rights Watch.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/> [[Médecins Sans Frontières]] (MSF) medical facilities in Yemen were attacked four times in three months.<ref name="MSF_2016-01-25_HFU"/> On 26 October 2015, HRW documented six Saudi-led airstrikes which bombed a MSF hospital in Haydan district (Sa'dah Governorate), wounding two patients.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/><ref name="MSF_2016-01-25_HFU">{{cite web | title=Yemen: Health facilities under attack – MSF wants answers – Access to health care for people affected by war must be guaranteed | url=http://www.msf.org/article/yemen-health-facilities-under-attack-msf-wants-answers | publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières | date=30 June 2015 | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eo9lOVEZ?url=http://www.msf.org/article/yemen-health-facilities-under-attack-msf-wants-answers | archivedate=25 January 2016 | url-status=live}}</ref><ref>[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/oct/27/yemen-hospital-hit-by-saudi-led-airstrikes "Airstrikes hit Médecins Sans Frontières hospital in Yemen"]. ''[[The Guardian]]''. 27 October 2015.</ref> A Saudi-led coalition airstrike then hit a MSF mobile clinic on 2 December 2015, in Al Houban district (Taizz). Eight people were wounded, including two MSF staff members, and one other civilian nearby was killed. On 10 January 2016, six people were killed and seven wounded when a hospital in Sa'ada was hit by a projectile.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/><ref name="MSF_2016-01-25_HFU"/> MSF said it could not confirm whether the hospital was hit in an air strike by warplanes of the Saudi-led coalition, or by a rocket fired from the ground, and at least one other landed nearby.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/><ref>{{cite news | title=Yemen crisis: MSF-backed hospital hit by missile | url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-35276253 | work=BBC News | date=10 January 2016 | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eSbsTjR9?url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-35276253 | archivedate=11 January 2016 | url-status=live}}</ref> On 21 January 2016, an MSF ambulance was hit by an airstrike. Seven people were killed and dozens were wounded.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Saudi Warnings No Free Pass to Attack – Coalition Should Assist, Not Threaten, Aid Agencies | url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/02/17/yemen-saudi-warnings-no-free-pass-attack | publisher=Human Rights Watch | date=17 February 2016 | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fN6QKC02?url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/02/17/yemen-saudi-warnings-no-free-pass-attack | archivedate=17 February 2016 | url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="MSF_2016-01-25_HFU"/>

MSF's director of operations Raquel Ayora said: "The way war is being waged in Yemen is causing enormous suffering and shows that the warring parties do not recognise or respect the protected status of hospitals and medical facilities. We witness the devastating consequences of this on people trapped in conflict zones on a daily basis. Nothing has been spared—not even hospitals, even though medical facilities are explicitly protected by international humanitarian law."<ref name="MSF_2016-01-25_HFU"/>

The Saudi embassy in London, in early February 2016, advised United Nations and other aid organizations to move their offices and staff away from "regions where the Houthi militias and their supporters are active and in areas where there are military operations". It claimed this was in order to "protect the international organizations and their employees".<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/> The UN refused to pull out the humanitarian aid workers and protested against the Saudi demands.<ref name="euronews-com_2016-02-17_YSS">{{cite news | first=Robert | last=Hackwill | title=Yemen struggles to see way out of war | url=http://www.euronews.com/2016/02/17/yemen-struggles-to-see-way-out-of-war/ | publisher=euronews.com | date=17 February 2016 | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fQUgVzV6?url=http://www.euronews.com/2016/02/17/yemen-struggles-to-see-way-out-of-war/ | archivedate=20 February 2016 | url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="de-euronews-com_2016-02-17_KZS">{{cite news | title=Wegen Jemen-Krieg: Kontroverse zwischen Saudi-Arabien und UN | url=http://de.euronews.com/2016/02/17/wegen-jemen-krieg-kontroverse-zwischen-saudi-arabien-und-un/ | publisher=de.euronews.com | date=17 February 2016 | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fO7Rgzfo?url=http://de.euronews.com/2016/02/17/wegen-jemen-krieg-kontroverse-zwischen-saudi-arabien-und-un/ | archivedate=18 February 2016 | language=german |url-status=live}}</ref> On 7 February 2016, the UN humanitarian chief Stephen O'Brien wrote to Saudi Arabia's UN Ambassador Abdallah al-Mouallimi, pointing out that Saudi Arabia is obligated under international law to permit access, and has "duty of care obligations under the conduct of military operations for all civilians, including humanitarian workers".<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/>

HRW declared, on 17 February 2016, that Saudi Arabia's warnings to stay away were insufficient to fulfil their legal obligations to protect aid stations and their occupants. James Ross, Legal and Policy Director at HRW, said: "A warning is no justification for an unlawful airstrike. They can't shift the blame for shirking their responsibility onto aid agencies that are struggling to address a deepening crisis."<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/>

After an air-strike on an MSF hospital in the Hajjah province on 15 August 2016, MSF announced the pulling of their staff from Saada and Hajjah provinces affecting 6 facilities. The group also complained that the results of previous investigations into hospital bombings by the Saudi-led coalition were never shared.<ref name="Almosawa">{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/08/19/world/middleeast/yemen-doctors-without-borders-hospitals.html|title=Doctors Without Borders Is Pulling Staff After Hospital Bombings in Yemen|last1=Almosawa|first1=Shuaib|date=18 August 2016|last2=Nordland|first2=Rod|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|issn=0362-4331|access-date=19 August 2016}}</ref>

=== Usage of cluster munitions ===
In early May 2015, [[Human Rights Watch]] accused Saudi Arabia of using US-supplied [[cluster munition]]s on at least two occasions. The Saudi military acknowledged using [[CBU-97 Sensor Fuzed Weapon|CBU-105 bombs]], but it claimed they were only employed against armoured vehicles and not in population centers.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/05/03/middleeast/yemen-hrw-cluster-munitions-saudi-arabia/|publisher=CNN|title=Report: Saudi Arabia used U.S.-supplied cluster bombs in Yemen|date=3 May 2015|access-date=4 May 2015}}</ref><ref name="NYT20150503SLG">{{cite news | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/05/03/world/middleeast/saudi-led-group-said-to-use-cluster-bombs-in-yemen.html| newspaper=[[The New York Times]] | first=Kareem | last=Fahim | title=Saudi-Led Group Said to Use Cluster Bombs in Yemen | date=3 May 2015}}</ref> Yemeni security officials claimed that cluster bombs were dropped in a civilian area of the Western suburbs of the Yemeni capital Sanaa. In an earlier statement, Saudi Arabia had denied that the Saudi-led military coalition was using cluster bombs at all.<ref name="auto2"/>

Internationally outlawed cluster bombs supplied by the USA were used by the Saudi-led military coalition and wounded civilians despite evidence of prior civilian casualties, based on multiple reports issued by [[HRW]].<ref>[http://edition.cnn.com/2016/02/29/politics/saudi-arabia-us-cluster-bombs-on-civilians/index.html "Rights group: Saudi Arabia used U.S. cluster bombs on civilians"]. [[CNN]], 29 February 2016.</ref>

On 8 January 2016, the UN Secretary General Ban Ki-moon announced that Saudi coalition use of cluster munitions could be a war crime.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="RTS_2016-01-08_UCB">{{cite news |last=Charbonneau |first=Louis |title=Use of cluster bombs in Yemen may be war crime: U.N. chief |work=[[Reuters]] |date=8 January 2016 |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-un-idUSKBN0UM23H20160108 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eR29nhQ3?url=http://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-un-idUSKBN0UM23H20160108 |archivedate=10 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> HRW condemned the Saudi-led coalition for the attacks saying: "The coalition's repeated use of cluster bombs in the middle of a crowded city suggests an intent to harm civilians, which is a war crime. These outrageous attacks show that the coalition seems less concerned than ever about sparing civilians from war's horrors."<ref name="HRW_2016-01-07_CDC"/> A week later, Amnesty International published new evidence that appeared to confirm reports of coalition forces using US-made cluster munitions on Sanaʽa on 6 January 2016.<ref name="AI_2016-01-15_NEC">{{cite web |title=Yemen: New evidence challenges coalition's denial it used cluster munitions in recent attack (Index number: MDE 31/3208/2016) |publisher=Amnesty International |date=15 January 2016 |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/documents/mde31/3208/2016/en/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eaAu2BAk?url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/documents/mde31/3208/2016/en/ |archivedate=16 January 2016 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/MDE3132082016ENGLISH.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eaB5ocg5?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/MDE3132082016ENGLISH.pdf |archivedate=16 January 2016 |url-status=live }}, {{cite web |title=original PDF |url=https://www.amnesty.org/download/Documents/MDE3132082016ENGLISH.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eaB0TghY?url=https://www.amnesty.org/download/Documents/MDE3132082016ENGLISH.pdf |archivedate=16 January 2016 |url-status=live }})</ref>

In December 2016, a Saudi spokesperson admitted that at least some of the coalition's cluster bombs were manufactured in the United Kingdom. British prime minister [[Theresa May]] refused to answer when asked in parliament when she first became aware that UK-made cluster bombs were being used.<ref>{{cite news |author=Rowena Mason |author2=Ewen MacAskill |date=19 December 2016 |title=Saudi Arabia admits it used UK-made cluster bombs in Yemen; Confirmation by Saudi-led coalition raises pressure on UK government which has refused to curb arms sales to Riyadh |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/dec/19/saudi-arabia-admits-use-uk-made-cluster-bombs-yemen|author2-link=Ewen MacAskill }}</ref>

[[Amnesty International]] has called on Saudi Arabia to destroy its stockpile of cluster bombs and accede to the International Convention on Cluster Munitions. It also asked the Saudi-led coalition to provide the United Nations with precise locations of cluster munition attacks.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Arabia: Immediately abandon all use of cluster munitions |date=19 December 2016 |publisher=[[Amnesty International]] |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2016/12/saudi-arabia-immediately-abandon-all-use-of-cluster-munitions}}</ref> The coalition has yet to do so.

In May 2019, Saudi Arabia's cargo ship Bahri-Yanbu was blocked from collecting weapons at the French [[Port of Le Havre]] by humanitarian groups. Later in the month, Italian union workers refused to load electricity generators on the ship and prevented it from docking, claiming that the weapons on-board would be used against civilians. Despite the protests, the ship docked.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.euronews.com/2019/05/21/italian-unions-refuse-to-load-saudi-ship-carrying-weapons-to-yemen|title=Italian unions refuse to load Saudi ship carrying weapons to Yemen|date=21 May 2019|publisher=Euronews|accessdate=21 May 2019}}</ref>

=== Calls for international independent investigations ===
A UN panel of experts said in a report for the UN Security Council in January 2016, which was leaked to ''The Guardian'', that the Saudi-led coalition had undertaken 119 sorties in Yemen that violated international humanitarian law.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI">{{cite news |last=MacAskill |first=Ewen |title=UN report into Saudi-led strikes in Yemen raises questions over UK role – Experts conclude Saudi-led coalition conducted widespread airstrikes against civilian targets in violation of international law |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |date=27 January 2016 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/27/un-report-into-saudi-led-strikes-in-yemen-raises-questions-over-uk-role |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6esB9N6T5?url=http://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/27/un-report-into-saudi-led-strikes-in-yemen-raises-questions-over-uk-role |archivedate=28 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="voanews-com_2016-01-28_UPA">{{cite web |title=UN Panel Alleges Violations of International Law in Yemen |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=26 January 2016 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/united-nations-panel-alleges-violations-international-law-yemen/3164380.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6esBLoiSS?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/united-nations-panel-alleges-violations-international-law-yemen/3164380.html |archivedate=28 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> The panel said it had "documented that the coalition had conducted airstrikes targeting civilians and civilian objects, in violation of international humanitarian law, including camps for internally displaced persons and refugees; civilian gatherings, including weddings; civilian vehicles, including buses; civilian residential areas; medical facilities; schools; mosques; markets, factories and food storage warehouses; and other essential civilian infrastructure, such as the airport in Sanaʽa, the port in Hudaydah and domestic transit routes". The report said: "Many attacks involved multiple airstrikes on multiple civilian objects. Of the 119 sorties, the panel identified 146 targeted objects. The panel also documented three alleged cases of civilians fleeing residential bombings and being chased and shot at by helicopters."<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/> While the UN experts were not allowed on the ground in Yemen, they studied satellite imagery of cities before and after attacks, that showed "extensive damage to residential areas and civilian objects".<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/><ref name="voanews-com_2016-01-28_UPA"/> The UN panel concluded that "civilians are disproportionately affected" by the fighting and deplored tactics that "constitute the prohibited use of starvation as a method of warfare".<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/> The report said: "The coalition's targeting of civilians through airstrikes, either by bombing residential neighbourhoods or by treating the entire cities of Sa'dah and Maran as military targets, is a grave violation of the principles of distinction, proportionality and precaution. In certain cases, the panel found such violations to have been conducted in a widespread and systematic manner."<ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/> The report called for an international commission, set up by the Security Council, that should "investigate reports of violations of international humanitarian law and human rights law in Yemen by all parties and to identify the perpetrators of such violations".<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/> Saudi Arabia had previously objected to an inquiry being set up.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC">{{cite news |title=UN panel calls for international inquiry in Yemen |agency=Agence France-Presse |publisher=ReliefWeb |date=27 January 2016 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/un-panel-calls-international-inquiry-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eqe81dHc?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/un-panel-calls-international-inquiry-yemen |archivedate=27 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Five days after the release of UN Panel of Experts report on Yemen, on 31 January 2016, the Saudi-led Arab coalition announced it had formed "an independent team of experts in international humanitarian law and weapons to assess the incidents and investigate the rules of engagement". The coalition said the objective was to "develop a clear and comprehensive report on each incident with the conclusions, lessons learned, recommendations and measures that should be taken" to spare civilians.<ref name="HRW_2016-02-17_SWN"/><ref name="AFP_2016-01-31_SLY">{{cite news |title=Saudi-led Yemen coalition announces probe into possible abuses |agency=Agence France-Presse |publisher=Reliefweb |date=31 January 2016 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/saudi-led-yemen-coalition-announces-probe-possible-abuses |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6exRpNN98?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/saudi-led-yemen-coalition-announces-probe-possible-abuses |archivedate=31 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 16 February 2016, [[Adama Dieng]], the U.N.'s [[Responsibility to protect#Special Advisors on the Prevention of Genocide and the Responsibility to Protect|Special Adviser on the Prevention of Genocide]], and [[Jennifer Welsh]], the [[Responsibility to protect#Special Advisors on the Prevention of Genocide and the Responsibility to Protect|Special Adviser on the Responsibility to Protect]], said in a joint statement: "We now expect that commitments by the Yemeni authorities and by Saudi Arabia to conduct credible and independent investigations into all alleged violations and provide reparations to victims will be swiftly implemented. It is imperative that the international community also gives immediate consideration to the most effective means of supporting this goal, including the possibility of establishing an international independent and impartial mechanism to support accountability in Yemen."<ref name="UN_2016-02-16_SAD">{{cite web |title=Statement by Adama Dieng, Special Adviser on the Prevention of Genocide and Jennifer Welsh, Special Adviser on the Responsibility to Protect, on the situation in Yemen (16 February 2016) |publisher=ReliefWeb |date=16 February 2016 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/statement-adama-dieng-special-adviser-prevention-genocide-and-jennifer-welsh-special |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fMujs0j6?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/statement-adama-dieng-special-adviser-prevention-genocide-and-jennifer-welsh-special |archivedate=17 February 2016 |url-status=live }} ({{cite press release |title=Statement by Adama Dieng, Special Adviser on the Prevention of Genocide and Jennifer Welsh, Special Adviser on the Responsibility to Protect, on the situation in Yemen |date=16 February 2016 |publisher=United Nations |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Microsoft%20Word%20-%202016-02-16%20OSAPG%20Statement%20on%20Yemen%20final.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fMuqlosr?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Microsoft%20Word%20-%202016-02-16%20OSAPG%20Statement%20on%20Yemen%20final.pdf |archivedate=17 February 2016 |url-status=live }})</ref>

On 19 September 2020, [[United Nations|UN]] report warned that the [[United Kingdom|UK]] and other countries of possibly providing arms to [[Saudi Arabia]] in terms of "aiding and assisting" the war crimes committed by the coalition in [[Yemen]]. The report warned of concerns regarding foreign nations supplying arms to parties of conflict in Yemen, blatantly disregarding documented patterns of severe violations of global humanitarian and human rights law regarding the conflict.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/uk-saudi-arabia-war-crimes-yemen-arms-exports-ban-un-b453921.html|title=UK could be 'aiding and assisting' Saudi Arabia war crimes by selling arms, UN report warns|accessdate=19 September 2020|website=Independent}}</ref>

===Alleged use of white phosphorus===
In September 2016, ''The Washington Post'' reported that Saudi Arabia "appears" to be using US-made [[white phosphorus munitions]] against Yemen, based on images and videos posted to social media. Under US regulations, white phosphorus is only allowed to be used to signal to other troops and to reduce visibility in open ground, creating a smoke-screen. It is not to be used to attack humans as it burns human flesh down to the bone, which is considered excessively cruel. A United States official said the department was looking into whether the Saudis used white phosphorus improperly.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Arabia appears to be using U.S.-supplied white phosphorus in its war in Yemen |author=Thomas Gibbons-Neff |date=19 September 2016 |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/checkpoint/wp/2016/09/19/saudi-arabia-appears-to-be-using-u-s-supplied-white-phosphorus-in-its-war-in-yemen/}}</ref>

=== UAE secret prisons ===
In October 2017, a Yemeni citizen died under "severe torture" inside a secret prison run by the United Arab Emirates in the south of Yemen. As videos showed, the body of Ahmed Dubba revealed disturbing signs of torture after it was released from Khanfar Prison. According to media reports, UAE forces in Yemen had carried out a detention campaign against religious scholars and preachers who opposed their presence in the country where prisoners were subject to physical and psychological torture. According to Yemeni rights group Sam, the issue of secret prisons in Yemen has become a regular phenomenon.<ref>{{cite news |date=30 September 2017 |title=Yemeni dies of torture in UAE run prison in Yemen |publisher=Middle East Monitor |url=https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20170930-yemeni-dies-of-torture-in-uae-run-prison-in-yemen/}}</ref>

===Targeting of wounded and medical personnel===
The United Nations alleged that the Saudi-led coalition had committed a war crime<ref name="Reuters Saudi violated">{{cite news |author=Michelle Nichols |date=20 October 2016 |title=Saudi coalition violated law with Yemen funeral strike: U.N. monitors |work=[[Reuters]] |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-saudi-un-idUSKCN12K2F1?il=0}}</ref> because the bombing was a 'double tap' attack. This is when the first bombing is followed by a second one soon after, which aims to attack the wounded, aid workers and medical personnel tending to them. The UN report said: "The second air strike, which occurred three to eight minutes after the first air strike, almost certainly resulted in more casualties to the already wounded and the first responders."<ref name="Reuters Saudi violated"/> Saudi Foreign Minister Adel al-Jubeir said that his government was being careful to abide by humanitarian law.<ref name="Reuters Saudi violated"/>

According to the [[Save the Children]] group, children have died as a result of Saudi Arabia delaying aid for Yemen by month.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Arabia delaying aid to Yemen is 'killing children', warns Save the Children; Saudi-led coalition accused of 'turning aid and commercial supplies into weapons of war' |author=Samuel Osborne |date=1 March 2017 |newspaper=[[The Independent]] |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/saudi-arabia-yemen-aid-delay-killing-children-save-the-children-warn-a7606411.html}}</ref>

===Use of child soldiers===
On late March 2019 the British newspaper ''[[The Mail on Sunday]]'' reported that British Special Forces are fighting on the same side as jihadists and militia which use child soldiers.<ref name="Wheeler">{{Cite web|url=https://www.plymouthherald.co.uk/news/uk-world-news/urgent-probe-royal-navy-special-2688497|title=Probe into Royal Navy Special Forces child soldiers claim|last1=Wheeler|first1=Richard|last2=Thomas|first2=Josh|date=2019-03-26|website=plymouthherald|access-date=2019-03-30|last3=Channon|first3=Max}}</ref> After the report, the shadow foreign secretary [[Emily Thornberry]], questioned these allegations in [[Parliament of the United Kingdom|the British parliament]] suggesting that the British forces may have been witnesses to war crimes, if the allegations were true. She claimed that as many as 40% of the soldiers in the Saudi coalition were children, a breach of international humanitarian law.<ref name="2019-03-27">{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2019/mar/27/serious-questions-over-sas-involvement-in-yemen-war|title='Serious' questions over SAS involvement in Yemen war|last=editor|first=Patrick Wintour Diplomatic|date=2019-03-27|work=The Guardian|access-date=2019-03-30|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> In response, the UK Foreign Office minister [[Mark Field]] called the allegations "very serious and well-sourced" and promised to get to the bottom of these allegations.<ref name="2019-03-27"/>

In April 2019 the Qatari-based news agency Aljazeera, reported, based in footage of the presence of child soldiers in the recruitment camps of the Saudi-UAE-led coalition. Children from 15 to 16 were recruited from poverty-driven Yemeni villages.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2019/03/exclusive-yemeni-child-soldiers-recruited-saudi-uae-coalition-190329132329547.html|title=Exclusive: Yemeni child soldiers recruited by Saudi-UAE coalition|website=www.aljazeera.com}}</ref>

In a controversial decision in 2019, that was opposed by many career professionals, the U.S. secretary of state waived the inclusion of Saudi Arabia on its annual list of countries that recruit child soldiers, even though it met all the criteria to be included. <ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/jun/18/mike-pompeo-saudi-arabia-yemen-sudan-child-soldiers|title=Pompeo blocks inclusion of Saudi Arabia on US child soldiers list|date=18 June 2019|via=www.theguardian.com}}</ref> Former deputy secretary of defense for the Middle East, [[Michael Mulroy]], said, "this is a glaring example of an OPAC signatory not adhering to the stipulations of their signed commitments. As an international community, we are not demanding 100 percent compliance, and that needs to change." <ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.mei.edu/publications/begin-children-child-soldier-numbers-doubled-middle-east-2019|title=Begin with the children: Child soldier numbers doubled in the Middle East in 2019|website=Middle East Institute}}</ref>

== Foreign involvement ==
{{main|Foreign involvement in the Yemeni Civil War}}
NATO powers such as the United Kingdom and the United States support the Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen primarily through arms sales and technical assistance.<ref name="bbc-com_2015-09-11_IYF">{{cite news |last=Gatehouse |first=Gabriel |title=Inside Yemen's forgotten war |work=BBC News |date=11 September 2015 |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34211979 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ciAUD4ey?url=http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34211979 |archivedate=1 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> France had also made recent military sales to Saudi Arabia.<ref name="HRW_2015-11-18_RBS">{{cite web | url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/11/18/us-reject-bomb-sales-saudi-arabia | archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dCxdWufn?url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/11/18/us-reject-bomb-sales-saudi-arabia | publisher=Human Rights Watch | date=18 November 2015 | title=US: Reject Bomb Sales to Saudi Arabia – Coalition Failure to Investigate Civilian Deaths in Airstrikes on Yemen |archivedate=21 November 2015 |url-status=live}}</ref> MSF emergency coordinator Karline Kleijer called the US, France and the UK part of the Saudi-led coalition, which imposed the weapons embargo and blocked all ships from entering Yemen with supplies.<ref name="theguardian-com_2015-11-09_CHG">{{cite news |last=Kleijer |first=Karline |title=Yemen: 'The children have a game called airstrike in which they fall to the ground' |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global-development-professionals-network/2015/nov/09/yemen-the-children-have-a-game-called-airstrike-in-which-they-fall-to-the-ground |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cy0GCNTv?url=http://www.theguardian.com/global-development-professionals-network/2015/nov/09/yemen-the-children-have-a-game-called-airstrike-in-which-they-fall-to-the-ground |date=9 November 2015 |archivedate=11 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> Rights groups have criticized the countries for supplying arms, and accuse the coalition of using [[cluster munition]]s, which are banned in most countries.<ref name="UK-RTS_2015-12-22_UBS">{{cite news |last=Nichols |first=Michelle |title=U.N. blames Saudi-led coalition for most attacks on Yemeni civilians |work=Reuters UK |date=22 December 2015 |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-yemen-security-un-idUKKBN0U51UZ20151222 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e1dGmEZF?url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-yemen-security-un-idUKKBN0U51UZ20151222 |archivedate=24 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> Oxfam pointed out that Germany, Iran, and Russia have also reportedly sold arms to the conflicting forces.<ref name="oxfam-org-uk_2015-09-11_UAS">{{cite web |title=UK arms sales fuelling Yemen crisis in potential breach of law says Oxfam |publisher=Oxfam UK |date=11 September 2015 |url=http://www.oxfam.org.uk/media-centre/press-releases/2015/09/uk-arms-sales-fuelling-yemen-crisis-in-potential-breach-of-law-says-oxfam |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6evkmD8Zp?url=http://www.oxfam.org.uk/media-centre/press-releases/2015/09/uk-arms-sales-fuelling-yemen-crisis-in-potential-breach-of-law-says-oxfam |archivedate=30 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> Tariq Riebl, head of programmes in Yemen for Oxfam, said, "it's difficult to argue that a weapon sold to Saudi Arabia would not in some way be used in Yemen," or "if it's not used in Yemen it enables the country to use other weapons in Yemen."<ref name="bbc-com_2015-09-11_IYF"/> Amnesty International urged the US and the UK to stop supplying arms to Saudi Arabia and to the Saudi-led coalition.<ref name="independent-co-uk_2015-10-08_AIU">{{cite news |last=Sandhu |first=Serina |title=Amnesty International urges Britain to stop supplying arms to Saudi Arabia – Airstrikes in Yemen have killed thousands of civilians |work=[[The Independent]] |date=8 October 2015 |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/amnesty-international-urges-britain-to-stop-supplying-arms-to-saudi-arabia-a6686611.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dECAZJCH?url=http://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/amnesty-international-urges-britain-to-stop-supplying-arms-to-saudi-arabia-a6686611.html |archivedate=22 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> On August 3, 2019, a United Nations report said the US, UK and France may be complicit in committing war crimes in Yemen by selling weapons and providing support to the Saudi-led coalition which is using the deliberate starvation of civilians as a tactic of warfare.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://therealnews.com/stories/un-report-on-yemen-us-uk-accomplices-to-atrocities-while-inaction-continues|title=UN Report on Yemen: US, UK Accomplices to Atrocities, While Inaction Continues|date= 4 September 2019|accessdate=4 September 2019|website=[[The Real News]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last= Wintour|first=Patrick|date=September 3, 2019 |title=UK, US and France may be complicit in Yemen war crimes – UN report|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/sep/03/uk-us-and-france-may-be-complicit-in-yemen-war-crimes-un-report|work=[[The Guardian]] |location= |access-date=September 4, 2019 }}</ref> Arms sale by [[United Kingdom]] to [[Saudi Arabia]] and the [[United Arab Emirates]] in 2019 reportedly soared by £1bn, i.e. 300%, in comparison to the figures in 2018. Andrew Smith of the [[Campaign Against Arms Trade]] condemned the increase and criticized the UK arms industry of being dominated by human rights abusers and dictatorships. UK-made fighter jets have been accused of causing catastrophic damage in [[Yemeni Civil War (2015–present)|Yemen]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/25/uk-arms-trade-repressive-regimes|title=Britain boosts arms sales to repressive regimes by £1bn|accessdate=25 April 2020|website=The Guardian}}</ref> According to a May 28, 2020 article by [[The New York Times]], the [[Donald Trump|Trump]] administration in January 2020 told lawmakers that it was planning to sell a cache of munitions to [[Saudi Arabia]], despite the kingdom's [[human rights]] record. Reportedly, the sale of the said $478 million, precision-guided missiles used in Yemen war to Saudi, and approval of licenses permitting [[Raytheon]] to expand manufacturing in Riyadh are objected by lawmakers in both, [[Democratic Party (United States)|Democrats]] and [[Republican Party (United States)|Republican]] parties.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/28/us/politics/congress-saudi-arabia-arms-sales.html|title=Trump Officials Consider Defying Congress to Sell More Weapons to Saudi Arabia|accessdate=28 May 2020|website=The New York Times}}</ref>

In early June 2020, the [[Government of France|French government]] published a report on the arms exports of 2019, where the sale of €1.4 billion arms was made to [[Saudi Arabia]]. [[Human Rights Watch]] urged the French authorities to halt any arms sale to Saudi, considering the country is accused in possible war crimes and human rights abuses in [[Yemen]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/06/10/france-should-halt-arms-exports-saudi-arabia-egypt|title=France Should Halt Arms Exports to Saudi Arabia, Egypt|accessdate=10 June 2020|website=Human Rights Watch}}</ref>In July 2020, Amnesty International revealed that France had promoted a private military center to train Saudi troops and backed it both, financially and politically. According to the report, France intended to train the Saudi soldiers in the operations of the latest versions of weapons that had already been used in the Yemeni conflict. The training center has been set up at the town of [[Commercy]] in [[Meuse (department)|Meuse]] with funds extracted from the French taxpayer's money, violating international treaties, as per Lebel.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rfi.fr/en/france/20200707-saudi-soldiers-are-training-in-military-camp-in-france-says-amnesty|title=Saudi soldiers are training in military camp in France, says Amnesty|accessdate=7 July 2020|website=RFI}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.dailysabah.com/world/mid-east/france-trains-saudi-soldiers-in-military-camp-to-wage-war-in-yemen-amnesty-international|title= France trains Saudi soldiers in military camp to wage war in Yemen: Amnesty International |accessdate= 4 October 2020|website=Daily Sabah}}</ref> In September 2020, [[Canada]] was listed among the countries, who contributed in fueling the [[Yemeni Civil War (2014–present)|Yemen Civil War]], by a [[United Nations]] panel. Following that, 39 human rights organizations, arms-control groups and labor unions, including the [[Public Service Alliance of Canada]], sent a joint letter to the Canadian Prime Minister [[Justin Trudeau]], urging for the country to end arms exports to [[Saudi Arabia]], which had been one of the crucial contributor to the humanitarian crisis causes in [[Yemen]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theglobeandmail.com/politics/article-trudeau-urged-to-end-arms-exports-to-saudi-arabia-after-canada-cited/|title=Trudeau urged to end arms exports to Saudi Arabia after Canada cited for fueling Yemen war|accessdate=17 September 2020|website=The Globe and Mail}}</ref>

According to official figures released by the [[Department for International Trade]](DIT), the [[United Kingdom]] has exported £11bn worth of arms in 2019, becoming the second highest arms exporter after [[United States]]. The UK traded arms despite June 2019 court ruling halting weapons sale to [[Saudi Arabia]] due to use in Yemen war causing the worst humanitarian crisis. In July 2020, Britain resumed arms sales to Saudi Arabia. Official figures of the weapons sale to Saudi Arabia were not included in the data, however, in 2019, 60% of the arms sales were made to Middle Eastern countries.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/oct/06/uk-remains-second-biggest-arms-exporter-with-11bn-of-orders|title=UK remains second biggest arms exporter with £11bn of orders|accessdate=6 October 2020|website=The Guardian}}</ref>

In October 2020, anti-arms trade campaigners legally challenged Britain’s arms sale to Saudi Arabia. The [[Campaign Against Arms Trade]] (CAAT) stated that UK-made weapons had been fueling a prolonged conflict in Yemen as the bombing by coalition led by Saudi Arabia has resulted in the killing of thousands of civilians over the past 5 years of war.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/oct/27/uk-faces-new-legal-challenge-over-arms-sales-to-saudi-arabia|title=UK faces new legal challenge over arms sales to Saudi Arabia|accessdate=27 October 2020|website=The Guardian}}</ref>

In late November 2020, Fourteen French human rights [[NGO]]s and humanitarian organisations urged the government to end its opacity on the sale of arms to [[Saudi Arabia]] and the [[United Arab Emirates]], in order to initiate parliamentary control. A December 2018 fact-finding mission on arms export control by co-rapporteurs and MPs, Jacques Maire and Michele Tabarot, was based on public opinion and mobilisation of NGOs against arms sale by the government to Saudi-led coalition, including UAE, which likely used it illicitly against Yemeni civilians. In the November 2020 dialogue, NGOs stressed over the significance of the Parliament’s duty to administer arms export by the French government to prevent its complicity in [[war crimes]] and events violating the international humanitarian law, specially in [[Yemen]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.fidh.org/en/region/europe-central-asia/france/call-for-parliamentary-control-over-french-arms-sales|title=A call for the establishment of parliamentary control over French arms sales|accessdate=26 November 2020|website=International Federation for Human Rights}}</ref>

|UN, Houthis
