A Houthi spokesman stated on 28 April 2015 that the airstrikes had killed 200 members of all pro-Houthi forces since the campaign started.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.globalpost.com/article/6530900/2015/04/28/20-dead-rebels-advance-heart-yemens-aden|title=20 dead as rebels advance in heart of Yemen's Aden|work=[[GlobalPost]]|url-status=live |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150704112207/http://www.globalpost.com/article/6530900/2015/04/28/20-dead-rebels-advance-heart-yemens-aden |archivedate= 4 July 2015}}</ref> In addition, UNICEF reported on 24 April 2015 that the strikes had killed 64 children.<ref name="hundredschildren"/>

Between 26 March and 21 April, ''[[The New York Times]]'' confirmed 18 airstrikes that resulted in civilian casualties.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/03/26/world/middleeast/geography-of-chaos-in-yemen-maps.html|title=Saudi-Backed Forces Gain Momentum|date=26 March 2015 |newspaper=[[The New York Times]]}}</ref>

According to the United Nations, between 26 March and 10 May 2015, the conflict, killed at least 828 Yemeni civilians, including 91 women and 182 children. One hundred and eighty-two were killed between 4 and 10 May alone, with most of those due to the airstrikes.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://thepeninsulaqatar.com/news/middle-east/337661/un-preparing-vast-aid-operation-in-yemen|title=UN preparing vast aid operation in Yemen|work=[[The Peninsula (newspaper)|The Peninsula]]}}</ref>
[[File:This neighborhood where more than 100 buildings have been damaged has brought attention to the plight of Yemeni blacks with neighboring communities coming to witness the damage - Sanaa - Oct-9-2015.png|thumb|240px|Yemeni capital Sanaa after airstrikes, 9 October 2015]]

On 6 May [[HRW]] reported that an airstrike struck a residential home in Saada, killing 27 members of one family, including 17 children<ref name="hrw.org"/> and on 26 May, 7 more members of the same family were killed in another airstrike.<ref name="reuters.com1"/>

On 27 May nearly 100 people were killed due to airstrikes hitting Sanaa, Sa'da and Hodeida in the largest ever one-day death toll throughout the conflict.<ref name="losangelestimes"/>

On 28 June a coalition airstrike hit and damaged the UN compound in Aden, severely damaging the [[UNDP]] building and injuring a guard.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.un.org/sg/statements/index.asp?nid=8779|title=United Nations Secretary-General Ban Ki-moon's Statements|author=United Nations Web Services Section|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

On 30 June HRW released a report stating that coalition airstrikes on the northern Yemeni city of Saada, a Houthi rebel stronghold, had killed dozens of civilians and wrecked homes and markets. The group said it had documented a dozen airstrikes on Saada that destroyed or damaged civilian homes, five markets, a school and a petrol station although there was no evidence of military use. "Saada City's streets are littered with bomb craters, destroyed buildings, and other evidence of coalition airstrikes," HRW's Sarah Leah Whitson said in the report<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/30/us-yemen-security-airstrikes-idUSKCN0PA28T20150630|title=Rights group says Arab bombings killed dozens of Yemeni civilians|work=[[Reuters]] |date=30 June 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> and later added. "These attacks appear to be serious laws-of-war violations that need to be properly investigated."<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/06/30/yemen-unlawful-airstrikes-kill-dozens-civilians|title=Yemen: Unlawful Airstrikes Kill Dozens of Civilians|publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=13 July 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

On 6 July airstrikes killed over 100 people including more than 30 civilians in Al Joob, Amran.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://firstlook.org/theintercept/2015/07/10/yemen-airstrike/|title=Photo Essay on Victims of Recent Saudi Airstrikes in Yemen|website=[[The Intercept]]|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> The state-run news agency said that 40 had been killed in a raid on a livestock market in al-Foyoush. Local residents also reported 30 deaths in a raid they said apparently targeted a Houthi checkpoint on the main road between Aden and Lahj. They said 10 of the dead were Houthi fighters. MSF head of mission in Yemen said "It is unacceptable that airstrikes take place in highly concentrated civilian areas where people are gathering and going about their daily lives, especially at a time such as Ramadan."<ref name="reuters.com5"/>

On 25 July airstrikes killed over 120 civilians in the town of Mokha, marking the deadliest strike yet against civilians. The airstrikes hit workers' housing for a power plant in Mokha, flattening some of the buildings, the officials said. A fire erupted in the area, charring many of the corpses. "It just shows what is the trend now of the airstrikes from the coalition," said Hassan Boucenine of the Geneva-based Doctors Without Borders. "Now, it's a house, it's a market, it's anything." He added that many of the workers had families visiting for the Eid al-Fitr holiday at the end of the holy month of Ramadan. Mokha, populated largely by fishermen, had a reputation as one of the safest places in the country embroiled in war, said Boucenine.<ref name="ap.org"/>

On 18 August AI reported that it had confirmed 141 civilian deaths from eight airstrikes.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.todayszaman.com/world_amnesty-all-sides-in-yemen-may-be-guilty-of-war-crimes_396849.html|title=Amnesty: All sides in Yemen may be guilty of war crimes|date=18 August 2015|work=[[Today's Zaman]]|url-status=dead|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20160226093310/http://www.todayszaman.com/world_amnesty-all-sides-in-yemen-may-be-guilty-of-war-crimes_396849.html|archivedate=26 February 2016}}</ref>

On 15 March 2016 Saudi-led airstrikes on a market in Mastaba killed at least 119 people, including 25 children.<ref>[http://www.salon.com/2016/04/07/saudi_coalition_massacred_119_yemenis_at_market_with_u_s_supplied_bombs/ "Saudi coalition massacred 119 Yemenis at market with U.S.-supplied bombs"]. [[Salon (website)|Salon]]. 7 April 2016.</ref>

The attack on 8 October 2016 killed 140 people and injuring 500 persons in one of the single worst death tolls in the two-year war. The United Kingdom is under pressure for exporting arms to Saudi Arabia.<ref name="ReferenceC">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-37613440|title=Yemen conflict: 'Saudi-led coalition plane' hit funeral|first=Frank|last=Gardner |authorlink=Frank Gardner (journalist) |date=10 October 2016|work=BBC News}}</ref>

Forces working for the internationally recognized government of [[Yemen]] claimed of being hit by [[airstrikes]] on 29 August 2019, while traveling towards the southern city of [[Aden]]. According to a government commander, the airstrike killed around 30 troops. No confirmation has been made on who carried out the attack, however, the commander claimed that a coalition led by [[Saudi Arabia]] and the [[United Arab Emirates]] is the only warring side in Yemen's 4-year-old conflict that is equipped with airpower.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/aug/29/fighting-breaks-out-between-former-allies-in-yemen|title=Yemeni troops hit by airstrikes amid fierce fighting for control of Aden
|accessdate=29 August 2019|newspaper=The Guardian}}</ref>

=== Civilian airstrike casualties ===
{{See also|Airstrikes on hospitals in Yemen}}
[[File:065 Procession (39025167311).jpg|thumb|Protest against the military intervention in Yemen, New York City, December 2017]]
On 24 August 2015, the UN special representative of the secretary-general for children and armed conflict said, that of 402 children killed in Yemen since late March 2015, 73 percent were victims of Saudi coalition-led airstrikes.<ref name="childrenandarmedconflict-un-org_2015-08-24_SSY">{{cite web |title=Statement on the situation in Yemen by Leila Zerrougui, Special Representative of the Secretary-General for Children and Armed Conflict |publisher=UN Office of the SRSG for Children and Armed Conflict |date=24 August 2015 |url=https://childrenandarmedconflict.un.org/press-release/statement-on-the-situation-in-yemen-by-leila-zerrougui-special-representative-of-the-secretary-general-for-children-and-armed-conflict/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6b2eHR6Az?url=https://childrenandarmedconflict.un.org/press-release/statement-on-the-situation-in-yemen-by-leila-zerrougui-special-representative-of-the-secretary-general-for-children-and-armed-conflict/ |archivedate=25 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="ipsnews-net_2015-08-25_MOC">{{cite news |last=D'Almeida |first=Kanya |title=Majority of Child Casualties in Yemen Caused by Saudi-Led Airstrikes |publisher=[[Inter Press Service]] |date=25 August 2015 |url=http://www.ipsnews.net/2015/08/majority-of-child-casualties-in-yemen-caused-by-saudi-led-airstrikes |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6b52Ixr1d?url=http://www.ipsnews.net/2015/08/majority-of-child-casualties-in-yemen-caused-by-saudi-led-airstrikes |archivedate=26 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> The UN also said at this time that an average of 30 people had been killed in Yemen every single day since the beginning of the war. On top of this, more than 23,000 had been wounded.<ref>{{cite news |title=4,500 killed in Yemen in 150 Days of Saudi-led bombing |author=Ben Norton |date=24 August 2015 |work=[[Mondoweiss]] |url=http://mondoweiss.net/2015/08/killed-saudi-bombing/|author-link=Ben Norton }}</ref>

On 11 September, UN Human Rights Commissioner said that of 1,527 civilians killed between 26 March and 30 June, at least 941 people were killed by airstrikes carried out by the Saudi-led coalition.<ref name="UNHRC_2015-09-07_SHR">{{cite web |title=Situation of human rights in Yemen – Report of the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights (A/HRC/30/31) – Advance Edited Version |publisher=UN Human Rights Council |date=7 September 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/situation-human-rights-yemen-report-office-united-nations-high-commissioner-human |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6bXoMdEZh?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/situation-human-rights-yemen-report-office-united-nations-high-commissioner-human |archivedate=14 September 2015 |url-status=live}}. PDF: {{cite web |title=Situation of human rights in Yemen – Report of the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights (A/HRC/30/31) – Advance Edited Version |publisher=UN Human Rights Council |date=7 September 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/A_HRC_30_31_AEV.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6bXoUO8BI?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/A_HRC_30_31_AEV.pdf |archivedate=14 September 2015 |url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="wsj_2015-12-10_HTY">{{cite web |last1=Fitch |first1=Asa |last2=al-Kibsi |first2=Mohammed |title=Heavy Toll in Yemen Conflict Draws Scrutiny – Civilians bear brunt of damage in war between Saudi-led coalition and Houthi rebels |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |date=10 December 2015 |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/heavy-toll-in-yemen-conflict-draws-scrutiny-1449743401 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e53CFrUZ?url=http://www.wsj.com/articles/heavy-toll-in-yemen-conflict-draws-scrutiny-1449743401 |archivedate=27 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="NYT_2015-09-12_ATT">{{cite news |first=Kareem |last=Fahim |title=Airstrikes Take Toll on Civilians in Yemen War |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=12 September 2015 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/13/world/middleeast/airstrikes-hit-civilians-yemen-war.html|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6d0Hls9wu?url=http://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/13/world/middleeast/airstrikes-hit-civilians-yemen-war.html?_r=2 |archivedate=13 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="globalpost-com_2015-11-30_WUH">{{cite news |last=Kouddous |first=Sharif Abdel |title=With US help, Saudi Arabia is obliterating Yemen |work=[[GlobalPost]] |date=30 November 2015 |url=http://www.globalpost.com/article/6696395/2015/11/30/yemen-conflict-saudi-arabia-airstrikes-war-crimes-united-states |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dxg3104L?url=http://www.globalpost.com/article/6696395/2015/11/30/yemen-conflict-saudi-arabia-airstrikes-war-crimes-united-states |archivedate=22 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 27 October, the OHCHR said that out of 2,615 civilians killed between 26 March and 26 October 2015, 1,641 civilians had reportedly been killed due to airstrikes carried out by the Saudi-led coalition.<ref name="UNOG_2015-10-27_RPB">{{cite web |title=Regular Press Briefing by the Information Service |publisher=[[United Nations Office at Geneva|UNOG]] |date=27 October 2015 |url=http://www.unog.ch/unog/website/news_media.nsf/%28httpNewsByYear_en%29/BFBC8D1DEEC1C846C1257EEB004A3211?OpenDocument |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cdKdsLUd?url=http://www.unog.ch/unog/website/news_media.nsf/(httpNewsByYear_en)/BFBC8D1DEEC1C846C1257EEB004A3211?OpenDocument |archivedate=29 October 2015 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref name="AA_2015-10-27_YSM">{{cite news |title=UN: Yemen's seven-month violence kills 2,615 civilians |publisher=[[Anadolu Agency]] |date=27 October 2015 |url=http://www.aa.com.tr/en/middle-east/un-yemens-seven-month-violence-kills-2-615-civilians/456735 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cfn75wac?url=http://www.aa.com.tr/en/middle-east/un-yemens-seven-month-violence-kills-2-615-civilians/456735 |archivedate=30 October 2015 |url-status=live}}</ref>

The January 2016 report of a UN panel of experts, presented to the UN security council, attributed 60 percent (2,682) of all civilian deaths and injuries in the war since 26 March 2015 to air-launched explosive weapons.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/>

On 1 February 2016 Reuters reported: "Mortars and rockets fired at Saudi Arabian towns and villages have killed 375 civilians, including 63 children, since the start of the Saudi-led military campaign in Yemen in late March, Riyadh said."<ref name="reuters-com_2016-02-01_SAS">{{cite news |first1=William |last1=Maclean |first2=Angus |last2=McDowall |title=Saudi Arabia says 375 civilians killed on its border in Yemen war |work=[[Reuters]] |date=1 February 2016 |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-saudi-idUSKCN0VA36T |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6f0VbHu3a?url=http://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-saudi-idUSKCN0VA36T |archivedate=2 February 2016 |url-status=live}}</ref>

On 16 September 2016, ''The Guardian'' reported: "The independent and non-partisan survey, based on open-source data, including research on the ground, records more than 8,600 air attacks between March 2015, when the Saudi-led campaign began, and the end of August this year. Of these, 3,577 were listed as having hit military sites and 3,158 struck non-military sites.... The UN has put the death toll of the 18-month war at more than 10,000, with 3,799 of them being civilians."<ref>[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/sep/16/third-of-saudi-airstrikes-on-yemen-have-hit-civilian-sites-data-shows "One in three Saudi air raids on Yemen hit civilian sites, data shows"]. ''[[The Guardian]]''. 16 September 2016.</ref>

In October 2016, a densely populated [[2016 Sana'a funeral air raid|funeral in Yemen was struck]], leaving at least 155 dead<ref name="Sanchez">{{cite news |last1=Sanchez|first1=Ray|title=US: No blank check for Saudi Arabia in Yemen|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2016/10/08/middleeast/yemen-airstrikes/ |publisher=CNN |accessdate=10 October 2016}}</ref> and 525 wounded,<ref name="Nadia">{{cite news |last1=Khomami|first1=Nadia|title=Airstrikes on Yemen funeral kill at least 140 people, UN official says|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/oct/08/saudi-led-coalition-airstrike-hit-yemen-funeral-officials-say |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=8 October 2016 |accessdate=10 October 2016}}</ref> including the senior military and security officials of the Shia Houthi and loyalists of former president Ali Abdullah Saleh.<ref name="Nadia"/> The attack was reportedly carried out by Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Adam|first1=Withnall|title=Britain and US pile pressure on Saudi Arabia over Yemen funeral bombing|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/yemen-sanaa-funeral-bombing-air-strikes-uk-arms-sales-us-saudi-arabia-coalition-latest-a7353231.html |work=[[The Independent]] |date=10 October 2016 |accessdate=10 October 2016}}</ref> Saudi Arabia accepts the finding of the Joint Incidents Assessment Team, a setup of coalition states to investigate complaints against coalitions' conduct in Decisive Storm, that coalition's bombardment at a funeral ceremony in [[Sana'a|Sanaʽa]], in which over 140 people were killed and more than 600 injured, was based on wrong information.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.arabnews.com/node/998181/middle-east|title= JIAT: Yemen funeral targeted based on wrong information; Coalition accepts findings|newspaper=Arab News|date= 15 October 2016|accessdate=16 October 2016}}</ref> Reportedly, the United States is reviewing its policy of support for the Saudi-led coalition. US Secretary of State John Kerry sought assurances from Saudi Arabia that incidents such as the airstrike on a civilian funeral in Sanaʽa will not happen again. He proposed a cease-fire and a return to talks aiming for a political resolution of the conflict. Deputy Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman said he hoped to institute a 72-hour cease-fire as soon as possible, provided the Houthis will agree.<ref>Mohammad al Kibsi, Ahmed al Omran, Karen Leigh and Felicia Schwartz, "Yemen raid spurs U.S. review of support", ''The Wall Street Journal'' (10 October 2016), p. A13.</ref>

[[File:Ongoing conflicts around the world.svg|thumb|250px|{{center|Ongoing armed conflicts in June 2019.}}
----
{{legend|maroon|Major wars, 10,000 or more deaths in current or past year}}
]]
In December 2017, Saudis killed and injured 600 Yemenis in 26 days.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.awdnews.com/index/saudis-kill-injure-600-yemenis-just-26-days/|title=Saudi's kill and injure 600 Yemeni's in just 26 days - AWDnews|website=www.awdnews.com|access-date=20 July 2018}}</ref>

On 9 August 2018, a [[Dahyan air strike|school bus was hit by a Saudi airstrike]], killing 51 people and injuring 79. 40 of the dead and 56 of the injured were children between the ages of 6 and 11.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2018/08/13/middleeast/yemen-children-school-bus-strike-intl/index.html|title=The schoolboys in Yemen were chatting and laughing. Then came the airstrike|author1=Nima Elbagir |author2=Salma Abdelaziz |author3=Sheena McKenzie |author4=Waffa Munayyer|publisher=}}</ref>

In the past few days from 7 November, more than 100 Saudi airstrikes had attacked civilian neighborhoods and a malnutrition clinic run by Save the Children in Hodeidah.<ref name="theguardian2018">{{cite web |last1=McKernan |first1=Bethan |title=Battle rages in Yemen's vital port as showdown looms |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/nov/07/yemen-hodeidah-airstrikes-saudi-led-coalition-ceasefire-calls |website=theguardian |accessdate=7 November 2018}}</ref>

According to the Yemen Data Project, the Saudi-led bombing campaign has killed or injured an estimated 17,729 civilians as of March 2019.<ref>{{cite news|author=<!--Staff writer(s); no by-line.-->|date= March 27, 2019|title=Study: 17,729 Yemeni Civilians Killed or Injured by U.S.-Backed Strikes|url=https://www.democracynow.org/2019/3/27/headlines/study_17_729_yemeni_civilians_killed_or_injured_by_us_backed_strikes|work=[[Democracy Now!]] |location= |access-date=March 31, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last= Raghavan|first=Sudarsan|date= March 27, 2019|title=Airstrike by Saudi-led coalition said to hit near Yemeni hospital, killing 8, including 5 children|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/airstrike-by-saudi-led-coalition-said-to-hit-yemeni-hospital-killing-7-including-4-children/2019/03/27/7103b829-eda9-462a-aec1-be304044ac5e_story.html|work=[[The Washington Post]] |location= |access-date=March 31, 2019}}</ref>

As per the [[Armed Conflict Location and Event Data Project]], the Saudi-led coalition has caused around 4,800 civilian deaths and the Houthis have caused around 1,300 out of 7,000 civilian fatalities since 2016. On 16 May 2019, another airstrike in a crowded residential area of Sana'a killed five civilians and injured 31.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/22/world/middleeast/saudi-yemen-airstrikes-civilians.html|title=Saudi Warplanes, Most Made in America, Still Bomb Civilians in Yemen|accessdate=22 May 2019|work=The New York times}}</ref>

An air strike in the northwest Yemen killed seven children and two women, as reported by the [[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]] on 13 July 2020. The [[Houthi movement|Houthi rebels]] claimed that the air strike was carried out by the Saudi-led coalition. However, [[Saudi Arabia]] denied any involvement in the air strike.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security/saudi-led-coalition-in-yemen-denies-killing-civilians-in-saada-air-strike-idUSKBN23O2U2|title=Saudi-led coalition in Yemen denies killing civilians in Saada air strike|accessdate=17 July 2020|website=Reuters}}</ref>

On 6 August 2020, an air strike in northern Yemen killed a large number of civilians. A report by humanitarian coordination agency, [[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs|UNOCHA]], indicated that as many as nine children were killed, while seven children and two women were injured. The [[Special Envoy of the Secretary-General|UN Special Envoy]] for Yemen, [[Martin Griffiths]], condemned air strikes and called for a transparent investigation into the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://de.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security/u-n-condemns-air-strikes-in-yemen-that-reportedly-killed-children-idUSKCN253277|title=U.N. condemns air strikes in Yemen that reportedly killed children|accessdate=7 August 2020|website=Reuters}}</ref>

== Killed journalists and media workers ==
{{Main|List of journalists killed in Yemen}}
In 2015 Yemen was ranked 168th out of 180 countries in the [[Reporters Without Borders]] (RSF) [[Press Freedom Index]]. According to an annual round-up published on 29 December 2015 by RSF, six journalists in Yemen (out of 67 worldwide) were killed in 2015 because of their work or while reporting.<ref name="RSF_2016-12-29_1JK">{{cite web |title=RSF Annual Round-up: 110 journalists killed in 2015 |publisher=Reporters sans Frontières |date=29 December 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/world/rsf-annual-round-110-journalists-killed-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eFq97f5X?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/world/rsf-annual-round-110-journalists-killed-2015 |archivedate=3 January 2016 |url-status=live }}. PDF: {{cite web |title=RSF Annual Round-up: 110 journalists killed in 2015 |publisher=Reporters sans Frontières |date=29 December 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/rsf_2015-part_2-en.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eFqCbhv5?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/rsf_2015-part_2-en.pdf |archivedate=3 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> According to the [[Committee to Protect Journalists]], at least six journalists were killed in airstrikes by the Saudi-led coalition between March 2015 and the end of January 2016.<ref name="CPJ_2016-01-19_FJK">{{cite web |title=Freelance journalist killed by Saudi coalition airstrike in Yemen |publisher=Committee to Protect Journalists |date=19 January 2016 |url=https://cpj.org/2016/01/freelance-journalist-killed-by-saudi-coalition-air.php |access-date=19 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="CPJ_2016-02-02_CUF">{{cite web |title=CPJ urges full, independent investigation into killing of journalists in Yemen |publisher=Committee to Protect Journalists |date=2 February 2016 |url=https://cpj.org/2016/02/cpj-urges-full-independent-investigation-into-kill.php |access-date=11 February 2016}}</ref>

On 17 January 2016, the freelance Yemeni journalist [[Almigdad Mojalli]] was killed in an airstrike by the Saudi-led coalition in Jaref, a Houthi-controlled district in the outskirts of Sanaʽa.<ref name="VOA_2016-01-17_AYK">{{cite news |title=Airstrike in Yemen Kills Freelance Journalist Working for VOA |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=17 January 2016 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/airstrike-in-yemen-kills-freelance-journalist-working-for-voa/3149762.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ecar39mI?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/airstrike-in-yemen-kills-freelance-journalist-working-for-voa/3149762.html |archivedate=18 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="RSF_2016-01-18_JKA"/> Mojalli had gone there, working for [[Voice of America]] (VOA), to interview survivors of air strikes in Jaref in which up to 21 civilians had been killed days earlier.<ref name="RSF_2016-01-18_JKA">{{cite web |title=Journalist killed in air strike near Sanaa |publisher=Reporters without Borders |date=18 January 2016 |url=http://en.rsf.org/yemen-journalist-killed-in-air-strike-18-01-2016,48746.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6edchmqaP?url=http://en.rsf.org/yemen-journalist-killed-in-air-strike-18-01-2016,48746.html |archivedate=18 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="telegraph-co-uk_2016-01-17_LYJ">{{cite news |last=Loveluck |first=Louisa |title=Leading Yemeni journalist who worked for international media killed in air strike |work=[[The Daily Telegraph]] |date=17 January 2016 |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/yemen/12104610/Leading-Yemeni-journalist-who-worked-for-international-media-killed-in-air-strike.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6edb9V3cz?url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/yemen/12104610/Leading-Yemeni-journalist-who-worked-for-international-media-killed-in-air-strike.html |archivedate=18 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> [[Rory Peck Trust]] honored him as "key source of information for visiting journalists" in Yemen.<ref name="RPT_2016-01-19_RAM">{{cite web |title=Remembering Almigdad Mojalli – The Yemeni freelancer was killed by airstrikes just outside Sana'a on 17th January |publisher=Rory Peck Trust |date=19 January 2016 |url=https://rorypecktrust.org/rpt-live/January-2016-%281%29/Remembering-Almigdad-Mojalli,-RPT-friend-and-bene.aspx |url-status=live }}</ref> [[Daniel Martin Varisco]], President of the American Institute for Yemeni Studies and Research Professor at [[Qatar University]], said in an obituary that Mojalli's work "was a voice documenting the humanitarian crisis that the world outside Yemen has largely ignored" and a voice that "has been silenced".<ref name="menatidningen-se_2016-01-19_VOW">{{cite web |last=Varisco Federation of Journalists (IFJ) |date=18 January 2016 |url=http://www.ifj.org/nc/news-single-view/backpid/1/article/yemen-journalist-killed-in-an-air-raid-by-the-saudi-led-coalition/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ehZKuXKR?url=http://www.ifj.org/nc/news-single-view/backpid/1/article/yemen-journalist-killed-in-an-air-raid-by-the-saudi-led-coalition/ |archivedate=21 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> UNESCO Director-General Irina Bokova and RSF reminded all the parties to the armed conflict in Yemen that they were required to respect and ensure the safety of all journalists by UN Security Council Resolution 2222, adopted in 2015, and by the [[Geneva Conventions]].<ref name="RSF_2016-01-18_JKA"/><ref name="UNNewsService_2016-01-20_YJD">{{cite news |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6egx2X9gJ?url=http://www.unesco.org/new/en/media-services/single-view/news/director_general_deplores_death_of_journalist_almigdad_mojalli_in_yemen/ |archivedate=21 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 21 January 2016, the 17-year-old TV cameraman Hashem al-Hamran was mortally injured by an air-strike by the Saudi-led coalition in the city of Dahian (Saada Governorate), when he was filming bombing raids for the Houthi-run television channel [[al-Masirah TV]]. He died from his wounds on 22 January 2016.<ref name="CPJ_2016-02-02_CUF"/><ref name="IFJ_2016-01-27_AJD">{{cite web |title=Further media violations in Yemen: another journalist dead and a newspaper silenced |publisher=International Federation of Journalists (IFJ) |date=27 January 2016 |url=http://www.ifj.org/nc/news-single-view/backpid/1/article/further-media-violations-in-yemen-another-journalist-dead-and-a-newspaper-silenced/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fCbulc1j?url=http://www.ifj.org/nc/news-single-view/backpid/1/article/further-media-violations-in-yemen-another-journalist-dead-and-a-newspaper-silenced/ |archivedate=10 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> The YJS, the IFJ and Irina Bokova, Director General of UNESCO, condemned the killing of Hashem Al Hamran.<ref name="IFJ_2016-01-27_AJD"/><ref name="UNESCO_2016-02-09_DGC">{{cite web |title=Director-General condemns killing of media worker Hashem Al Hamran in Yemen |publisher=UN Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization |date=9 February 2016 |url=http://www.unesco.org/new/en/unesco/about-us/who-we-are/director-general/singleview-dg/news/director_general_condemns_killing_of_media_worker_hashem_al_hamran_in_yemen/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fCbkxHHr?url=http://www.unesco.org/new/en/unesco/about-us/who-we-are/director-general/singleview-dg/news/director_general_condemns_killing_of_media_worker_hashem_al_hamran_in_yemen/ |archivedate=10 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

The director of [[Yemen TV]], Munir al-Hakami, and his wife, Suaad Hujaira, who also worked for the state-owned, Houthi-controlled broadcaster, were killed along with their three children by a coalition air strike on 9 February 2016.<ref name="independent-co-uk_2016-02-12_YJA"/><ref name="UNESCO_DGCK">{{cite web |title=Director-General condemns killing of media workers Munir al-Hakimi and Suad Hujaira in Yemen |publisher=UN Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization | |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="NYT_2016-02-10_AKF">{{cite news |last=Almosawa |first=Shuaib |title=Yemen: Airstrike Kills Family in Capital |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=10 February 2016 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/02/11/world/middleeast/yemen-airstrike-kills-family-in-capital.html|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fW195VWs?url=http://www.nytimes.com/2016/02/11/world/middleeast/yemen-airstrike-kills-family-in-capital.html?_r=2 |archivedate=23 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> They were living in a residential area nowhere near a possible military target;<ref name="independent-co-uk_2016-02-12_YJA">{{cite news
