|archivedate=23 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="NYT_2016-02-10_AKF"/> the killing of the two media workers was condemned by the head of UNESCO.<ref name="UNESCO_DGCK"/>

Zaid al-Sharabi, an [[Emirates News Agency]] journalist, was killed by a Houthi set bomb which was hidden inside a motocycle and placed near a restaurant in [[Mokha]] on 29 January 2019. The bomb killed a total of 6 people and wounded another Emirates News Agency journalist, Faisal Al Thubhani.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.thenational.ae/uae/abu-dhabi-tv-cameraman-killed-in-yemen-market-bombing-1.819370|title=Abu Dhabi TV cameraman killed in Yemen market bombing|publisher=The National|last1=Reynolds|first1=Ryan|date=29 January 2019}}</ref>

== Infrastructure damage and humanitarian situation ==
{{Seealso|2016–20 Yemen cholera outbreak}}
In February 2016, the UN Security Council noted that in terms of "numbers of people in need" the humanitarian crisis in Yemen was "the largest in the world".<ref name="UNSC_2016-02-18_SCP">{{cite web |title=Security Council Press Statement on Situation in Yemen |date=18 February 2016 |publisher=UN Security Council |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/security-council-press-statement-situation-yemen-3 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fRZLGBeZ?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/security-council-press-statement-situation-yemen-3 |archivedate=20 February 2016 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=https://www.un.org/press/en/2016/sc12250.doc.htm |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fRZQDXY4?url=http://www.un.org/press/en/2016/sc12250.doc.htm |archivedate=20 February 2016 |url-status=live }})</ref> In August 2015, the head of the International Red Cross said, "Yemen after five months looks like Syria after five years."<ref>{{cite news |last= Loveluck |first= Louisa |date= 19 August 2015 |title= Yemen 'already looks like Syria after five years of war' |url= https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/yemen/11813169/Yemen-already-looks-like-Syria-after-five-years-of-war.html |newspaper= [[The Daily Telegraph]] |access-date= 23 February 2016 }}</ref>

[[File:Bin Salman - the Butcher of Yemen.jpg|thumb|Protest outside [[10 Downing Street]] against a visit by Saudi Arabian Crown Prince [[Mohammed bin Salman]], London, March 2018]]

The U.N. human rights office reported more than 8,100 civilians were killed or wounded between 26 March and the end of 2015, the vast majority from airstrikes by Saudi-led coalition forces.<ref name="VOA_2016-01-05_YWT">{{cite news |first=Lisa |last=Schlein |title=Yemen War Taking Big Toll on Civilians |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=5 January 2016 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/yemen-war-civilian-toll/3131796.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eSfB5fLb?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/yemen-war-civilian-toll/3131796.html |archivedate=11 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

At the beginning of May 2015, the Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights (OHCHR) said, that there had been "severe destruction of civilian infrastructure, including houses, in many districts" since 26 March.<ref name="OHCHR_2015-05-05_PBN">{{cite web|url=http://www.ohchr.org/EN/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=15924&LangID=E|title=Press briefing notes on Yemen, Serbia, Honduras and Albinism website launch|publisher=Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights|archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YJ7biPDu?url=http://www.ohchr.org/EN/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=15924&LangID=E|archivedate=5 May 2015|url-status=live|access-date=7 May 2015|df=dmy-all}}</ref><ref name="UNNewsCentre_2015-05-05_YCD"/> Severe damage caused by attacks on Yemen's essential civilian infrastructure such as airports in Sanaʽa and Hodeida by the Saudi-led military coalition was obstructing the delivery of much-needed humanitarian assistance and movement of humanitarian personnel according to the International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) and Médecins Sans Frontières (MSF).<ref name="MSF-ca_2015-05-04_MAI">{{cite web |title=Yemen: MSF and ICRC alarmed by attacks on country's infrastructure and humanitarian lifelines |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières (MSF) |date=4 May 2015 |url=http://www.msf.ca/en/article/yemen-msf-and-icrc-alarmed-by-attacks-on-country-s-infrastructure-and-humanitarian-lifelines |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fKohpKOh?url=http://www.msf.ca/en/article/yemen-msf-and-icrc-alarmed-by-attacks-on-country-s-infrastructure-and-humanitarian-lifelines |archivedate=16 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="UNNewsCentre_2015-05-04_URO">{{cite news |title=Yemen: UN relief official urges 'safe and reliable' access to Sana'a airport to deliver critical aid |date=4 May 2015 |publisher=UN News Centre |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50762 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fKu5JmGC?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50762 |archivedate=16 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="UNOCHA-UNHC_2015-05-04_SHC">{{cite web |title=Statement by the Humanitarian Coordinator for Yemen, Johannes Van Der Klaauw (4 May 2015) |date=4 May 2015 | publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, UN Humanitarian Coordinator in Yemen |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/statement-humanitarian-coordinator-yemen-johannes-van-der-klaauw-4-may-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fKuODCkL?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/statement-humanitarian-coordinator-yemen-johannes-van-der-klaauw-4-may-2015 |archivedate=16 February 2016 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/PR_EN_0.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fKuSFWSp?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/PR_EN_0.pdf |archivedate=16 February 2016 |url-status=live }})</ref>

In the first weeks since 26 March massive destruction of civilian infrastructure particularly happened in Aden and Sa'da, according to OHCHR.<ref name="UN-OHCHR_2015-05-22_PBN">{{cite web |title=Press briefing notes on Hungary, Yemen and Saudi Arabia |publisher=UN Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights |date=22 May 2015 |url=http://www.ohchr.org/EN/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=16001&LangID=E |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YjDGQKu4?url=http://www.ohchr.org/EN/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=16001&LangID=E |archivedate=23 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="UNNewsCentre_2015-05-22_URO">{{cite news |title=Yemen: UN rights office urges all parties to adhere to international law as civilian toll grows |publisher=UN News Centre |date=22 May 2015 |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50940 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fKr6TKn4?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50940 |archivedate=16 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In August 2015, air attacks of the Saudi-led coalition on port facilities at Al-Hudaydah "in clear contravention of international humanitarian law", said [[Under-Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs and Emergency Relief Coordinator]] [[Stephen O'Brien]].<ref name="AFP_2015-08-20_YAR">{{cite news |title=Yemen air raids condemned as blast hits governor office |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=20 August 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-air-raids-condemned-blast-hits-governor-office |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6awe95TOq?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-air-raids-condemned-blast-hits-governor-office |archivedate=21 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="UNOCHA20150827YHB1"/>

In mid-February 2016, Stephen O'Brien said the situation in Yemen was a "humanitarian catastrophe", with 21 million people in need of some kind of aid, 7.6&nbsp;million people "severely food-insecure", and over 3.4&nbsp;million children out of school.<ref name="AJE catastrophe">{{cite web |title= 'Humanitarian catastrophe' unfolding in Yemen: UN |url= http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2016/02/catastrophe-unfolding-yemen-160217054116797.html |publisher= [[Al Jazeera]] English |date= 17 February 2016 |access-date= 17 February 2016 }}</ref> O'Brien noted the situation had not been helped by the diversion of an aid vessel by coalition forces.<ref name="AJE catastrophe"/>

According to Lamya Khalidi, an archaeologist: ''At least sixty of Yemen's monuments have been damaged or destroyed'' in the bombing campaign by Saudi-led coalition in March 2015. Among these monuments are unique archaeological monuments, old cities, museums, mosques, churches and tombs.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.alaraby.co.uk/english/indepth/2018/3/26/yemen-suffers-cultural-vandalism-during-its-war|title=Yemen suffers cultural vandalism during its war|first=Jonathan|last=Fenton-Harvey|publisher=}}</ref><ref>https://www.cambridge.org/core/services/aop-cambridge-core/content/view/53D08264CAACB808618BCF9D70053D25/S0020743817000691a.pdf/div-class-title-the-destruction-of-yemen-and-its-cultural-heritage-div.pdf</ref>

=== Timeline ===
On 26 March, Interior Ministry officials linked to Ansar Allah documented that 23 civilians had been killed and 24 wounded. Among the dead were 5 children, ages 2 to 13, 6 women and an elderly man. The wounded included 12 children, ages 3 to 8, and 2 women due to airstrike against Sanaʽa particularly in [[Bani Hawat]], a predominantly Houthi neighborhood near Sanaa's airports and al-Nasr, near the presidential palace. HRW documented the deaths of 11 civilians, including 2 women and 2 children, other than those provided by the Yemeni officials along with 14 more wounded, including 3 children and 1 woman. According to AI, that bombing destroyed at least 14 homes in [[Bani Hawat]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.eurasiareview.com/28032015-yemen-saudi-led-airstrikes-take-civilian-toll-says-hrw/|publisher=Eurasia Review|title=Yemen: Saudi-led Airstrikes Take Civilian Toll, Says HRW|date=28 March 2015|access-date=30 March 2015|url-status=dead|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150402094024/http://www.eurasiareview.com/28032015-yemen-saudi-led-airstrikes-take-civilian-toll-says-hrw/|archivedate=2 April 2015}}</ref>

On 31 March, [[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs|OCHA]] reported that 13 of 22 Governorates were affected and highlighted infrastructure effects that detailed coalition bombing of a refugee camp that killed 29 and injured 40. Fuel shortages in the south threatened water access to citizens and in Lahj, electricity and water services had not been functioning for several days.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-escalating-conflict-situation-report-no-1-31-march-2015|title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 1 (as of 31 March 2015)|publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]]}}</ref> Later that day, AI reported that at least six civilians, including four children, were burned to death as a result of an airstrike. It reported that two fuel stations were destroyed. In al-Kadima area in al-Kita, several passengers were killed in a car that had stopped to refuel and a worker was injured. The third strike, apparently aimed at a passing fuel tanker, set fire to at least three civilian homes. AI then stated that "it is becoming increasingly apparent that the Saudi Arabian-led coalition is turning a blind eye to civilian deaths and suffering caused by its military intervention."<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/articles/news/2015/03/yemen-civilians-burn-to-death-in-further-airstrikes/|title=Yemen: At least six civilians burn to death in further airstrikes overnight|publisher=Amnesty International}}</ref>

On 17 April, OCHA reported on the increasing deterioration of the humanitarian situation, reporting airstrikes hitting in Saada City a water tank, the electricity station, a petrol station, a plastics processing factory, a shopping centre and a housing complex. Several days earlier, airstrikes had hit private homes, the post office, a community centre, government offices, markets and vehicles. Local partners estimated about 50 dead within the past week. In Sanaʽa residential neighborhoods near Assir, Ayban and Faj Attan were affected due to their proximity to military camps. In Amran, airstrikes hit a petrol station, an educational institute and a bridge. According to local reports, a local water corporation in Hajjah (Abbs District) was hit. The report also stated that civilian casualties were under-reported as families without access to hospitals bury their members at home.<ref name="reliefweb.int">{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report_20150417_final.pdf |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 4 |date=17 April 2015 |publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]]}}</ref>

On 20 April coalition airstrikes hit the Fajj Atan military base, causing a large explosion that killed 38 civilians and injured over 500. The airstrike also targeted the office of Yemen Today, a TV network owned by [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]], killing three and injuring other workers. An eyewitness reported that emergency rooms were overwhelmed.<ref name="kills944">{{cite web |url=http://www.expatica.com/ch/news/country-news/Yemen-violence-kills-944-injures-3487-WHO_470764.html|title=Yemen violence kills 944, injures 3,487: WHO|access-date=26 April 2015|date=21 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/20/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0NB0R820150420|title=Air strike on missile base in Yemen capital kills 25, wounds hundreds|work=[[Reuters]] |date=20 April 2015 |access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref> The head of the [[ICRC]] in Yemen later clarified that 90 people had died during this attack.<ref name="lifeundersiege">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global-development-professionals-network/2015/apr/24/life-under-seige-in-yemen-bullets-and-shrapnel-came-into-the-house|title=Life under siege in Yemen: 'Bullets and shrapnel came into the house'|work=[[The Guardian]]}}</ref>

On 21 April the BBC reported a warning from the UN about worsening health services and a dire need for medicines.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32394471 |title= Yemen conflict: Dozens killed in Saudi-led air strikes | work= BBC News|date=21 April 2015 |access-date= 21 April 2015}}</ref>

On 24 April UNICEF released a report stating that since the start of the military intervention, 115 children had been killed, with at least 64 from aerial bombardment.The F-14's of Saudi Arabia often strike Militia hold outs that miss and hit shelters the homeless and houses. <ref name="hundredschildren">{{cite web |url=http://www.unicef.org/infobycountry/media_81680.html|title=Hundreds of children killed or maimed in deadly month-long fighting in Yemen – UNICEF|date=24 April 2015|publisher=UNICEF}}</ref>

According to OCHA's fifth report, released on 26 April, humanitarian operations would come to a complete halt within two weeks and hospitals in both Sanaa and Aden would close completely due to the lack of fuel. The lack of fuel affected water supplies. Markets in affected governorates are not able to provide food, with wheat grain and flour prices rising by 42% and 44%, respectively. The healthcare system faced an imminent collapse with hospitals struggling to operate due to lack of medicines and supplies. Essential medicine prices increased by 300%.

Casualties from 19 March to 22 April reached 1,080 (28 children and 48 women) and 4,352 wounded (80 children and 143 women). According to the WFP, 12&nbsp;million people were food insecure, a 13% rise.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Yemen%20SitRep%20for%2026%20April%202015.pdf|title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 5 |date=26 April 2015 |publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]]}}</ref>

On 29 April [[OCHA]] reported that airstrikes hit SIA on 28 April, damaging the runway and hampering aid deliveries. Airstrikes were also reported at Al Hudayda Airport and Saada. Widespread internet and phone disruptions were reported in several governorates due to the lack of fuel and electricity. On 25 April, the Yemen Public Telecommunications Corporation warned that unless the fuel crisis was resolved, telecommunication services (mobile phones, internet, and land lines) would shut down within a week. The disruption in communication was affecting information flow on humanitarian needs and operations. On 29 April, Haradh was heavily bombarded, including areas near the main hospital. Food distribution and aid would reportedly stop within a week if additional fuel could not be obtained. As of 29 April the Al Hudaydah Governorate ran out of fuel and aid operations could not be completed.<ref name="UNOCHA20150429ECF"/>

On 30 April OCHA's Flash Update 22 reported that airstrikes hit the only main roads that connect the Sanaʽa Governorate with Ibb. It also indicated that over 3,410 people from Yemen had arrived in Somalia since the fighting escalated, with 2,285 arrivals registered in Puntland and 1,125 registered in the Somaliland. A further 8,900 migrants were registered in Djibouti, 4,700 of whom were third country nationals.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Flash%20Update%20on%20the%20Escalating%20Conflict%20-%20No.%2022%20-%2030%20April%202015.pdf |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Flash Update 22 | date=30 April 2015 |publisher=[[ReliefWeb]] |accessdate=25 February 2016}}</ref>

On 4 May coalition airstrikes hit SIA, destroying a cargo ship and other planes used to transport food and supplies.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/posttv/world/middle_east/planes-in-flames-after-airstrikes-at-yemen-airport/2015/05/04/25f66d5d-c90e-40a4-889f-f5833f73a0c8_video.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150505021425/http://www.washingtonpost.com/posttv/world/middle_east/planes-in-flames-after-airstrikes-at-yemen-airport/2015/05/04/25f66d5d-c90e-40a4-889f-f5833f73a0c8_video.html|archive-date=5 May 2015|title=Planes burn at Yemen airport following airstrikes|date=4 May 2015|work=[[The Washington Post]]|url-status=dead}}</ref> OCHA reported that several airstrikes hit the Al Hudayda airport and surrounding areas in Al Hudayda City. In Aden, the districts of Craiter and Al-Muala were without electricity, water and telecommunication for over a week according to residents.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/ocha_yemen_flash_update_on_the_escalating_conflict_-_no._24_-_04_may_2015.pdf|title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Flash Update 24 |publisher=ReliefWeb |accessdate=10 June 2017}}</ref>

On 5 May, in order to send humanitarian aid, van der Klaauw haggled with the coalition to stop bombing SIA.{{citation needed|date=September 2019}} He emphasized the effects on persons with disabilities stating that over 3,000,000 people with disabilities could not meet their basic needs. The conflict forced more than 300 centres to close. He added that they were especially concerned about an airstrike that targeted a military field hospital.<ref name="UNNewsCentre_2015-05-05_YCD" />

On 6 May, the OCHA reported lack of fuel to support humanitarian operations beyond one week, with fuel and [[food prices]] continuing to increase.<ref name="UNOCHA20150506ECS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 6 |publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]] |date=6 May 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-escalating-conflict-situation-report-no-6-06-may-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YXsGAXs9?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-escalating-conflict-situation-report-no-6-06-may-2015 |archivedate=15 May 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 6 |publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]] |url=https://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/yemen_ocha_situation_report_6_may_2015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YXsOP4DL?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/yemen_ocha_situation_report_6_may_2015.pdf |archivedate=15 May 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref> The [[World Food Programme]] declared that shortages of fuel has changed to a serious threat for hospitals and food supplies. Edward Santiago, country director for Save the Children, said in statement a short time ceasefire is not enough to allow for humanitarian supplies.<ref name= aid>{{cite news | url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/06/us-yemen-security-aid-idUSKBN0NR0DQ20150506 | title=Aid agencies warn fuel shortages may end their work in Yemen | work=[[Reuters]] | date=6 May 2015 | access-date=7 May 2015}}</ref>

On 7 May, trade sources stated that merchant ships had been delayed weeks Yemen and in one case, following inspection and approval, a food supply ship was denied access. The food crisis increased to include over 20&nbsp;million people (80% of the population) going hungry.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/reu-yemen-conflict-delays-food-ships-backs-up-deliveries/2754190.html|title=Yemen Conflict Delays Food Ships, Backs Up Deliveries|publisher=[[Voice of America]] |access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref> Airstrikes destroyed a mine factory and a communications center. Local sources reported that 13 villagers were killed due to shelling near the border.<ref>{{cite news |author=Mohammed Ghobari |author2=Mohammed Mukhashaf |url=http://ca.reuters.com/article/topNews/idCAKBN0NT0H920150508|title=Saudi-led coalition bombs Houthis in north Yemen, offers five-day truce |work=[[Reuters]] |date=8 May 2015 |access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref>

On 18 May, HRW documented airstrikes that hit homes and markets and killed and wounded civilians. HRW documented the bombing of four markets.<ref name="hrw.org"/>
[[File:Waiting (17392342903).jpg|thumb|The conflict is exacerbating Yemen's [[water scarcity]], Sanaa, 21 May 2015]]
On 21 May, OCHA reported airstrikes that hit two farms adjacent to a humanitarian facility in Hajjah Governorate and resulted in civilian casualties. A warehouse containing humanitarian supplies was damaged in another strike. In Sa'adah City, satellite imagery analysis identified widespread damage to infrastructure with 1,171 structures affected, damaged or destroyed. The analysis showed that as of 17 May, 35 impact craters existed within the city, mostly along the runway of Sa'ada airport. Similar imagery of Aden identified 642 affected structures, including 327 destroyed. Local partners reported that 674 schools were forced to close in Sanaʽa, affecting 551,000 students.<ref name="reliefweb.int1"/>

Fuel prices increased by over 500% and food supplies by 80% since 26 March. The continued restrictions on the arrival of goods via air and sea ports, and insecurity on roads, restricted the delivery of essential supplies. In Sanaʽa, security concerns due to airstrikes prevented delivery of food assistance.

On 21 May, five Ethiopian migrants were killed and two others injured in an airstrike that hit open space 500 metres from an IOM-managed Migrant Response Centre. With continued conflict and import restrictions, Emergency (IPC Phase 4) outcomes were likely in the coming month. In six governorates, reports from OCHA partners show that basic food items are no longer available (Aden, Abyan, Al Dhale'e, Al Bayda, Lahj, Sa'ada).<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Yemen_OCHA%20Situation%20Report_22%20May%202015_EN_final.pdf |title=Yemen: Escalating Conflict Situation Report No. 8 |date= 22 May 2015 |publisher=[[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs]] |accessdate=25 February 2016}}</ref>

On 3 June, The Operations Room of the Ministry of Health in Sanaʽa was damaged. It manages emergency operations nationwide.<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-06-05_YDH">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Deteriorating Humanitarian Crisis Situation Report No. 10 (as of 3 June 2015) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=5 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-deteriorating-humanitarian-crisis-situation-report-no-10-3-june-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z5AqhkYJ?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-deteriorating-humanitarian-crisis-situation-report-no-10-3-june-2015 |archivedate=6 June 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report_No.10_EN_final.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z5COHSET?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report_No.10_EN_final.pdf |archivedate=6 June 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref>

On 5 June, ''The Washington Post'' reported that several Yemeni cultural and heritage strikes had been repeatedly targeted by Saudi airstrikes. Reports stated that Al-Qahira Castle, the 1,200-year-old al-Hadi Mosque and Dhamar Museum with over 12,500 artifacts<ref>{{cite news | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/27/opinion/yemeni-heritage-saudi-vandalism.html | newspaper=[[The New York Times]] | first=Lamya | last=Khalidi | title=Yemeni Heritage, Saudi Vandalism | date=26 June 2015}}</ref> were destroyed and the Great Dam of Marib was hit.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/worldviews/wp/2015/06/05/the-world-may-be-ignoring-the-destruction-of-cultural-treasures-in-yemen/|title=The world may be ignoring the destruction of cultural treasures in Yemen|last=Taylor|first=Adam|date=5 June 2015|work=[[The Washington Post]]|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

On 17 June, an OCHA report highlighted that food security had continued to worsen, with 19 out of 22 governorates now classified 'crisis' or 'emergency'. Half the population was 'food insecure' and nearly a quarter 'severely food insecure. A joint analysis of household food security by the UN [[Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations|Food and Agriculture Organization]] (FAO) WFP and the Ministry of Planning and International Cooperation in Yemen (MoPIC) found that Yemen was sliding into catastrophe. More than six million Yemenis were then in a Phase 4 Emergency, and nearly 6.9&nbsp;million people are in a Phase 3 Crisis: These figures indicate that Yemen was approaching a complete breakdown in food security and health.<ref name="UNOCHA20150617NAS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: New Analysis Shows Deepening Food Crisis – Crisis Update 40 – 17 June 2015 (1000hrs) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=17 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-new-analysis-shows-deepening-food-crisis-crisis-update-40-17-june-2015-1000hrs |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZOgdlJSG?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-new-analysis-shows-deepening-food-crisis-crisis-update-40-17-june-2015-1000hrs |archivedate=19 June 2015 |url-status=live}} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Crisis%20Update%20-%20No.%2040%20-%2017%20June%202015_%20Food_Crisis.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZOgq5sd8?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Crisis%20Update%20-%20No.%2040%20-%2017%20June%202015_%20Food_Crisis.pdf |archivedate=19 June 2015 |url-status=live}})</ref>
[[File:This textile factory was bombed in July leaving more than 1,300 people unemployed Many of the workers are now looking for work as day laborers Sanaa Yemen Nov-2015.jpg|thumb|An airstrike in Sanaʽa on a textile factory in July 2015 left more than 1,300 people unemployed (photo: [[Almigdad Mojalli|A. Mojalli]]/VOA, November 2015)<ref name="VOA_2015-12-10_FJD">{{cite news | first1=Heather |last1=Murdock |first2=Almigdad |last2=Mojalli |author2link=Almigdad Mojalli |title=Factories, Jobs Destroyed in Yemen War | publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=10 December 2015 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/factories-jobs-destroyed-yemen-war/3097676.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dhHzeeml?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/factories-jobs-destroyed-yemen-war/3097676.html |archivedate=11 December 2015 |url-status=live }} Cf.: {{cite news | first=Heather |last=Murdock |title=Factories, Jobs Destroyed in Yemen War |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/factories-jobs-destroyed-in-yemen-war/3097650.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dhIAb4g6?url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/factories-jobs-destroyed-in-yemen-war/3097650.html |archivedate=10 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>]]
[[File:Apartment building destroyed in 5-9-2015 in sana'a-2.jpg|thumb|Apartment building destroyed by a strike in Sanaa on 5 September 2015]]

On 26 July, the [[OCHA]] announced that airstrikes hit the residential complex of the Al Mukha Power Station in Al Mukha District, Taiz Governorate with health facilities reporting 55 deaths and 96 injuries and media reports as high as 120, all civilians.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Flash%20Update%20-%20No.%2042%20-%2027%20July%202015_%20Taizz%20Attacks.pdf |title=Yemen: Taizz airstrikes Crisi Update 42 | date= 26 July 2015 |publisher=[[ReliefWeb]] |accessdate=25 February 2016}}</ref>

On 27 August, the [[OCHA]] announced that airstrikes targeting that Al-Hudaydah port facilities late on 17 August and early 18 August had brought the port activities to a near halt and that the port was empty of all vessels and remained non-operational. A UN-chartered aid vessel carrying 2,230 MT of mixed food commodities left the port and was rerouted to Djibouti.<ref name="UNOCHA20150827YHB1">{{cite web |title=Yemen Humanitarian Bulletin No 1 – 27 August 2015 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=27 August 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-bulletin-no-1-27-august-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6b7wqkWna?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-bulletin-no-1-27-august-2015 |archivedate=28 August 2015 |url-status=live}} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Humanitarian%20Bulletin%20No%201%20-%2027%20August%202015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6b7x106Wl?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Humanitarian%20Bulletin%20No%201%20-%2027%20August%202015.pdf |archivedate=28 August 2015 |url-status=live}})</ref>

On 5 January 2016, an airstrike by the Saudi-led military coalition hit the Al Noor Center for Care and Rehabilitation of Blind, in the Safiah district of Sanaʽa,<ref name="news-vice-com_2016-01-05_SCB">{{cite news |last=Oakford |first=Samuel |title=The Saudi Coalition Bombed A Rehabilitation Center for Blind People in Yemen |publisher=[[Vice News]] |date=5 January 2016 |url=https://news.vice.com/article/saudi-arabia-bombed-a-rehabilitation-center-for-blind-people-in-yemen }}</ref><ref name="MEE_2016-01-05_YCF">{{cite web |last=MacDonald |first=Alex |title=Yemen centre for blind 'hit in Saudi coalition air raid' |publisher=[[Middle East Eye]] |date=5 January 2016 |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/saudi-led-coalition-airstrikes-reportedly-hit-centre-blind-yemen-capital-128298478 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eMrc6cDM?url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/saudi-led-coalition-airstrikes-reportedly-hit-centre-blind-yemen-capital-128298478 |archivedate=7 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="HRW_2016-01-13_HES">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Houthis Endangered School for Blind – Coalition Airstrike Shows Added Risks for People With Disabilities |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=13 January 2016 |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/01/13/yemen-houthis-endangered-school-blind |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eWrwHqs7?url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/01/13/yemen-houthis-endangered-school-blind |archivedate=14 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> the capital's only center, school, and home for people with visual disabilities.<ref name="HRW_2016-01-13_HES"/><ref name="VOA_2016-01-14_YCD"/> Five people were injured. Human Rights Watch and media reported, if the bomb had exploded, the damage would have been much worse.<ref name="HRW_2016-01-13_HES"/><ref name="VOA_2016-01-14_RGH"/> Human Rights Watch blamed both the Saudi-led coalition for hitting civilian targets and the Houthi militants battling the coalition. HRW said Houthi militants were partially to blame for using civilian sites for military purposes. Armed Houthis were stationed near the Al Noor center, putting the students at risk.<ref name="HRW_2016-01-13_HES"/><ref name="VOA_2016-01-14_YCD">{{cite news |last1=Murdock |first1=Heather |last2=Mojalli |first2=Almigdad |author2link=Almigdad Mojalli |title=Houthis and Saudi Coalition Put Students at Risk, Rights Group Says |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=14 January 2016 |url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/houtis-saudi-coalition-put-students-at-risk-rights-group-says/3146173.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ed9Nn2So?url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/houtis-saudi-coalition-put-students-at-risk-rights-group-says/3146173.html |archivedate=18 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="VOA_2016-01-14_RGH">{{cite news |last=Murdock |first=Heather |title=Rights Group: Houthis, Saudi Coalition Put Blind Students at Risk |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=14 January 2016 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/houthis-saudi-coalition-blind-students-airstrikes-human-rights-watch/3146193.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ed8rY3t2?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/houthis-saudi-coalition-blind-students-airstrikes-human-rights-watch/3146193.html |archivedate=18 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 20 April 2016 the UN General Assembly Security Council in a report covering the period January to December 2015 "verified a sixfold increase in the number of children killed and maimed compared with 2014, totalling 1,953 child casualties (785 children killed and 1,168 injured). More than 70 per cent were boys. Of the casualties, 60 per cent (510 deaths and 667 injuries) were attributed to the Saudi Arabia-led coalition."<ref>https://www.globalsecurity.org/military/library/report/2016/a-70-836.pdf page 27, paragraph 167</ref>

On 8 October 2016, airstrikes by Saudi-led coalition force kill 140 people and injuring 500 persons in one of the single worst death tolls in the two-year war. There are coalitions between Saudi Arabia and his allies in the subject. Also, the United Kingdom is under pressure for exporting Lucrative Arms and weapons to Saudi Arabia.<ref name="ReferenceC"/>

On 2 August 2018, ''The New York Times'' reported that at least 30 people were killed when the Saudi-led coalition air force hit a fish market, the entrance to the main hospital and a security compound.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2018/08/02/world/middleeast/yemen-saudi-hudaydah-missiles.html|title=Saudis Escalate Siege of Port in Yemen, Alarming Aid Groups|publisher=|newspaper=The New York Times|date=2 August 2018|last1=Kalfood|first1=Mohammed Ali|last2=Coker|first2=Margaret}}</ref>

On 9 August 2018, a [[Dahyan air strike|Saudi airstrike in Dahyan]] hit a school bus causing approximately 51 deaths. Many of these deaths were schoolchildren and other civilians.

On 8 October 2019, Yemen made an agreement to hand over Aden to Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20191008-yemen-imminent-agreement-to-hand-over-aden-to-saudi-arabia/|title=Yemen: Imminent agreement to hand over Aden to Saudi Arabia|date=8 October 2019|website=Middle East Monitor}}</ref>

On 7 February 2020, Yemeni hospitals were attacked, leaving more than thousands of civilians in need of immediate medical attention followed by a disrupted healthcare facility. The attack was a result of clashes between warring parties of Yemen; Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen and [[Houthis]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/02/1057101|title=Hospitals in Yemen attacked, disrupting healthcare for thousands of vulnerable civilians|accessdate=10 February 2020|website=UN News}}</ref> <ref>{{cite web|url=https://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Attacks%20on%20Marib%20hospitals%20limit%20medical%20services%20available%20to%20thousands%20of%20displaced%20people.pdf|title=Attacks on Marib hospitals limit medical services available to thousands of displaced people|accessdate=10 February 2020|website=Relief Web}}</ref>

=== Saada ===
Saada was the governorate of origin of 500,794 IDPs (out of 2,509,068 in total) as of December 2015.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-12-10_TFP6R"/>

On 18 April, an airstrike in Saada hit an Oxfam warehouse, damaging humanitarian supplies and killing at least one civilian. Aid groups widely condemned the strike.<ref name="oxfam">{{cite web |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/04/22/yemen-warehouse-strike-threatens-aid-delivery|title=Yemen: Warehouse Strike Threatens Aid Delivery|date=23 April 2015|publisher=Human Rights Watch}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.oxfam.org.uk/blogs/2015/04/yemen|title=Oxfam Condemns Coalition Bombing of a Warehouse Containing Vital Humanitarian Aid|publisher=Oxfam|date=20 April 2015}}</ref>

On 8 and 9 May 2015, large-scale displacement was reported in Saada to neighbouring areas, after the Saudi-led military coalition declared the entire Saada governorate a "military zone" and started heavy airstrikes.<ref name="UNOCHA_2015-11-22_2HNO"/><ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-06-12_YHN">{{cite web |title=2015 Yemen Humanitarian Needs Overview (Revised) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=12 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/2015-yemen-humanitarian-needs-overview-revised |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZEhTbAHW?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/2015-yemen-humanitarian-needs-overview-revised |archivedate=12 June 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Yemen%20Humanitarian%20Needs%20Overview%202015%20%28Revised%29.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZEj8snAn?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Yemen%20Humanitarian%20Needs%20Overview%202015%20(Revised).pdf |archivedate=12 June 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref> Around 70,000 people, including 28,000 children, fled from the Governorate of Sa'ada. The [[Save the Children]]'s Country Director in Yemen, Edward Santiago, said that many more were "largely unable to flee for safety because of the de facto blockade imposed by the coalition leading to severe fuel shortages".<ref name="STC_2015-05-10_AAC"/> On 9 May 2015, the U.N. Humanitarian Coordinator for Yemen, Johannes van der Klaauw, condemned the air strikes on Saada city as being in breach of international humanitarian law.<ref name="ReutersUS_2015-05-09_SLS"/><ref name="OCHAYemen_2015-05-09_SBH"/>

In August 2015 the [[Agency for Technical Cooperation and Development]] (ACTED) reported that "the crisis has taken an immeasurably heavy toll on civilians in this poor, rural governorate, causing death, injury and frequent damage and destruction of infrastructure."<ref name="ACTED_2015-08-10_AGS">{{cite web |title=A grave situation in Sa'ada: needs mount as access remains restricted |publisher=Agency for Technical Cooperation and Development (ACTED) |date=10 August 2015 |url=http://www.acted.org/fr/node/11537 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6agyrlq1s?url=http://www.acted.org/fr/node/11537 |archivedate=11 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In January 2016 the Houthi-controlled Saada area, including medical facilities run by Médecins Sans Frontières (MSF), received almost daily attacks. Michael Seawright, a Saada-based MSF project coordinator, said that they treated a high number of casualties, many with severe injuries. The Shiara hospital in Razeh District in Saada City, the only hospital with a trauma centre in the governorate of Saada and in most of northern Yemen, was hit on 10 January, and several people were killed, including medical personnel. MSF had been working in the facility since November 2015.<ref name="MSF_2016-01-27_IHN">{{cite web |first=Michael |last=Seawright |title=Yemen: 'I Have Never Seen Such Destruction' |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières |date=27 January 2016 |url=http://www.doctorswithoutborders.org/article/yemen-i-have-never-seen-such-destruction |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6es60YQCn?url=http://www.doctorswithoutborders.org/article/yemen-i-have-never-seen-such-destruction?utm_source=feedburner&utm_medium=feed&utm_campaign=Feed:+DoctorsWithoutBordersPR+(Doctors+Without+Borders/Médecins+Sans+Frontières+Press+Releases) |archivedate=28 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="MSF_2016-01-10_Upd-01-11_Upd-01-17_AMS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Another MSF-supported hospital bombed – Update – As of 11 January, the death toll has risen to five |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières |date=10 January 2016 |url=http://www.msf.org/article/yemen-another-msf-supported-hospital-bombed |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eScA1UiM?url=http://www.msf.org/article/yemen-another-msf-supported-hospital-bombed |archivedate=11 January 2016 |url-status=live }} (Update: 11 January 2016); Cf.: {{cite web |title=MSF-Supported Hospital Bombed in Northern Yemen – Update January 11, 2016 |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières |date=10 January 2016 |url=http://www.doctorswithoutborders.org/article/msf-supported-hospital-bombed-northern-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6es83Fil0?url=http://www.doctorswithoutborders.org/article/msf-supported-hospital-bombed-northern-yemen |archivedate=28 January 2016 |url-status=live }} (Update: 11 January 2016) and {{cite web |title=MSF-supported hospital bombed in Yemen: death toll rises to six |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières |date=10 January 2016 |url=http://www.msf.org/article/msf-supported-hospital-bombed-yemen-death-toll-rises-six |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ehi64cIY?url=http://www.msf.org/article/msf-supported-hospital-bombed-yemen-death-toll-rises-six |archivedate=21 January 2016 |url-status=live }} (Update: 17 January 2016)</ref>

=== Sanaʽa ===
457.502 IDPs (out of 2,509,068 in total) originated from Sanaʽa Governorate and Sanaʽa city as of December 2015.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-12-10_TFP6R"/>

After the Old City of Sanaʽa was heavily bombed in May 2015, causing severe damage to many of its historic buildings, Director-General of UNESCO, Irina Bokova, said "I am particularly distressed by the news concerning air strikes on heavily populated areas such as the cities of Sanaʽa and Saa'dah."<ref name="whc-unesco-org_2015-05-12_UDC">{{cite web |title=UNESCO Director-General calls on all parties to protect Yemen's cultural heritage |publisher=UNESCO World Heritage Convention |date=12 May 2015 |url=http://whc.unesco.org/en/news/1278 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YgrRppBp?url=http://whc.unesco.org/en/news/1278 |archivedate=21 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Following a surge in aerial bombing raids in the Old City of Sanaʽa in June 2015, the UN warned, that the country's extensive archaeological and historic heritage had been increasingly under threat.<ref name="un-org_2015-06-16_URU">{{cite web |title=Yemen: UN reports uptick in civilian deaths as fighting in country continues |publisher=UN News Centre |date=16 June 2015 |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51161 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZLnaXJWV?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51161 |archivedate=17 June 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> In July 2015, the Old City of Sanaʽa, which had sustained serious damage due to armed conflict, was added to List of World Heritage in Danger.<ref name="whc-unesco-org_2015-07-02_YOC">{{cite web |title=Yemen's Old City of Sana'a and Old Walled City of Shibam added to List of World Heritage in Danger |publisher=UNESCO World Heritage Centre |date=2 July 2015 |url=http://whc.unesco.org/en/news/1310/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZjPCv2LR?url=http://whc.unesco.org/en/news/1310/ |archivedate=2 July 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 6 September 2015, Al Sabaeen paediatric hospital in Sanaʽa had to be evacuated after a nearby airstrike. The United Nations' Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs (UN-OCHA) described the event as "a severe blow to a tattered health system".<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-09-14_HBY2">{{cite web |title=Humanitarian Bulletin – Yemen – Issue 2 – 13 September 2015 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=14 September 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20YEMEN%20HUMANITARIAN%20BULLETIN%20-14%20September.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6bd2xfIWq?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20YEMEN%20HUMANITARIAN%20BULLETIN%20-14%20September.pdf |archivedate=18 September 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> Before its closure the Al Sabaeen paediatric hospital—standing amid bombed out buildings in the center of Sanaʽa—had been the primary paediatric hospital in the area.<ref name="savethechildren-org_2015-08-30_LYH">{{cite web |title=Key Yemen Hospital on the Brink of Closure as Airstrikes Intensify on Sana'a |publisher=Save the Children |date=30 August 2015 |url=http://www.savethechildren.org/site/apps/nlnet/content2.aspx?c=8rKLIXMGIpI4E&b=9241341&ct=14757311¬oc=1 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6bBrVVAoW?url=http://www.savethechildren.org/site/apps/nlnet/content2.aspx?c=8rKLIXMGIpI4E&b=9241341&ct=14757311&notoc=1 |archivedate=31 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> "Before the crisis it had a catchment population of about 300,000; but, since the crisis that number has risen to almost 3 million, with the entire governorate reliant on it for specialist care," said [[Save the Children]] spokesperson Mark Kaye.<ref name="savethechildren-org_2015-08-30_LYH"/><ref name="voanews-com_2015-09-02_YOB">{{cite news | first=Henry |last=Ridgwell |title=Yemen 'on Brink of Disaster' as Medical Shortages Soar |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=2 September 2015 |url=http://www.voanews.com/content/yemen-on-brink-of-disaster-as-medical-shortages-soar/2942612.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cuRYhNW6?url=http://www.voanews.com/content/yemen-on-brink-of-disaster-as-medical-shortages-soar/2942612.html |archivedate=9 November 2015 |url-status=live }} Cf.: {{cite news | first=Henry |last=Ridgwell |title=Yemen 'on Brink of Disaster' as Medical Shortages Soar |publisher=[[Voice of America]] |date=2 September 2015 |url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/2942599.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cuRLHt9I?url=http://www.voanews.com/media/video/2942599.html |archivedate=9 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

A joint report by the UK-based charity Action on Armed Violence (AOAV) and the UN-OCHA, that concluded that airstrikes were responsible for 60 percent of civilian casualties in the first seven months of 2015,<ref name="theintercept-com_2015-11-16_AOS">{{cite web | first=Iona |last=Craig |authorlink=Iona Craig |title=The Agony of Saada – U.S. and Saudi Bombs Target Yemen's Ancient Heritage |website=[[The Intercept]] |date=16 November 2015 |url=https://theintercept.com/2015/11/16/u-s-and-saudi-bombs-target-yemens-ancient-heritage/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dD0UOYGl?url=https://theintercept.com/2015/11/16/u-s-and-saudi-bombs-target-yemens-ancient-heritage/ |archivedate=21 November 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="OCHAuAOAV_2015-09-22_EWY">{{cite web |first=Robert |last=Perkins |title=State of Crisis: Explosive Weapons in Yemen |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, Action on Armed Violence |date=22 September 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/state-crisis-explosive-weapons-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ccovcJy1?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/state-crisis-explosive-weapons-yemen |archivedate=28 October 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=https://aoav.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/State-of-Crisis.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ccp1yzOn?url=https://aoav.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/State-of-Crisis.pdf?utm_source=AOAV+Default&utm_campaign=c00a9a63d9-AOAV-OCHA&utm_medium=email&utm_term=0_25220d1bac-c00a9a63d9-106874805 |archivedate=28 October 2015 |url-status=live }}, {{cite web |title=original PDF |url=https://aoav.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/State-of-Crisis.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cw53MFEt?url=https://aoav.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/State-of-Crisis.pdf |archivedate=10 November 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref> came to the result, that more than half (53 per cent) of the reported civilian toll was recorded in Sanaʽa and surrounding districts.<ref name="UNOCHA_2015-09-29_YHB3">{{cite web | title=Yemen Humanitarian Bulletin No 3 – 29 September 2015 [EN/AR] |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=29 September 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-bulletin-no-3-29-september-2015-enar |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cw49t52p?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-bulletin-no-3-29-september-2015-enar |archivedate=10 November 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA_Yemen_Humanitarian_Bulletin_Issue_3-29_Sept2015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cw4OMhlO?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA_Yemen_Humanitarian_Bulletin_Issue_3-29_Sept2015.pdf |archivedate=10 November 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref>

On 7 January 2016, HRW reported and condemned that the Saudi Arabia-led coalition forces had used cluster bombs on residential areas of Sanaa on 6 January.<ref name="HRW_2016-01-07_CDC">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Coalition Drops Cluster Bombs in Capital – Indiscriminate Weapon Used in Residential Areas |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=7 January 2016 |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/01/07/yemen-coalition-drops-cluster-bombs-capital-0 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eMMxYX3X?url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/01/07/yemen-coalition-drops-cluster-bombs-capital-0 |archivedate=7 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 8 January the United Nations warned that their use could be a war crime.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="RTS_2016-01-08_UCB"/><ref name="UNNewsService_2016-01-08_UCD">{{cite news |title=UN chief 'deeply concerned' about intensification of airstrikes and ground fighting in Yemen |publisher=UN News Service |date=8 January 2016 |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=52966 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eP9o9I8Y?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=52966 |archivedate=9 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="un-org_2016-01-08_SAS">{{cite web |title=Statement attributable to the Spokesman for the Secretary-General on Yemen |publisher=United Nations |date=8 January 2016 |url=https://www.un.org/sg/statements/index.asp?nid=9372 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ePAjdf3a?url=http://www.un.org/sg/statements/index.asp?nid=9372 |archivedate=9 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> The UN Secretary-General Ban Ki-moon said he was "particularly concerned about reports of intense airstrikes in residential areas and on civilian buildings in Sanaʽa, including the Chamber of Commerce, a wedding hall and a centre for the blind".<ref name="un-org_2016-01-08_SAS"/><ref name="business-standard-com_2015-12-21_UWC">{{cite news |title=UN warns cluster bomb use in Yemen may amount to war crime |newspaper=[[Business Standard]] |date=9 January 2016 |agency=AFP |url=http://www.business-standard.com/article/pti-stories/un-warns-cluster-bomb-use-in-yemen-may-amount-to-war-crime-116010900011_1.html |access-date=21 December 2015 }}</ref>

=== Internally Displaced Persons (IDP) ===
[[File:Yemen IDPs crisis-en.jpg|thumb|400px|Development of the number of IDPs and IDP returnees (January 2010 – June 2018)<ref name="Weltbank_2016-01_EEW">{{cite book |last1=Devarajan |first1=Shanta publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, UN Country Team in Yemen | archivedate=22 April 2017 | date=November 2016 | url-status=dead | df=dmy-all }}''</ref>]]
In April and May 2015 mass displacement was observed primarily in Saada, Amran and Hajjah governorates as airstrikes and shelling intensified in the north of Yemen.<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-06-12_YHN"/>

On 13 April, OCHA reported that (as of 11 April) more than 120,000 people were estimated to have been [[internally displaced person|internally displaced]] since 26 March 2015.<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-04-13_ECF">{{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/flash%20update%20-%2013%20April%202015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YZc5dNUG?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/flash%20update%20-%2013%20April%202015.pdf |archivedate=16 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 17 May the UN, citing Yemen's health services, said that as of 15 May 545,000 had been internally displaced because of the war,<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-05-17_HPS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Humanitarian Pause, Situation Report No. 4 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=17 May 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-pause-situation-report-no-4 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YcEm7vdy?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-pause-situation-report-no-4 |archivedate=18 May 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report%20No.%204%20on%20the%20Humanitarian%20Pause%20-%2016%20May%202015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YcF6EZQl?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report%20No.%204%20on%20the%20Humanitarian%20Pause%20-%2016%20May%202015.pdf |archivedate=18 May 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref><ref name="AFP_2015-05-19_ESH"/> up from 450,000 announced on 15 May 2015.<ref name="AFP_2015-05-19_ESH">{{cite news |last1=al-Jabiri |first1=Jamal |last2=al-Haidari |first2=Fawaz |title=UN says half a million Yemenis displaced as capital pounded |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=19 May 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/un-says-half-million-yemenis-displaced-capital-pounded |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YeDvt9ue?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/un-says-half-million-yemenis-displaced-capital-pounded |archivedate=19 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="unhcr-org_2015-05-15_UFE">{{cite web |title=First UN flights brings emergency aid to Yemen |publisher=UNHCR |date=15 May 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/first-un-flights-brings-emergency-aid-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YbNnt6uF?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/first-un-flights-brings-emergency-aid-yemen |archivedate=17 May 2015 |url-status=live }} (original URL: http://www.unhcr.org/55561d7b9.html)</ref><ref name="AFP_2015-05-17_HRA">{{cite news |title=Huthi rebels absent as Yemeni parties gather in Riyadh |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=17 May 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/huthi-rebels-absent-yemeni-parties-gather-riyadh |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YbMKP3tm?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/huthi-rebels-absent-yemeni-parties-gather-riyadh |archivedate=17 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 1 June, the UN announced that 1,019,762 people had been internally displaced as of 28 May 2015.<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-06-01_YHS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Humanitarian Snapshot – Displacement (as of 31 May 2015) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=1 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-snapshot-displacement-31-may-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z3gt6Hbp?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-snapshot-displacement-31-may-2015 |archivedate=5 June 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/IDP%20Humanitarian%20Snapshot_31May2015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z3hAAgbk?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/IDP%20Humanitarian%20Snapshot_31May2015.pdf |archivedate=5 June 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref><ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-06-04_YRI">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Rapid Increase in Casualties, Displacement and Scale of Destruction Flash Update 38 – 4 June 2015 (1000hrs) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=4 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-rapid-increase-casualties-displacement-and-scale-destruction-flash-update-38-4 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z3bcK42F?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-rapid-increase-casualties-displacement-and-scale-destruction-flash-update-38-4 |archivedate=5 June 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/ocha_yemen_flash_update_-_no._38_-_4_june_2015_final.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Z3bzpu5M?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/ocha_yemen_flash_update_-_no._38_-_4_june_2015_final.pdf |archivedate=5 June 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref>

On 6 July the UN announced that as of 2 July there were 1,267,590 internally displaced people in Yemen.<ref name="UN-OCHA_2015-07-06_YHS">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Humanitarian Emergency Situation Report No. 14 (as of 6 July 2015) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=6 July 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-emergency-situation-report-no-14-6-july-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZrcwNZe2?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-humanitarian-emergency-situation-report-no-14-6-july-2015 |archivedate=8 July 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report%20No.%2014%20-issued%20on%207%20July%202015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZrdHrree?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Situation%20Report%20No.%2014%20-issued%20on%207%20July%202015.pdf |archivedate=8 July 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref>

On 5 August, a task force of the Global Protection Cluster announced their estimate of 1,439,118 internally displaced persons from more than 250,000 households in Yemen.<ref name="UN-OCHA_UNHCR_2015-08-05_YPC">{{cite web |title=Yemen Protection Cluster:Task Force on Population Movements 4th Report, 05th August 2015 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, UN High Commissioner for Refugees, Protection Cluster |date=5 August 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-protection-clustertask-force-population-movements-4th-report-05th-august-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6apNDZeCk?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-protection-clustertask-force-population-movements-4th-report-05th-august-2015 |archivedate=16 August 2015 |url-status=live }} {{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/TFPM%204th%20TFPM%20report%20-%2005%20August%202015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6apNPURMU?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/TFPM%204th%20TFPM%20report%20-%2005%20August%202015.pdf |archivedate=16 August 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 15 October the IOM-UNHCR displacement-tracking mechanism published new data showing in the 5th RFPM report that the IDP population had reached 2,305,048 people.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-10-14_TFP5R">{{cite web |title=Task Force on Population Movement, 5th Report, 14 October 2015 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, UN High Commissioner for Refugees, Protection Cluster |date=14 October 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/task-force-population-movement-5th-report-14-october-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cgVwlh6t?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/task-force-population-movement-5th-report-14-october-2015 |archivedate=31 October 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=original on humanitarianresponse.info |url=https://www.humanitarianresponse.info/en/system/files/documents/files/tfpm_5th_report_-_14_oct_2015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cgW2E0oA?url=https://www.humanitarianresponse.info/en/system/files/documents/files/tfpm_5th_report_-_14_oct_2015.pdf |archivedate=31 October 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref><ref name="UNHCR_2015-10-27_DCR">{{cite web |title=Briefing Note: Despite conflict, refugees continue to arrive by boat in Yemen |publisher=UN High Commissioner for Refugees |date=27 October 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/briefing-note-despite-conflict-refugees-continue-arrive-boat-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cdJudc9r?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/briefing-note-despite-conflict-refugees-continue-arrive-boat-yemen |archivedate=29 October 2015 |url-status=live }}, original: http://www.unhcr.org/562f6bba6.html unhcr.org</ref>

The 6th RFPM report (published on 10 December 2015) gave a figure of 2,509,068 internally displaced persons.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-12-10_TFP6R"/> Much of the increase from the previous report, published in October, could be attributed to improved tracking methods.<ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-12-10_TFP6R">{{cite web |title=Task Force on Population Movement, 6th Report, 10 December 2015 |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs, UN High Commissioner for Refugees, Protection Cluster |date=10 December 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/task-force-population-movement-6th-report-10-december-2015 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dnRaxQyv?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/task-force-population-movement-6th-report-10-december-2015 |archivedate=15 December 2015 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=PDF |url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/tfpm_6th_report_10_december_2015.pdf |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6dnRv5N9M?url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/tfpm_6th_report_10_december_2015.pdf |archivedate=15 December 2015 |url-status=live }})</ref><ref name="OCHA_UNHCR_PC_2015-10-14_TFP5R"/>

===Starvation and diseases===
{{See also|Famine in Yemen}}
[[File:100 Blockades (39025204441).jpg|thumb|"Let Yemen Live" protest at US and Saudi missions to the [[United Nations|UN]], New York City, December 2017]]
On 14 June 2015, OCHA reported a large outbreak of [[Dengue fever]] that killed over 113 people and infected over 4,000. Patients could not be treated due to lack of water in affected areas. OCHA was also investigating reports of a [[Measles]] outbreak. Health officials considered the breakdown in health services, including decrease in immunization coverage, closure of health facilities and difficulty in accessing health services as possible contributing factors.<ref name="UNOCHA20150614PHC">{{cite web |title=Yemen: Public Health Crisis Escalates Flash Update 39 – 14 June 2015 (1000hrs) |publisher=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs |date=14 June 2015 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-public-health-crisis-escalates-flash-update-39-14-june-2015-1000hrs |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6ZJ4rROwb?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-public-health-crisis-escalates-flash-update-39-14-june-2015-1000hrs |archivedate=15 June 2015 |url-status=live}} ([http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/OCHA%20Yemen%20Flash%20Update%20-%20No.%2039%20-%2014%20June%202015_%20Public_Health_Crisis.pdf PDF])</ref>

In June 2015, Oxfam's humanitarian programme manager in Sanaa said that Saudi-led [[blockade|naval blockade]] "means it's impossible to bring anything into the country. There are lots of ships, with basic things like flour, that are not allowed to approach. The situation is deteriorating, hospitals are now shutting down, without diesel. People are dying of simple diseases."<ref name="auto"/>

On 1 July 2015, the UN announced that Yemen was at the highest level of humanitarian disaster with over 80% of the population needing help. UN agencies agreed to classify Yemen as a level 3 emergency as the UN Envoy for Yemen stated that Yemen is one step away from famine.<ref>{{cite news | url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/07/01/world/middleeast/ap-un-united-nations-yemen-humanitarian.html | newspaper=[[The New York Times]] | title=UN Declares Highest-Level Humanitarian Emergency in Yemen | date=1 July 2015}}</ref>

In February 2016, the OCHA reported that 21 million people (85% of the population) were in need of some form of humanitarian assistance, 7.6&nbsp;million people were "severely" food insecure, and that more than 3.4&nbsp;million children were not attending school.<ref name="AJE catastrophe"/>

On 4 October 2016, the UN children's agency [[UNICEF]] said 1.5&nbsp;million children in Yemen suffer of [[malnutrition]], including 370,000 enduring very severe malnutrition.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/oct/04/yemen-famine-feared-as-starving-children-fight-for-lives-in-hospital |title=Yemen famine feared as starving children fight for lives in hospital |work=[[The Guardian]]|date=4 October 2016}}</ref>

In October 2016, health authorities in Yemen confirmed a [[cholera]] [[2017 Yemen cholera outbreak|outbreak]] in Sanaa and Taiz.<ref>[https://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/decries-cholera-outbreak-yemen-42650112 "UN Decries Cholera Outbreak in Yemen"]. [[ABC News]]. 7 October 2016.</ref> In June 2017, cholera cases passed 100,000 with 798 deaths in the country. The water and sanitation systems are largely inoperable<ref>{{cite news|title=Yemen cholera cases pass 100,000 amid 'unprecedented' epidemic|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-40200017 |work=BBC News |date=8 June 2017 |accessdate=9 June 2017}}</ref> Numerous international humanitarian organisations have pointed to the Saudi-led naval and aerial blockade and bombing campaign as central causes behind the preventable cholera epidemic.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Federspiel |first1=Frederik |last2=Ali |first2=Mohammad |title=The cholera outbreak in Yemen: lessons learned and way forward |journal=BMC Public Health |date=4 December 2018 |volume=18 |issue=1 |pages=1338 |doi=10.1186/s12889-018-6227-6 |pmid=30514336 |pmc=6278080 |issn=1471-2458}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Bachman |first1=Jeffrey S. |title=A 'synchronised attack' on life: the Saudi-led coalition's 'hidden and holistic' genocide in Yemen and the shared responsibility of the US and UK |journal=Third World Quarterly |date=1 February 2019 |volume=40 |issue=2 |pages=298–316 |doi=10.1080/01436597.2018.1539910 |s2cid=159170998 |issn=0143-6597}}</ref>

{{Quote|text=With the right medicines, these [diseases] are all completely treatable – but the Saudi Arabia-led coalition is stopping them from getting in.|author=Grant Pritchard, [[Save the Children]]'s interim country director for Yemen, April 2017 |source=[[Vice News]]<ref>{{cite web|author=Subscribe |url=https://news.vice.com/story/saudi-arabia-donates-to-end-yemen-cholera-outbreak-it-helped-start |title=Saudi Arabia donates millions to end Yemen cholera outbreak it helped start – VICE News |publisher=News.vice.com |date=2017-06-08 |accessdate=2018-04-24}}</ref>}}

More than 50,000 children in Yemen died from starvation in 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/nov/16/lift-yemen-blockade-to-save-children-un-agencies-tell-saudis|title=Saudis must lift Yemen blockade or 'untold' thousands will die, UN agencies warn|first=Patrick Wintour Diplomatic|last=editor|date=16 November 2017 |newspaper=The Guardian}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.chicagotribune.com/news/nationworld/ct-save-the-children-yemen-20171116-story.html|title=50,000 children in Yemen have died of starvation and disease so far this year, monitoring group says|first=Associated|last=Press|work=Chicago Tribune |date=16 November 2017}}</ref> The number rose to 85,000 as of December 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2018/12/yemen-head-mission-monitoring-hodeidah-ceasefire-arrives-181222111535539.html|title=Yemen: Head of UN mission monitoring Hodeidah ceasefire arrives|website=www.aljazeera.com}}</ref> The [[famine]] in Yemen is the direct result of the Saudi Arabian-led intervention and [[blockade of Yemen]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2017/08/31/opinion/columnists/yemen-famine-cholera.html|title=The Photos the U.S. and Saudi Arabia Don't Want You to See|first=Nicholas|last=Kristof|date=31 August 2017|newspaper=The New York Times}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/investigates/special-report/yemen-saudi-blockade/|title=Saudi de facto blockade starves Yemen of food and medicine|website=Reuters|date=11 October 2017}}</ref> In December 2017, the ''Guardian'' reported: "Data on coalition airstrikes collected by the Yemen Data Project have recorded 356 air raids targeting farms, 174 targeting market places and 61 air raids targeting food storage sites from March 2015 to the end of September 2017."<ref>{{cite news |title=Bombed into famine: how Saudi air campaign targets Yemen's food supplies |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/dec/12/bombed-into-famine-how-saudi-air-campaign-targets-yemens-food-supplies |work=The Guardian |date=12 December 2017}}</ref>

According to the [[United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs|OCHA]]'s March 2019 report, 108,889 suspected cholera and acute watery diarrhea cases were reported between January and mid-March, with one third cases of children below 5 five years. Around 190 people died in the mentioned period.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/Yemen_Humanitarian_Update_no5_FINAL.pdf|title=YEMEN HUMANITARIAN UPDATE|publisher=OCHA}}</ref> In August 2016, a Joint Incidents Assessment Team was formed by the coalition parties to investigate alleged laws of war violations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/report/2018/08/24/hiding-behind-coalition/failure-credibly-investigate-and-provide-redress-unlawful|title=Hiding Behind the Coalition|publisher=Human Rights Watch|accessdate=24 August 2018}}</ref> But the team failed to meet international standards regarding transparency, impartiality, and independence. It failed to investigate and apply human rights law in the civil war and instead acted as a shield against the parties accountable for the war.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2019/04/01/why-congress-must-act-now-yemen|title=Why Congress Must Act Now on Yemen|publisher=Human Rights Watch|accessdate=1 April 2019}}</ref>

== Operation costs ==
In December 2015, David Ottaway, a senior scholar at the [[Woodrow Wilson International Center for Scholars|Wilson Center]] in Washington, estimated the Saudi-led military coalition was spending $200&nbsp;million a day on military operations in Yemen. His sources speculate that the Saudis are supplying most of the funding.<ref name="bloomberg-com_2015-12-21_STO">{{cite news |last=Carey |first=Glen |title=The Saudi Town on the Frontline of Yemen's War |publisher=[[Bloomberg News]] |date=21 December 2015 |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-12-21/in-one-saudi-town-gunfire-all-day-brings-yemen-war-near-home |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6eor0bdcl?url=http://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-12-21/in-one-saudi-town-gunfire-all-day-brings-yemen-war-near-home |archivedate=26 January 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 20 October 2020, State Secretariat for Economic Affairs (Seco) published a report that Swiss companies exported war material to the value of almost 690 million francs. According to this report Saudi Arabia, currently involved in a conflict in Yemen bought war material from Switzerland for 3.8 million francs.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thelocal.ch/20201020/swiss-weapons-exports-up-38-percent-despite-pandemic|title= Swiss weapons exports up 38 percent despite pandemic|accessdate=20 October 2020|website=The Local}}</ref>

== Responses ==

=== In Yemen ===

==== Opposition ====
[[File:Ali Abdullah Saleh-2.jpg|thumb|140px|Yemen's former president [[Ali Abdullah Saleh]] was initially allied with Houthis, until they assassinated him on accounts of treason.]]
Following the call by the leader of the Houthi movement, [[Abdul-Malik al-Houthi]], tens of thousands Yemenis of various socioeconomic backgrounds took to the streets of the rebel-controlled capital, Sanaʽa, to voice their anger at the Saudi intervention.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/03/coalition-jets-continue-hit-houthi-targets-yemen-150327022702372.html|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]]|title=Coalition jets continue to hit Houthi targets in Yemen|date=27 March 2015|access-date=27 March 2015}}</ref>

On 21 April 2015, representatives of 19 Yemeni political parties and associations rejected UN Resolution 2216, stating that it encouraged terrorist expansion, intervened in Yemen's sovereign affairs, violated Yemen's right of self-defence and emphasized the associations' support of the Yemeni Army.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.khabaragency.net/news24649.html|title=اليمن.. 19 حزباً سياسياً يعلنون رفض قرار مجلس الأمن رقم 2216|work=وكالة خبر للأنباء|access-date=26 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.alwatanvoice.com/arabic/news/2015/04/21/702251.html|title=احزاب سياسيه يمنية تعلن رفضها لقرار مجلس الامن رقم (2216)|website=دنيا الوطن}}</ref>

On 23 April, a spokesman for the Houthis said UN-sponsored peace talks should continue, but only following "a complete halt of attacks" by the coalition.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/04/22/middleeast/yemen-crisis/|title=Amid Saudi Arabia's airstrikes in Yemen, Houthis call for peace talks|date=23 April 2015|publisher=CNN}}</ref>

In a televised address on 24 April, Saleh called on the Houthis and other armed groups to withdraw from the territory they had seized and participate in UN-sponsored peace talks, in exchange for an end to the air campaign.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32458774 |title=Yemen conflict: Ex-leader Saleh appeals to Houthi allies |date=24 April 2015 |work=BBC News }}</ref> Exiled Yemeni Foreign Minister rejected the peace proposal saying that Saleh had no role in the talks.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/26/yemen-security-yaseen-idUSL8N0XN0OJ20150426|title=Yemen minister rejects peace talks call from ex-president|work=[[Reuters]] | date=26 April 2015}}</ref>

On 26 April, the General Authority for Archeology and Museums in Yemen condemned attacks targeting historical sites. The statement highlighted an attack that completely destroyed an ancient fortress in the [[Damt District]] of the [[Ad Dali' Governorate]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://almashhad-alyemeni.com/news51536.html|title=استنكار شعبي واسع استهداف الاماكن والمواقع التاريخية في اليمن – المشهد اليمني|publisher=almashhad-alyemeni.com}}</ref> Yemeni political parties issued a letter to UN Secretary-General [[Ban Ki-moon]] requesting that he continue the peace talks. The letter emphasized that Yemen was still under attack by air, land and sea and that the existing blockade was increasing the humanitarian crisis and that education had been denied for 3 million students due to the "random attacks".<ref>{{cite web |url=http://almashhad-alyemeni.com/news51534.html|title=أحزاب ومكونات سياسية يمنية توجه رسالة لأمين عام الامم المتحدة – المشهد اليمني|publisher=almashhad-alyemeni.com}}</ref>

On 2 May 2015, the Yemenis Forum of Persons With Disability stated that 300 centres and organizations had been forced to stop operations following the intervention. The organization denounced the air and sea blockade that "increased the suffering of the disabled greatly".<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.sabanews.net/ar/news394971.htm|title=Saba Net :: سبأ نت|publisher=sabanews.net}}</ref> The same day Hussein al-Ezzi, the Houthi head of foreign relations, sent a letter addressed to Secretary General Ban seeking an end to the "unjustified Saudi aggression".<ref>{{cite web |title=Houthis ask UN to stop Saudi airstrikes in Yemen|url=http://www.albawaba.com/news/houthis-ask-un-stop-saudi-airstrikes-yemen-689506|date=3 May 2015 |website=Al Bawaba|access-date=3 May 2015}}</ref> He asked the UN to seek an end to what Houthis described as blatant aggression against the country.<ref name="end">{{cite news |last= Abdullah|first=Khaled |title=Yemeni Houthis call on U.N. to end Saudi strikes: statement|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/02/us-yemen-saudi-war-idUSKBN0NN0OY20150502|date=2 May 2015 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>

On 7 May, 17 humanitarian agencies stressed that life-saving aid would run out in a week and emphasized the need to remove the existing blockade. The International Non-Government Organizations Forum in Yemen appealed for allowing basic materials to enter the country immediately.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.sabanews.net/en/news395278.htm|title=Agencies warn of risk of preventing aid arrival to Yemen|agency=[[Saba News Agency]] |access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref>

On 10 May, Houthi military spokesman Sharaf Luqman welcomed the Russian initiative, which advocated a suspension of military operations and also lifting the blockade.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://news.videonews.us/yemens-houthis-welcome-proposed-russian-truce-0912861.html|title=Yemen's Houthis welcome proposed Russian truce|last=Tezelden|first=Alim|publisher=Video News |access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref>

On 26 March 2017, the second anniversary of the war, over a hundred thousand Houthi supporters demonstrated in Sanaa protesting the Saudi aggression and expressing solidarity.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-protests/thousands-of-yemenis-rally-in-sanaa-on-wars-second-anniversary-idUSKBN16X0R9|title=Thousands of Yemenis rally in Sanaa on war's second anniversary|author=Editorial|work=Reuters |access-date=29 June 2018}}</ref>

==== Support ====
[[File:Secretary Kerry Shakes Hands With Yemeni President Hadi Before Bilateral Meeting in Saudi Arabia (17212641020).jpg|thumb|Yemen's President [[Abdrabbuh Mansur Hadi]] in Riyadh, Saudi Arabia, 7 May 2015]]
Anti-Houthi groups, especially Sunnis, while supporting the intervention did not wish for the return to power of Hadi, since they viewed him as the man "who ceded control of the capital without a fight six months ago".<ref>[https://www.economist.com/news/middle-east-and-africa/21647362-saudi-arabia-starts-bombing-its-southern-neighbour-riyadh-enters-fray "War in Yemen: Riyadh enters the fray"], ''The Economist''.</ref>
