On 3 April, the Al-Islah party, the Yemeni branch of the Muslim Brotherhood, declared its support for the campaign.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/yemens-houthis-quit-aden-palace-after-saudi-strikes-2092238263|publisher=[[Middle East Eye]]|date=3 April 2015|title=Yemen's Houthis quit Aden palace after Saudi strikes}}</ref> Supporters of the party reportedly suffered consequences, including kidnappings and raids, as a result of this declaration.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/yemen-rebels-stage-raids-on-suspected-opponents/2015/04/05/1e785854-db19-11e4-bf0b-f648b95a6488_story.html|title=Yemen rebels stage raids on suspected opponents amid Saudi-led airstrikes|date=5 April 2015|work=[[The Washington Post]]|first=Ali|last=al-Mujahed}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/saudi-led-bombing-campaign-deepens-rifts-yemen-1264640346|title=Saudi-led bombing campaign deepens rifts in Yemen|date=10 April 2015|publisher=[[Middle East Eye]]}}</ref>

On 26 April, the foreign minister in Hadi's government, Riad Yaseen, rejected Saleh's calls for UN-sponsored peace talks on the ground.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/26/us-yemen-security-yaseen-idUSKBN0NH0NL20150426|title=Yemeni foreign minister rejects peace talks call from ex-president|date=26 April 2015 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>

=== Saudi Arabia ===

==== Opposition ====
On 5 April a firefight broke out between anti-government Shiite rioters and security forces in Saudi Arabia's [[Shia Islam in Saudi Arabia|Shiite-minority]] in Eastern Province, with one police officer killed and three others injured.<ref>{{cite news |title=Police officer killed in security raids on Saudi Arabia's Eastern Province|url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/security-forces-raid-saudi-arabias-eastern-province-stop-anti-yemen-war-protests-451186533|quote=One police officer was killed and three others injured on Sunday in Saudi Arabia's Eastern Province, as government forces clashed with locals, according to a Ministry of Interior statement.}}</ref> The firefight broke out after calls in the Eastern Province to protest against the military intervention.<ref>{{cite news |title=Police officer killed in security raids on Saudi Arabia's Eastern Province|url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/security-forces-raid-saudi-arabias-eastern-province-stop-anti-yemen-war-protests-451186533|quote=The latest round of clashes in Awamiyah on Sunday came after calls in the province for protests against Saudi Arabia's military intervention in Yemen, where Riyadh is battling to push back Shiite Houthi rebels who have expanded their powerbase to the capital Sanaa and beyond, forcing the sitting president into exile.}}</ref>

On 29 April, King [[Salman of Saudi Arabia|Salman]] dismissed his appointed [[crown prince]], [[Muqrin of Saudi Arabia]]. Some regional political analysts speculated that the decision was precipitated by Muqrin's alleged opposition to the intervention. Salman appointed [[Muhammad bin Nayef]], who publicly announced his support of the operation, to replace Muqrin.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.miamiherald.com/news/nation-world/world/article19897737.html|title=Saudi king names new heir in sign of toughening regional stance|newspaper=[[The Miami Herald]] |date=29 April 2015|access-date=1 May 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Yemen's War Shakes Up the Saudi Palace|url=http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2015/04/29/yemen-s-war-shakes-up-the-saudi-palace.html}}</ref>
[[File:President Donald Trump & Deputy Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman bin Abdulaziz Al Saud, March 14, 2017 cropped.jpg|thumb|Crown Prince [[Mohammad bin Salman]] (right) is considered the architect of the war in Yemen]]

==== Support ====
On 21 April, Saudi prince [[Al-Waleed bin Talal]] reportedly offered 100 [[Bentley]]s to participating pilots. The announcement was met with substantial criticism.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Prince Al-Waleed bin Talal faces backlash for 'promising Bentleys to fighter pilots bombing Yemen'|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/saudi-prince-faces-backlash-for-promising-bentleys-to-fighter-pilots-bombing-yemen-10197372.html|quote=A Saudi Prince has come under fire on social media after reportedly promising luxury Bentley cars to fighter pilots involved in bombing strikes in Yemen. | location=London|work=[[The Independent]]|first=Heather|last=Saul|date=23 April 2015}}</ref>

Among the general populace, the war was popular.<ref>{{cite news |title=Saudi Arabia: The challenged kingdom|url=https://www.economist.com/news/briefing/21651829-new-leaders-saudi-arabia-want-increase-its-clout-they-face-hard-task-challenged |date=23 May 2015 |work=[[The Economist]] |access-date=31 May 2015}}</ref>

=== Other coalition countries ===

==== Bahrain ====
[[File:King Hamad of Bahrain and Advisers Sit With Secretary Kerry at Outset of Meeting Amid Egyptian Development Conference.jpg|thumb|King [[Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa]] of Bahrain in 2015]]
On 3 April Bahrainis protested against the war on Yemen.<ref>{{cite news |title=Bahrain Arrests Rights Activist Over Tweets About Torture|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/04/world/middleeast/bahrain-arrests-rights-activist-over-tweets-about-torture.html|quote=Protesters in Bahrain on Friday denounced the military intervention in Yemen, holding up posters of Abdul-Malik al-Houthi, the rebel leader who comes from the Zaydi sect, an offshoot of Shiite Islam. | newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|first=Robert|last=Mackey|date=3 April 2015}}</ref> A prominent [[Bahraini opposition]] politician, Fadhel Abbas, was reportedly arrested by Bahraini authorities for condemning the bombing as "flagrant aggression".<ref>{{cite news |title=Bahrain Arrests Rights Activist Over Tweets About Torture|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/04/world/middleeast/bahrain-arrests-rights-activist-over-tweets-about-torture.html|quote=Last week, Bahrain's police force announced the arrest of an opposition politician, Fadhel Abbas, and an associate for supposedly disturbing the peace with a statement posted on Twitter that condemned the bombing of Yemen as "flagarent aggression" that violated international law. | newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|first=Robert|last=Mackey|date=3 April 2015}}</ref>

==== Egypt ====
Supporters of the [[Egyptian Muslim Brotherhood]] demonstrated against Egypt's military intervention.<ref>{{cite news |title=Muslim Brotherhood split on Saudi strikes in Yemen|url=http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2015/04/yemen-operation-decisive-storm-egypt-brotherhood-reaction.html# |publisher=[[Al-Monitor]] |quote=Most of the reactions were clear, with the exception of the Brotherhood's, whose Yemeni branch supported the operation and Egyptian branch rejected it. Regardless of the Brotherhood's views on Egypt's participation, they were criticized by their supporters who held demonstrations opposing military action.}}</ref>

==== Kuwait ====
Shiite parliament member Abdul Hamid Dashti reportedly criticized the war and described it as an "act of aggression".<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.worldakhbar.com/gulf/kuwait/27760.html|title=الكويت : فيديو.. نائب كويتي يصف عاصفة الحزم بالعدوان|first=فريق|last=التحرير|date=21 April 2015}}</ref> A prominent Shiite lawyer, Khalid Al Shatti, was summoned by Kuwaiti authorities for his criticism of the Saudi government.<ref>{{cite news |author1=Madeleine Wells|title=Sectarianism and authoritarianism in Kuwait|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/monkey-cage/wp/2015/04/13/sectarianism-and-authoritarianism-in-kuwait/ |work=[[The Washington Post]] |date=13 April 2015 |access-date=24 April 2015}}</ref>

On 28 April, Kuwaiti Foreign Minister [[Sabah Al-Khalid Al-Sabah]] stated that the only solution to the Yemen crisis was political.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.kuna.net.kw/ArticleDetails.aspx?id=2438351&language=en|title=KUNA : Political solution in Yemen is only solution – Kuwaiti FM – Politics|date=28 April 2015|publisher=kuna.net.kw}}</ref>

=== International ===
{{Main|International reactions to the Saudi-led intervention in Yemen (2015–present)}}
[[File:Secretary Kerry Poses With Saudi Arabia Foreign Minister Al-Jubeir, British Foreign Secretary Johnson and United Arab Emirates Foreign Minister Al Nahyan in London (27801916664).jpg|thumb|Foreign Ministers of the U.S., the U.K., Saudi Arabia and the United Arab Emirates, before a working dinner focused on Yemen, 19 July 2016]]
The [[Arab League]], United States, [[Turkey]], [[Organisation of Islamic Cooperation|OIC]] and [[Hamas]] voiced support for the intervention,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://latimes.com/world/middleeast/la-fg-joint-arab-military-force-20150329-story.html|newspaper=[[Los Angeles Times]]|title=Arab League's joint military force is a 'defining moment' for region|date=29 March 2015 |first1=Christina|last1=Boyle|first2=Zaid|last2=al-Alayaa |access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.france24.com/en/20150326-turkey-support-saudi-yemen-erdogan-interview-france-24|publisher=[[France 24]] |title=Turkey supports Saudi mission in Yemen, says Iran must withdraw|date=26 March 2015}}</ref><ref>[http://www.arabnews.com/saudi-arabia/news/725241 "Hamas supports military operation for political legitimacy in Yemen"]. Arab News. 30 March 2015.</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.arabnews.com/featured/news/723946|newspaper=Arab News|title=OIC supports military action in Yemen|date=27 March 2015}}</ref> but the [[European Union]], Russia<ref>[http://www.agsiw.org/russia-maneuvers-opposing-forces-yemen/ "Russia Maneuvers between Opposing Forces in Yemen"]. The Arab Gulf States Institute in Washington. 25 January 2017.</ref> and the United Nations criticised it.<ref>{{cite news |title=EU warns of serious regional consequences of Yemeni crisis|url=http://www.laprensasa.com/309_america-in-english/3022119_eu-warns-of-serious-regional-consequences-of-yemeni-crisis.html |publisher=Laprensasa |date=29 March 2015 |access-date=29 March 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.newsweek.com/saudi-arabia-accuse-putin-hypocrisy-after-letter-arab-league-317899|work=[[Newsweek]]|title=Saudi Arabia Accuse Putin of Hypocrisy After Letter to Arab League|first=Damien|last=Sharkov|date=30 March 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50464 |publisher=UN News Centre|title=Senior UN officials deeply concerned over civilian casualties in wake of recent fighting in Yemen|date=31 March 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref> The United Kingdom, and France supported the intervention,<ref>[http://www.france24.com/en/20150412-france-fabius-support-saudi-campaign-yemen-houthis "France voices support for Saudi campaign in Yemen"]. [[France 24]]. 12 April 2015.</ref> and along with Canada have supplied the Saudi military with equipment.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/yemen/11557098/Yemen-crisis-British-ministers-clash-over-supplying-bombs-to-Saudi-Arabia-as-coalition-launches-new-air-strikes.html |work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]| title=Yemen crisis: British MPs clash over supplying bombs to Saudi Arabia as coalition launches new air strikes |date=23 April 2015 |location=London |first=Con |last=Coughlin |authorlink=Con Coughlin}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url= https://www.theglobeandmail.com/news/politics/saudi-arms-deal-breaks-canadas-export-controls-opponents-argue/article29769283/|title=Human rights groups ask Trudeau to end 'immoral' arms deal with Saudi Arabia |work=[[The Globe and Mail]]|date=27 April 2016}}</ref><ref name="Saudi 2016">[https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-arms-idUSKCN10X1MM "Arms sales to Saudi 'illicit' due to civilian deaths in Yemen: campaigners"]. Reuters. 22 August 2016.</ref>

[[Iran]] condemned intervention as "US-backed aggression".<ref>[http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/saudi-air-strikes-yemen-iran-condemns-us-backed-aggression-1493620 "Saudi air strikes in Yemen: Iran condemns 'US-backed aggression'"]. [[International Business Times]]. 26 March 2015</ref> [[Permanent Representative of Iran to the United Nations|Iran's U.N. Ambassador]] Gholamali Khoshroo said that "those who violate international law, including international humanitarian law, should be held accountable for their acts and there should be no room for impunity."<ref>[https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/13/yemen-security-iran-un-idUSL1N0Y41JR20150513 "Iran complains to UN of foiled Yemen aid as ship standoff looms"]. Reuters. 13 May 2015.</ref> Iraqi Prime Minister [[Haidar al-Abadi]] expressed the [[Federal government of Iraq|Iraqi government]]'s opposition to the intervention: "This (Yemen war) can engulf the whole region in another conflict. We don't need another [[Sectarianism|sectarian war]] in the region."<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-iraq-yemen-idUSKBN0N629R20150415 |title=Iraq PM says Yemen could stoke regional war, slams Saudi operations |work=[[Reuters]] |date=15 April 2015}}</ref> The [[Hezbollah]] secretary general criticized Saudi Arabia and its allies, saying "all invaders end up being defeated".<ref>
{{cite news
| title = Hizballah chief criticises Saudi Arabia for Yemen intervention
| url = https://www.alaraby.co.uk/english/news/2015/3/28/hizballah-chief-criticises-saudi-arabia-for-yemen-intervention
| accessdate = 5 March 2016
 }}
</ref>

The [[China|Chinese]] foreign ministry expressed in January 2016 its support for the intervention and the Hadi government, while stressing its desire for a resumption of stability in Yemen.<ref>https://www.reuters.com/article/us-saudi-china-yemen/china-offers-support-for-yemen-government-as-xi-visits-saudi-arabia-idUSKCN0UY0C1, 20 January 2016</ref>

[[Somalia]]'s government blamed the Saudi-led coalition for the killing of at least 42 [[Somali diaspora|Somali refugees]] off the Yemeni coast. Somali Prime Minister [[Hassan Ali Khaire]] called the attack on a boat carrying refugees "atrocious" and "appalling".<ref name="somali"/>

[[File:122 Arrests (38309419014).jpg|thumb|Protesters against the US-backed Saudi-led war on Yemen were led away handcuffed by [[New York City|New York]] police outside the [[United States Mission to the United Nations|US mission to the UN]] on 11 December 2017]]

Asian countries including China, [[India]], [[Malaysia]] and Pakistan, moved within days to [[International reactions to the Saudi-led intervention in Yemen (2015–present)#Evacuations and other actions|evacuate their citizens from Yemen]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/03/29/yemen-security-china-idUSL6N0WV0EE20150329 |work=[[Reuters]]|title=Chinese warship docks in Aden to evacuate nationals – port official|first=Noah|last=Browning|date=29 March 2015|access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.janes.com/article/50545/malaysia-sends-c-130s-for-yemen-evacuation|title=Malaysia sends C-130s for Yemen evacuation|last=Mahadzir|first=Dzirhan|publisher=[[Jane's Information Group]]|date=9 April 2015|access-date=18 April 2015|url-status=dead|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20150417030921/http://www.janes.com/article/50545/malaysia-sends-c-130s-for-yemen-evacuation|archivedate=17 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Pakistan evacuates hundreds during pause in Yemen strikes – Saudi official|url=http://in.reuters.com/article/2015/03/29/yemen-security-pakistan-idINKBN0MP05G20150329 |work=[[Reuters]] |date=29 March 2015 |access-date=29 March 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.thehindu.com/news/national/india-begins-evacuating-citizens/article7054994.ece|newspaper=[[The Hindu]] |title=India begins evacuating citizens|date=3 April 2015|location=Chennai, India|first1=Dinakar|last1=Peri|first2=Renuka|last2=Phadnis |access-date=3 April 2015}}</ref>

On 4 April, the [[International Committee of the Red Cross|ICRC]] called for a 24-hour humanitarian ceasefire after the coalition blocked three aid shipments to Yemen.<ref name="reuters.com">{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/04/yemen-security-icrc-pause-idUSL6N0X109R20150404|title=Red Cross seeks 24-hour ceasefire in Yemen to deliver aid |work=[[Reuters]] | first=Stephanie|last=Nebehay|date=4 April 2015}}</ref> Russia also called for "humanitarian pauses" in the coalition bombing campaign, bringing the idea before the [[United Nations Security Council]] in a 4 April emergency meeting.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/US/wireStory/russia-urges-call-humanitarian-pause-yemen-30099311|publisher=[[ABC News]] |title=Russia Urges UN to Call for 'Humanitarian Pause' in Yemen|first=Edith|last=Lederer|date=4 April 2015 }}</ref> Saudi Arabia's UN ambassador raised questions over whether humanitarian pauses are the best way of delivering humanitarian assistance.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/04/04/uk-yemen-security-russia-idUKKBN0MV0JU20150404|title=Russia calls for pause in Yemen air strikes to evacuate foreigners|work=Reuters UK | date=4 April 2015}}</ref> On 7 April, China renewed calls for an immediate ceasefire.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2015-04/07/c_134131136.htm|title=China calls for ceasefire in Yemen|access-date=15 April 2015}}</ref>

On 10 April, the [[Parliament of Pakistan|Pakistani Parliament]] declined a Saudi Arabian request to join the coalition. The Parliament clarified the wish to maintain a neutral diplomatic stance.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/10/us-yemen-security-idUSKBN0N10LO20150410|title=Pakistan declines Saudi call for armed support in Yemen fight |work=[[Reuters]] |date=10 April 2015 |access-date=15 April 2015}}</ref>
[[File:Francois Hollande Carcassonne-1089.jpg|thumb|left|France authorised $18&nbsp;billion (€16&nbsp;billion) in arms sales to Saudi Arabia in 2015.<ref name="Saudi 2016"/>]]

On 16 April a group of US and UK-based Yemen scholars wrote an open letter, stating that the operation was illegal under international law and calling for the UN to enforce an immediate ceasefire.<ref name="TWP_2015-04-18_TYS">{{cite news |last=Tharoor |first=Ishaan |title=Top Yemen scholars in the West condemn Saudi Arabia's war |work=[[The Washington Post]] – Blogs |date=18 April 2015 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/worldviews/wp/2015/04/18/top-yemen-scholars-in-the-west-condemn-saudi-arabias-war/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Xu0iMU4D?url=http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/worldviews/wp/2015/04/18/top-yemen-scholars-in-the-west-condemn-saudi-arabias-war/ |archivedate=19 April 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 19 April, international aid agency [[Oxfam]] condemned SA over airstrikes it said hit one of its warehouses containing humanitarian supplies in Saada.<ref>{{cite news |url= http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/04/20/uk-yemen-security-humanitarian-idUKKBN0NB0DT20150420|title=Aid agency Oxfam condemns Saudi air strike in Yemen|date=20 April 2015 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref>

Aid groups came out against the air campaign: [[Amnesty International]] said some of the coalition's airstrikes "appear to have failed to take necessary precautions to minimize harm to civilians and damage to civilian objects".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.amnesty.org/articles/news/2015/04/yemen-investigate-relentless-airstrikes-that-have-left-hundreds-of-civilians-dead/|title=Yemen: Relentless airstrikes that have left hundreds of civilians dead must be investigated|date=24 April 2014|publisher=Amnesty International}}</ref> [[Reporters without Borders]] condemned a strike in Sanaa on 20 April that caused the deaths of four employees of Al-Yemen Al-Youm TV and injured ten others; it also condemned attacks on journalists by pro-Houthi forces.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://en.rsf.org/yemen-journalists-killed-injured-as-24-04-2015,47811.html|title=Journalists Killed, Injured as Security Situation Worsens|date=24 April 2015|publisher=Reporters without Borders}}</ref>

On 4 May the UN called on the coalition to stop attacking Sanaa Airport to allow delivery of humanitarian aid.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/04/yemen-security-humanitarian-idUSL5N0XV3TT20150504|title=UPDATE 1-UN urges Saudi-led coalition to stop targeting Yemen airport |work=[[Reuters]] | date=4 May 2015}}</ref> On 10 May the UN Humanitarian Coordinator for Yemen stated that the attacks on Saada province were in breach of international law.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.i24news.tv/en/news/international/middle-east/70605-150509-saudi-led-strikes-in-yemen-in-breach-of-international-law-un-coordinator|title=Malaysian forces join Saudi-led coalition in Yemen|publisher=i24news|access-date=11 May 2015}}</ref> On 29 June, Secretary General Ban Ki-moon denounced a coalition airstrike that had hit a UN compound in Aden the previous day and requested a full investigation.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51289 |title=United Nations News Centre|date=29 June 2015|publisher=UN News Service Section|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

[[File:Advocating the early entry into force of the CTBT, Article 14 Conference 2009 - Flickr - The Official CTBTO Photostream (173).jpg|thumb|UN Secretary-General [[Ban Ki-moon]] has criticized Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen]]
[[Human Rights Watch]] criticized the [[UN Security Council]] repeatedly for "remaining almost silent on coalition abuses".<ref name="NYT_2015-12-22_MAY">{{cite news |title=UN: Most Attacks on Yemen Civilians From Saudi-Led Coalition |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |agency=[[Associated Press]] |date=22 December 2015 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/12/22/world/middleeast/ap-un-united-nations-yemen.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e1cmULS1?url=http://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/12/22/world/middleeast/ap-un-united-nations-yemen.html?_r=0 |archivedate=24 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="HRW_2015-11-26_WMT"/><ref name="HRW_2015-12-22_SUT">{{cite web |last=Herrmann |first=Amy |title=Dispatches: Special UN Treatment for Saudi-led Coalition in Yemen? |publisher=Human Rights Watch |date=22 December 2015 |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/12/22/dispatches-special-un-treatment-saudi-led-coalition-yemen |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e080nqsI?url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2015/12/22/dispatches-special-un-treatment-saudi-led-coalition-yemen |archivedate=23 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> In January 2016 an unpublished United Nations panel investigating the Saudi-led bombing campaign in Yemen uncovered "widespread and systematic" attacks on civilian targets in violation of international humanitarian law, calling UN Security Council up for an international commission of inquiry.<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="theguardian-com_2016-01-27_URI"/><ref name="voanews-com_2016-01-28_UPA"/> Saudi Arabia had previously objected to an inquiry being set up,<ref name="AFP_2016-01-27_UPC"/><ref name="AI_2015-10-02_URY">{{cite web |title=UN resolution on Yemen fails to launch international investigation into war crimes |publisher=Amnesty International |date=2 October 2015 |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2015/10/un-resolution-on-yemen-fails-to-launch-international-investigation-into-war-crimes/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6c7YnQ9N6?url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2015/10/un-resolution-on-yemen-fails-to-launch-international-investigation-into-war-crimes/ |archivedate=8 October 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> and had not been supported by Western governments.<ref name="globalpost-com_2015-11-30_WUH"/><ref name="NYT_2015-12-22_SLW">{{cite news |last=Sengupta |first=Somini |title=Saudi-Led War in Yemen Frays Ties With the U.S. |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=22 December 2015 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/12/23/world/middleeast/saudi-led-war-in-yemen-frays-ties-with-the-us.html |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6e1cLlyUj?url=http://www.nytimes.com/2015/12/23/world/middleeast/saudi-led-war-in-yemen-frays-ties-with-the-us.html?_r=0 |archivedate=24 December 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="news-vice-com_2016-01-07_UTH">{{cite news |last=Oakford |first=Samuel |title=The UN's Top Human Rights Official in Yemen is Now 'Persona Non Grata' |publisher=[[Vice News]] |date=7 January 2016 |url=https://news.vice.com/article/the-uns-top-human-rights-official-in-yemen-is-now-persona-non-grata |access-date=28 January 2016 }}</ref><ref name="theatlantic-com_2015-10-02_LOW">{{cite news |last=Chandler |first=Adam |title=Looking the Other Way in Yemen – The U.S. allowed the Saudis to block a UN inquiry into the thousands of deaths in Yemen's civil war |work=[[The Atlantic]] |date=2 October 2015 |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2015/10/united-states-united-nations-yemen-war/408751/ |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6cP9VRi5Z?url=http://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2015/10/united-states-united-nations-yemen-war/408751/ |archivedate=19 October 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In February 2016 the [[Secretary-General of the United Nations|Secretary-General of the UN]] (UNSG) [[Ban Ki-moon]] raised strong concerns over continued Saudi-led airstrikes, saying that "coalition air strikes in particular continue to strike hospitals, schools, mosques and civilian infrastructures" in Yemen. He urged States that are signatories to the [[Arms Trade Treaty]] to "control arms flows to actors that may use them in ways that breach of international humanitarian law".<ref name="un-org_2016-02-05_SGA">{{cite web |title=Secretary-General's address at event co-organized by the United Nations Association of the United Kingdom and Chatham House |publisher=un.org (UNSG Ban Ki-moon) |date=5 February 2016 |url=https://www.un.org/sg/statements/index.asp?nid=9440 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6f9HqmpHY?url=http://www.un.org/sg/statements/index.asp?nid=9440 |archivedate=8 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="ECHO_2016-02-08_EDF">{{cite web |title=Yemen – Conflict (ECHO, UN, Media) (ECHO Daily Flash of 8 February 2016 |publisher=European Commission Humanitarian Aid Office |date=8 February 2016 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-conflict-echo-un-media-echo-daily-flash-8-february-2016 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6f9Gs2eHK?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-conflict-echo-un-media-echo-daily-flash-8-february-2016 |archivedate=8 February 2016 |url-status=live }} ({{cite web |title=original |url=http://erccportal.jrc.ec.europa.eu/ECHO-Flash |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6f9H2KJnw?url=http://erccportal.jrc.ec.europa.eu/ECHO-Flash |archivedate=8 February 2016 |url-status=live }})</ref>

In June 2016, Ban Ki-moon removed a Saudi-led coalition from a list of [[children's rights]] violators,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/06/10/world/middleeast/saudi-arabia-yemen-children-ban-ki-moon.html |title= United Nations Chief Exposes Limits to His Authority by Citing Saudi Threat |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=8 June 2016}}</ref> saying that Saudi Arabia threatened to cut Palestinian aid and funds to other UN programs if coalition was not removed from blacklist for killing children in Yemen. According to one source, there was also a threat of "clerics in Riyadh meeting to issue a [[fatwa]] against the UN, declaring it anti-Muslim, which would mean no contacts of OIC members, no relations, contributions, support, to any UN projects, programs".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jun/08/saudi-arabia-united-nations-blacklist-yemen-ban-ki-moon |title=Saudi Arabian allies pressured UN chief to issue blacklist reversal, sources say |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=8 June 2016}}</ref>

In September 2016, British Foreign Secretary [[Boris Johnson]] was accused of blocking the UN inquiry into Saudi war crimes in Yemen.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/boris-johnson-yemen-criticised-human-rights-watch-amnesty-international-blocking-war-crimes-inquiry-a7330136.html |title=Boris Johnson criticised by human rights groups after blocking inquiry into war crimes in Yemen |work=[[The Independent]] |date=27 September 2016}}</ref>

In April 2018, French President [[Emmanuel Macron]] voiced support for the Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen and defended France's arms sales to the Saudi-led coalition.<ref name="yemen">{{cite news |title=France's Macron defends Saudi arms sales, to hold Yemen conference |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-france-saudi-yemen/frances-macron-defends-saudi-arms-sales-to-hold-yemen-conference-idUSKBN1HH30P |work=Reuters |date=10 April 2018}}</ref>

Bahri Abha – the Saudi Arabian ship arrived on 10 December 2019, at the Sagunto, Valencia port, where they were faced by Spanish Control Arms campaign organizations. Since the beginning of the Yemen war, the same ship has reportedly ferried $162 million worth of US-made arms to the kingdom. The organizations of the likes of Amnesty International, FundiPau, Greenpeace and Oxfam Intermón have objected to the shipment of arms from Spanish port.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2019/12/spain-ensure-saudi-arabian-ship-carries-no-arms-through-spanish-ports/|title= Spain: Ensure Saudi Arabian ship carries no arms through Spanish ports|accessdate=10 December 2019|website=Amnesty International}}</ref>

On June 15, 2020, Secretary-General of the UN, [[António Guterres]], removed the Saudi-led coalition from a list of children's rights violators despite continued grave violations against children in Yemen.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/06/15/un-chiefs-list-shame-drops-saudi-led-coalition|title= UN Chief's 'List of Shame' Drops Saudi-Led Coalition|accessdate=15 June 2020|website=Human Rights Watch}}</ref>

== Al-Qaeda and Islamic State ==
{{See also|al-Qaeda insurgency in Yemen}}
Both [[al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula]] (AQAP) and [[Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant|Islamic State]] had a presence in Yemen before the Saudi-led intervention. AQAP had controlled substantial pieces of territory for some time, while Islamic State claimed for twin bombings in Sanaa the following month that killed 140 people and injured hundreds more.<ref>{{cite news | url = https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-31998682 | title = Islamic State in Yemen: Why IS is seeking to expand | last = Mendelsohn | first = Barak | date = 21 March 2015 | work = BBC News | access-date = 24 February 2016 }}</ref>

The two radical groups have used the conflict to expand and consolidate, an obvious fact accepted by the Pentagon.<ref name="NYT allow Qaeda">{{Cite news | url = https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/17/world/middleeast/khaled-bahah-houthi-rebel-yemen-fighting.html | title = War in Yemen Is Allowing Qaeda Group to Expand | last1 = Al-batati | first1 = Saeed | date = 16 April 2015 | last2 = Fahim | first2 = Kareem | newspaper = [[The New York Times]] | access-date = 24 February 2016 }}</ref> The Houthis disengaged fighting AQAP to face rival Yemeni militias at the same time as they were being hit by coalition air strikes;<ref name="NYT allow Qaeda"/><ref>{{cite news |last= Salisbury |first= Peter |date= 28 October 2014 |title= The Houthis Are Battling al Qaeda Amid a 'Slow-Burning Coup' in Yemen |url= https://news.vice.com/article/the-houthis-are-battling-al-qaeda-amid-a-slow-burning-coup-in-yemen |publisher= [[Vice News]] |access-date= 24 February 2016 |quote= [T]hey are deadly serious about eradicating AQAP [...] the group's desire to break AQAP's grip on the north of the country remains undimmed. }}</ref> A source indicates that Yemeni troops in the south remained in their bases instead of confronting al-Qaeda militants, fearing Saudi air strikes on any troop movements.<ref name="GDJ prison break">{{cite news |title = Al-Qaeda Commander Freed in Yemen Prison Break|url = https://www.buzzfeed.com/gregorydjohnsen/al-qaeda-commander-freed-in-yemen-prison-break|publisher = BuzzFeed |last = Johnsen|first = Gregory D.|date = 2 April 2015 |access-date = 4 February 2016}}</ref> There are questions about the ability of the country to confront its Islamist militancy problem due to the major infrastructure damage caused by the war.<ref name="GDJ prison break"/>

Within weeks of the commencement of the Yemen's civil war, AQAP had exploited the chaos to [[Battle of Mukalla (2015)|capture]] the south-eastern port city of [[Mukalla]],<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/03/world/middleeast/yemen-al-qaeda-attack.html|title=Saudi Leaders Have High Hopes for Yemen Airstrikes, but Houthi Attacks Continue |date=2 April 2015 |newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|first1=David D. |last1=Kirkpatrick |authorlink=David D. Kirkpatrick |first2=Kareem |last2=Fahim |access-date=4 April 2015}}</ref> along with nearby military, transport, and economic infrastructure.<ref name="NYT allow Qaeda"/> A series of prison breaks by al-Qaeda—they emptied Mukalla's jail of 300 prisoners and emptied 1,200 inmates in June 2015 from the central prison in [[Taiz]]—released jailed jihadists of all ranks.<ref>{{cite news |title = Al-Qaeda frees 300 prisoners in Yemen jail break|url = https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/yemen/11510765/Al-Qaeda-frees-300-prisoners-in-Yemen-jail-break.html|newspaper = [[The Daily Telegraph]] |last = Alexander|first = Harriet|date = 2 April 2015 |access-date = 4 February 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title = Around 1,200 escape from Yemen prison, including al Qaeda suspects|url = https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-prison-idUSKCN0PA2JZ20150630 |date = 30 June 2015 |work = [[Reuters]] |access-date = 4 February 2016}}</ref> Reports indicate that Yemen's prisons had, in preceding years, reportedly become "de facto jihadi academies", as veteran militants were placed in cells alongside young, regular criminals.<ref name="GDJ prison break"/>

The coalition campaign against the Houthis in Yemen's city of Aden in July 2015 and subsequent chaos increased AQAP and Islamic State presence in the city.<ref>{{cite news |title = Has Yemen war handed Aden to jihadists? |url = https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-34115952 |work = BBC News |first = Frank |last = Gardner |authorlink=Frank Gardner (journalist) |date = 2 September 2015 |access-date = 24 February 2016}}</ref> Residents of Aden faced a wave of bombings and shootings that prevented efforts at stabilization.<ref name="AFP_2016-02-09_YCK">{{cite news |title=Yemen clashes kill 6, including 4 family members |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=9 February 2016 |url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-clashes-kill-6-including-4-family-members |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fBkQEcon?url=http://reliefweb.int/report/yemen/yemen-clashes-kill-6-including-4-family-members |archivedate=10 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref> AQAP conducted assassinations of judges, security officials, and police.<ref name="trust-org_2016-02-09_WOA">{{cite news |first1=Mohammed |last1=Ghobari |first2=Yara |last2=Bayoumy |title=Wave of Aden killings tests Gulf role in Yemen |agency=[[Reuters]] |date=9 February 2016 |url=http://news.trust.org/item/20160209090050-7bw5j/?source=fiOtherNews3 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6fBj4zgsV?url=http://news.trust.org/item/20160209090050-7bw5j/?source=fiOtherNews3 |archivedate=10 February 2016 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 26 August 2015, Bob Semple, a British petroleum engineer who was kidnapped and held as a hostage by Al Qaeda in Yemen was freed by the UAE armed forces after 18 months of captivity.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.emirates247.com/news/freed-british-hostage-pays-tribute-to-uae-2015-08-26-1.601371|title=Freed British hostage pays tribute to UAE|publisher=emirates246|access-date=7 September 2015}}</ref>

At the start of February 2016, AQAP recaptured Azzan, an important commercial city in Shabwa province.<ref>{{cite news |title = Al Qaeda Is Making Serious Gains Amid Chaos of Yemen's Civil War |url = https://news.vice.com/article/al-qaeda-is-making-serious-gains-amid-chaos-of-yemens-civil-war|publisher = [[Vice News]]|date = 1 February 2016|last = Asher-Schapiro|first = Avi |access-date = 24 February 2016}}</ref> A few weeks later, al-Qaeda fighters and Saudi-led coalition forces were seen fighting a common target; the Houthis.<ref name="bbc-20160222">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-35630194 |title=Yemen conflict: Al-Qaeda joins coalition battle for Taiz |work=BBC News |date=22 February 2016 |access-date=23 February 2016}}</ref>
But the situation is different in Aden, the AQAP/ISIS and pro-Hadi that were fighting a common enemy in Taiz are enemies in Aden. On 29 February 2016, a suicide car killed 4 pro-Hadi troops in Shiek Othman district in Aden, the city that Hadi uses as a temporary capital.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.digitaljournal.com/news/world/suicide-bombing-kills-4-in-yemen-s-aden-official/article/458895|title=Suicide bombing kills 4 in Yemen's Aden: official|accessdate=29 February 2016}}</ref>

The United Arab Emirates has spearheaded an active role against fighting [[Al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula|AQAP]] and [[Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant – Yemen Province|ISIL-YP]] presence in Yemen through a partnership with the United States.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ispionline.it/it/pubblicazione/uaes-military-priorities-yemen-counterterrorism-and-south-15573|title=Uae's military priorities in Yemen: Counterterrorism and the South|last1=Ardemagni|first1=Eleonora|website=.ispionline.it|date=28 July 2016}}</ref> In April 2016, UAE armed forces assisted Yemeni forces in retaking the city of [[Mukalla]] from AQAP during the [[Battle of Mukalla (2016)|Battle of Mukalla]].<ref>{{cite news|work=[[The New York Times]]|date=24 April 2016|title=Yemeni Troops, Backed by United Arab Emirates, Take City From Al Qaeda|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/25/world/middleeast/yemeni-troops-backed-by-united-arab-emirates-take-city-from-al-qaeda.html}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|work=[[Politico]]|date=2 May 2016|title=The Giant Al Qaeda Defeat That No One's Talking About|url=https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/05/us-middle-east-victory-al-qaeda-213864}}</ref> In August 2017, the UAE armed forces assisted a Yemeni army offensive against AQAP in [[Shabwah Governorate]].<ref>{{Cite news|work=[[Military Times]]|title=US puts boots on the ground in Yemen to attack AQAP|url=https://www.militarytimes.com/flashpoints/2017/08/04/us-ground-forces-airstrikes-attack-aqap-in-yemen/|date=4 August 2017}}</ref>

In an Op-Ed in ''The Washington Post'' [[Yousef Al Otaiba]], the UAE ambassador to the United States, described that the intervention has reduced [[Al-Qaeda in the Arabian Peninsula|AQAP]] presence in Yemen to its weakest point since 2012 with many areas previously under their control liberated.<ref name="WP">{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/global-opinions/wp/2018/09/12/the-arab-coalition-is-making-progress-against-extremists-in-yemen/|work=The Washington Post |title=The Arab coalition is making progress against extremists in Yemen|date= 12 September 2018}}</ref> The ambassador declared that more than 2,000 militants have been removed from the battlefield, with their controlled areas now having improved security and a better delivered humanitarian and development assistance such as to the port city of [[Mukalla]] and other liberated areas.<ref name="WP"/> An Associated Press investigation outlined that the military coalition in Yemen actively reduced AQAP in Yemen without military intervention, instead by offering them deals and even actively recruiting them in the coalition because "they are considered as exceptional fighters".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://apnews.com/f38788a561d74ca78c77cb43612d50da|agency=The Associated Press |title=AP Investigation: US allies, al-Qaida battle rebels in Yemen|date=7 August 2018}}</ref> UAE Brigadier General Musallam Al Rashidi responded to the accusations by stating that Al Qaeda cannot be reasoned with and cited that multiple of his soldiers have been killed by them.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.apnews.com/f9588898ba3b408295da9dc6219704aa|title=UAE responds to AP report on deals with al-Qaida in Yemen|date=13 August 2018|publisher=Associated Press}}</ref> The UAE military stated that accusations of allowing AQAP to leave with cash contradicts their primary objective of depriving AQAP of its financial strength.<ref name=TIDx>{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/uae-yemen-civil-war-al-qaeda-aden-dar-saad-gulf-saudi-arabia-conflict-a8492021.html|title=Inside the UAE's war on al-Qaeda in Yemen|newspaper=The Independent |last1=Trew|first1=Bel|date=15 August 2018}}</ref> The notion of the coalition recruiting or paying AQAP has been thoroughly denied by the United States [[The Pentagon|Pentagon]] with Colonel Robert Manning, spokesperson of the Pentagon, calling the news source "patently false".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2018/aug/8/pentagon-denies-us-allies-bribe-recruit-al-qaeda/|title=Pentagon denies reports of U.S. allies bribing, recruiting al Qaeda fighters in Yemen|work=The Washington Times|access-date=29 August 2018}}</ref> The governor of [[Hadramut]] Faraj al-Bahsani, dismissed the accusations that Al Qaeda has joined with the coalition rank, explaining that if they did there would be sleeper cells and that he would be "the first one to be killed". According to ''The Independent'', AQAP activity on social media as well as the number of terror attacks conducted by them has decreased since the Emirati intervention.<ref name=TIDx/>

In January 2019, CNN stated that Saudi Arabia and the UAE provided al-Qaeda linked groups in Yemen with US-made military equipment including vehicles.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/02/saudi-arabia-uae-gave-weapons-al-qaeda-linked-groups-cnn-190205055102300.html|title=Saudi Arabia, UAE gave US arms to al-Qaeda-linked groups: Report|website=www.aljazeera.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/interactive/2019/02/middleeast/yemen-lost-us-arms/|title=US arms sold to Saudi Arabia and UAE end up in wrong hands|website=www.cnn.com}}</ref>

On 25 June 2019, Saudi special forces announced that they captured the leader of the ISIL-YP, [[Abu Osama al-Muhajer]], on the 3 June along with other members including the chief financial officer of the organization.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security-isis/saudi-forces-say-they-have-captured-leader-of-yemen-branch-of-islamic-state-idUSKCN1TQ1TX|title=Saudi forces say they have captured leader of Yemen branch of Islamic State|work=Reuters|date=25 June 2019}}</ref>

In April 2020, Yemeni journalist Salah Bin Laghbar revealed documents showing cooperation between Saudi-led coalition and al-Qaeda in Yemen; "An official document from the al-Humiqani tribe warns Saudi-led coalition against sending weapons to terrorist organizations through the [[Al-Rashad Union|Al-Rashad Party]], [[Muslim Brotherhood]] and terrorist Abdul Rahman Abu al-Harith al-Humiqani, who is affiliated with Daesh."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20200409-yemen-document-exposes-saudi-coalition-support-for-al-qaeda-in-baydah/|title=Yemen: Document exposes Saudi coalition support for Al-Qaeda in Baydah|date=9 April 2020|website=Middle East Monitor}}</ref>

== Other effects ==
[[File:Registration of Indian citizens evacuating from Yemen in progress (2015) - 1.jpg|thumb|Registration of Indian citizens evacuating from Yemen, March 2015]]
On 25 March 2015, [[Gulf Air]], the Bahraini flag carrier airline announced the immediate suspension of service to Sanaʽa.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://atwonline.com/airports-routes/gulf-air-suspends-sana-service-due-worsening-security|work=[[Air Transport World]] |title=Gulf Air suspends Sana'a service due to worsening security|date=25 March 2015|access-date=25 March 2015}}</ref> [[List of airlines of Somalia|Somali airlines]] such as [[Daallo Airlines]] and [[Jubba Airways]] also encountered difficulties, as they were unable to fly over Yemen after its airspace became restricted.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.garoweonline.com/page/show/post/2126/saudi-arabia-airstrikes-in-yemen-disrupt-somalia-flights|title=Saudi Arabia airstrikes in Yemen disrupt Somalia flights|date=26 March 2015 |publisher=[[Garowe Online]] |access-date=26 March 2015}}</ref> On 15 April 2015, Turkish Airlines suspended all Yemen flights until 1 June.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aa.com.tr/en/news/494389--turkish-airlines-suspends-yemen-flights|title=Turkish Airlines suspends Yemen flights|date=15 April 2015|publisher=Andalou Agency}}</ref>

Following Hadi's request, the administration of the Egypt-based [[Nilesat]] and Saudi-based [[Arabsat]], two satellite communication companies, stopped broadcasting Yemeni state-run television channels that had fallen under Houthi control. The channels included Al-Yemen, Al-Eman, [[Saba News Agency]] and Aden TV. Armed Houthis closed down the Sanaʽa offices of four media outlets, including [[Al Jazeera]], Yemen Shabab and [[Suhail]] channels, as well as Al-Masdar's newspaper and website. Al-Saeeda channel was also stormed, but was allowed to remain open on the condition it not broadcast anti-Houthi material. Houthi Political Office member Mohammad Al-Bukhaiti said the channels were closed for supporting the coalition.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.yementimes.com/en/1871/news/5009/Deadly-strikes-hit-Yemen-for-fourth-night.htm|title=Deadly Strikes Hit Yemen for Fourth Night |date=29 March 2015|newspaper=[[Yemen Times]] |access-date=30 March 2015}}</ref>

King Salman replaced his half-brother Muqrin as crown prince with Muhammad bin Nayef and named his son [[Mohammed bin Salman]] as defence minister, and then-Ambassador to the United States [[Adel al-Jubeir]] as foreign minister. Some reports linked the cabinet reshuffle to the war.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2015/04/29/yemen-s-war-shakes-up-the-saudi-palace.html|website=The Daily Beast|title=Yemen's War Shakes Up the Saudi Palace|first=Bruce|last=Riedel |authorlink=Bruce Riedel |date=29 April 2015|access-date=30 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/29/us-saudi-politics-jubeir-newsmaker-idUSKBN0NK12H20150429 |work=[[Reuters]] |title=Saudi foreign minister is Washington insider, confidant of king|date=29 April 2015 |first=William|last=Maclean |access-date=30 April 2015}}</ref> At least one political analyst suggested that Muqrin was not supportive of the military intervention, and that this cost him his position.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.thenewstribune.com/2015/04/28/3765544/saudi-king-names-counterterrorism.html|newspaper=[[The News Tribune]]|location=Tacoma, Wash.|title=Saudi king, facing challenges in Yemen, fires his heir, foreign minister|first=Tom|last=Hussain|date=28 April 2015|access-date=30 April 2015|archive-url=https://archive.today/20150430230639/http://www.thenewstribune.com/2015/04/28/3765544/saudi-king-names-counterterrorism.html|archive-date=30 April 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> Prince Muqrin's Yemeni Lineage was pointed out as another possible cause.<ref>{{cite news |last=Varghese|first=Johnlee|url=http://www.ibtimes.co.in/political-earthquake-saudi-arabia-prince-muqrins-yemeni-lineage-cost-him-crown-630774 |title='Political Earthquake' in Saudi Arabia: Prince Muqrin's Yemeni Lineage Cost him the Crown?|work=[[International Business Times]]|date=29 April 2015|access-date=2 May 2015}}</ref>

The exiled Yemeni government sent a request to the UN, asking for foreign troops on the ground.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/may/07/yemen-president-un-ground-intervention-halt-houthi-rebel-aden-hadi|title=Yemen's exiled government asks UN for ground troops to halt Houthi advance|first=Kareem|last=Shaheen|date=7 May 2015|via=www.theguardian.com}}</ref>

On 19 June 2015, [[WikiLeaks]] announced the intention of releasing over 500,000 Saudi diplomatic documents to the internet. In its statement, WikiLeaks referred to a recent electronic attack on the Saudi Foreign Ministry by a group calling itself the [[Yemen Cyber Army]], but did not indicate whether they passed the documents to WikiLeaks.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/world/middle-east/WikiLeaks-says-its-leaking-over-500000-Saudi-documents/articleshow/47742125.cms?from=mdr|title=WikiLeaks says it's leaking over 500,000 Saudi documents|work=[[The Times of India]] |access-date=29 July 2015}}</ref>

== Peace talks ==
{{Update section|date=April 2019}}
{{Main|Yemeni peace process}}

=== Cease fire talks ===
On 15 May 2015, new UN envoy to Yemen Ismail Ould Cheikh Ahmed proposed peace talks in Geneva. Rebel spokesman Hamed al-Bokheiti said the Houthis were willing to hold talks in any "neutral" country.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.haaretz.com/news/middle-east/middle-east-updates/1.656611|title=Middle East updates / Clashes in Yemen mar truce as UN envoy pushes for talks |date=15 May 2015|work=[[Haaretz]] |access-date=18 May 2015}}</ref> Five days later the [[Secretary-General of the United Nations]], [[Ban Ki-moon]] announced that peace talks would be held in Geneva starting on 28 May and urged all parties to participate.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32814680|title=Yemen conflict: UN to sponsor peace talks in Geneva|work=BBC News}}</ref> Houthi rebels reiterated their support for the talks while exiled government officials said they would participate only if the Houthi's withdrew from occupied cities.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.timesofisrael.com/saudi-arabia-rejected-israeli-offer-of-iron-dome/|title=Saudi Arabia 'rejects Israeli offer to supply Iron Dome'|work=The Times of Israel}}</ref>

On 26 May, Ban announced that the peace talks were to be postponed indefinitely after exiled Yemeni officials refused to attend until rebels withdrew from all occupied cities.<ref name="un-org20150526BCF">{{cite news |title=Ban calls for postponement of Yemen consultations, urges 'soonest possible' return to dialogue |publisher=UN News Centre |date=26 May 2015 |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50971 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6YpesL1By?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=50971 |archivedate=27 May 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 6 June the UN announced that peace talks would take place on 14 June<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/06/us-yemen-security-un-idUSKBN0OM0QT20150606|title=U.N. to convene Yemen peace talks on June 14 |work=[[Reuters]] |first=Michelle |last=Nichols |date=6 June 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> Both the exiled officials and the Houthi group confirmed their attendance.<ref name="reuters.com3"/>

=== 15–19 June 2015 talks ===
Secretary-General Ban called for a "humanitarian pause" during the Muslim holy month of [[Ramadan]]. Peace talks between the exiled government and the Houthis concluded in Geneva without reaching a ceasefire.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.dawn.com/news/1189260/talks-on-yemen-war-end-without-agreement |title=Talks on Yemen war end without agreement | newspaper=[[Dawn (newspaper)|Dawn]] |location=Pakistan |date= 20 June 2015| access-date= 20 June 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Chanda|first=Abikh|url=https://www.dailystar.com.lb/News/Middle-East/2015/Jun-15/302154-ban-calls-for-two-week-ceasefire-in-yemen-talks.ashx |title= Ban calls for immediate humanitarian truce in Yemen |newspaper=[[The Daily Star (Lebanon)|The Daily Star]] |location=Lebanon |date= 15 June 2015| access-date= 20 June 2015}}</ref>

=== Ramadan peace agreement ===
On 4 July 2015, Houthi spokesman Mohammed Abdul Salam said in a post on his Facebook page that he had met Ahmed on Friday to discuss a Ramadan truce. The US and EU announced their support for a humanitarian truce.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/07/04/us-yemen-security-idUSKCN0PD12N20150704|title=Yemen's Houthis say Ramadan humanitarian pause under discussion |work=[[Reuters]] |date=4 July 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

On 9 July, the UN announced an unconditional truce between 10 July until the end of [[Eid ul Fitr]] on 17 July. The Special Envoy to Yemen assured the agreement of all warring factions.<ref name="un-org20150709UCW">{{cite web |title=Yemen: UN chief welcomes announcement of humanitarian ceasefire |publisher=UN News Centre |date=9 July 2015 |url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51371 |archiveurl=https://www.webcitation.org/6Zu4aaeOy?url=http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51371 |archivedate=9 July 2015 |url-status=live }}</ref> The truce was interrupted within an hour by airstrikes.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://uk.news.yahoo.com/us-drone-strike-kills-4-al-qaida-fighters-194906562.html |title=Airstrikes pierce new Yemen truce following ground fighting|date=11 July 2015 |publisher=[[Yahoo! News]] UK |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> Coalition spokesman later added that the coalition was not bound by the truce and that any truce would be counterproductive.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/07/12/saudi-led-coalition-says-its-not-bound-by-un-declared-truce/|title=Saudi-led coalition says its not bound by UN-declared truce|publisher=Fox News Channel|date=12 July 2015 |access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref> It later added that it was not requested to pause by the exiled Yemeni Government.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jul/11/yemen-fighting-breaks-un-truce-less-than-one-day|title=Yemen: fighting breaks UN ceasefire less than one day after it took effect|work=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=13 July 2015}}</ref>

=== Further peace talks ===
On 8 September 2015, [[Vice News]] revealed a leaked email by UN Envoy to Yemen Ismail Ould Cheikh Ahmed. In it, the envoy confirms that Houthi rebels and the party of former president and Houthi ally Ali Abdullah Saleh have expressed willingness to accept—with some reservations—a UN Security Council resolution, approved in April. This demanded the rebels "withdraw their forces from all areas they have seized, including the capital, Sanaa". "AA/GPC agreed to a new wording on UNSC resolution 2216 that states unequivocally that they are committed to the implementation of 2216 (see document attached) with the exception of article which infringe on Yemeni sovereignty and those related to sanctions," wrote Ould Cheikh Ahmed, referring to Ansar Allah (AA)—another name for the Houthis—and Saleh's General People's Congress party (GPC). "In addition, the new text includes acceptance of the return of the current government for a period of 60 days during which a government of national unity shall be formed," wrote the envoy in the email. According to Ould Cheikh Ahmed, during talks, the Houthis gave ground on certain language, including "mandatory support by the international community for reconstruction that was in the earlier version". "The latter was particularly opposed by KSA [[Kingdom of Saudi Arabia]] and GCC [[Gulf Cooperation Council]] who did not want it to be interpreted as a form of mandatory compensation," added the UN envoy.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.vice.com/article/leaked-un-email-on-yemen-shows-difficulty-of-negotiations-and-fears-over-al-qaedas-growing-presence|title=Leaked UN Email on Yemen Shows Difficulty of Negotiations – and Fears Over Al Qaeda's Growing Presence|publisher=[[Vice News]]|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref>

On 10 September, UN Envoy to Yemen announced that all parties had agreed to peace talks. A statement from Hadi's office following a meeting on the issue of new talks affirmed the president's "complete support for the sincere efforts exerted by the special envoy". It urged Ahmed to "exert efforts to achieve the public and honest commitment on the part of the Houthis and Saleh" to implement 14 April council resolution unconditionally.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2015/09/10/un-envoy-announces-new-yemen-peace-talks-next-week|title=UN envoy announces new Yemen peace talks next week|work=[[U.S. News & World Report]] |access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref> On 13 September, the exiled Yemeni government announced that it would no longer participate in the peace talks.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://edition.cnn.com/2015/09/13/middleeast/yemen-president-u-n-talks/|title=As U.N. Yemen talks near, President pulls out|last=Almasmari|first=Hakim |authorlink=Hakim Almasmari |date=13 September 2015|publisher=CNN|access-date=15 November 2015}}</ref>

=== 2016 talks ===
On 18 April, peace talks aimed at ending Yemen's civil war that were set to begin faltered before they could start, when delegates representing Yemen's Houthi rebels refused to attend.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/19/world/middleeast/yemen-peace-effort-falters-as-houthis-refuse-to-attend-talks.html|title=Yemen Peace Effort Falters as Houthis Refuse to Attend Talks|last1=Al-batati|first1=Saeed|date=18 April 2016|last2=Fahim|first2=Kareem|newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref>

On 20 April, talks convened, based on UN Security Council resolution 2216 which called for the Houthi fighters to withdraw from areas they seized since 2014 and hand heavy weapons back to the government.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2016/04/yemen-peace-talks-kuwait-160423045644770.html|title=UN Yemen envoy hails 'constructive' peace talks|publisher=[[Al Jazeera]] |access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref>

On 6 August, the UN special envoy to Yemen, Ismail Ould Cheikh Ahmed, announced the suspension in Kuwait, where the talks were being held. He said that the negotiations were not a failure and that they would resume in a month at an undisclosed location. Mr. Ahmed is the second United Nations envoy to try to broker peace talks between the Houthis and other factions in Yemen since March 2015. His predecessor quit after similar peace talk efforts failed. After the breakdown of the talks, one of the Houthi negotiators, Nasser Bagazgooz, blamed the United Nations envoy for seeking what he said amounted to a military solution on behalf of the Saudi-led coalition.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/08/07/world/middleeast/yemen-peace-talks-cease-fire.html|title=Talks to End War in Yemen Are Suspended|last=Nordland|first=Rod|date=6 August 2016|newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref> Previous negotiations floated the idea of forming a unity government—composed of Houthi and former Hadi government leaders. But the exiled Hadi leaders have consistently rejected any deal that would diminish their power over Yemen, and the Houthis have said that they will reject any deal that does not give them a seat at the table.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://theintercept.com/2016/08/11/lopsided-peace-talks-collapse-saudis-resume-yemen-bombing-and-u-s-sells-more-weapons/|title=Lopsided Peace Talks Collapse, Saudis Resume Bombing Yemen and U.S. Sells More Weapons|last=Emmons2016-08-11T18:45:04+00:00|first=Alex EmmonsAlex|website=[[The Intercept]] |access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2016/05/yemen-talks-kuwait-war-saudi-arabia-houthis-hadi-government.html|title=Yemen peace talks stuck in stalemate|date=20 May 2016 |publisher=[[Al-Monitor]] |access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.middleeasteye.net/news/yemens-houthis-challenge-un-peace-deal-demanding-unity-president-2076774143|title=Houthis demand 'unity' president as part of Yemen peace deal|access-date=13 August 2016}}</ref>

;November ceasefire

The Saudi-led military coalition and Houthis (Ansar Allah) arrived at a swift ceasefire agreement effective 17 November 2016, as a result of efforts of US Secretary of State John Kerry and Omani dignitaries.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.shiitenews.org/index.php/yemen |title=John Kerry says Yemen's Houthis and Saudi coalition agree to ceasefire |work=[[The Guardian]] | date= 15 November 2016| accessdate=17 November 2016}}</ref>

=== 2020 ceasefire in response to the COVID-19 pandemic ===
After the United Nations urged both sides to pursue peace talks in order to respond to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Yemen]],<ref>{{cite news|date=2 April 2020|title=As coronavirus spreads, U.N. seeks Yemen urgent peace talks resumption|language=en|work=Reuters|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-yemen-security/as-coronavirus-spreads-u-n-seeks-yemen-urgent-peace-talks-resumption-idUSKBN21K1P4|accessdate=8 April 2020}}</ref> the Saudi-led coalition called a unilateral ceasefire beginning 9 April at noon, to support efforts to mitigate the [[COVID-19 pandemic]].<ref>{{cite news|date=9 April 2020|title=Ceasefire begins in Yemen to help combat virus|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-52224358|accessdate=12 April 2020}}</ref> However, despite pledging ceasefire in [[Yemen]], [[Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen|Saudi-led coalition]] carried out dozens of airstrikes in the span of a week. The Yemen Data Project stated that at least 106 Saudi-led airstrikes, across 26 raids in Yemen had been carried out by the Kingdom in just one week.<ref>{{cite news|title=Saudi-led coalition bombs Yemen 'dozens' of times despite declaring ceasefire last week to combat coronavirus|website=Independent|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/coronavirus-yemen-coalition-bombs-saudi-ceasefire-news-a9470801.html|accessdate=18 April 2020}}</ref> On July 2, coalition fighter jets launched scores of airstrikes on several Yemeni provinces. The operation was a response to ballistic missile and drone launchings by the Houthis against Saudi Arabia.<ref>{{cite news|date=2 July 2020|title=Saudi-led coalition hits Houthi-held areas in renewed air raids|work=Al Jazeera|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/07/saudi-led-coalition-hits-houthi-held-areas-renewed-air-raids-200702072034014.html}}</ref> Both sides stepped up their attacks in September.<ref>{{cite news |title=Tercera noche de bombardeos contra posiciones de los hutíes en Saná |url=https://www.msn.com/es-mx/news/other/tercera-noche-de-bombardeos-contra-posiciones-de-los-hut%C3%ADes-en-san%C3%A1/ar-BB18ZwZ6?ocid=msedgntp |accessdate=Sep 13, 2020 |work=www.msn.com |agency=EFE |date=September 13, 2020 |language=es}}</ref>
